## Volume 20

## 770

B"H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef Dekel
Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your regards through Mr. Landau, and I hereby acknowledge receipt of the **Yizkor** book and the two volumes of **Gevilei Eish**. Thank you for your thoughtfulness. It is my hope that if you publish further works, you will send them to the library here, especially since the library serves the public good. However, may it be Hashem’s will that the content of future publications be connected to joyous events and the remembrance of joyous events, and that there be an abundance of goodness and joy, as the verse prophesies: "I will thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me; [but] Your anger has turned away and You have comforted me" (Yeshayahu 12:1). This means that the consolation will be to such a degree that the thanksgiving will be with one’s whole heart, even for the fact that "You were angry with me."

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize, on this occasion, that the purpose of any remembrance is to influence action, for "the deed is the essential thing." The ultimate intent of the aforementioned remembrance is to perpetuate the values of our people, whose eternity is bound up with our eternal Torah and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." These were given by Hashem, who is "You are the same, and Your years will not end," and who is, at the same time, the Creator of man, his Maker, and the Creator of the world in all its details. Therefore, He is the only One who can know the ways and means by which man, as an individual and as a collective, can ensure his existence and the life conditions appropriate for him. And since all Yisrael are responsible for one another, it is incumbent upon each and every person to utilize all their ability and potential to increase the establishment and existence of our people, the Children of Yisrael, by disseminating the eternal values of our eternal Torah in the widest possible circles, in a manner that is constantly increasing.

And all the more so, the merit, responsibility, and obligation in this are great for all those who have influence in wide circles, whether through speech, writing, or especially through printed materials. And we have been promised: "He who comes to purify himself is assisted."

May it be Hashem’s will that you do this with joy and a glad heart.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I send to you and to all who are yours my wishes for a good and sweet year.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah*.

## 7447

B"H, Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Avraham Krinizi, Mayor of Ramat Gan

Greetings and Blessings,

I was pleased to receive your regards via Mr. Yoel Frankel, who also brought your books, *B'Koach HaMaaseh* and *Mit Di Tzen Finger*. I trust that you will continue to send your future publications to the library here as well. Thank you in advance.

It is well known that a Jew seeks and finds a hint and a connection in every matter. The title you chose for your book, *B'Koach HaMaaseh* ("Through the Power of Action"), is surely influenced and borrowed from the words of our Sages that "action is the essential thing." These words also serve as a response to various schools of thought which suggest that the existence of the Jewish people can be sustained based on the slogan, "The Merciful One desires the heart," and especially based on the wise man’s statement that the heart is the king of the organs. This is not the case; rather, every matter must be expressed primarily through action, for only then is it proof and a sign that the matter touches one’s inner self. It is characteristic that the entire Book of Koheles, which on the face of it is a philosophical debate whose theme, at first glance, is the negation of the world of action and labor, nevertheless concludes with the final verdict: "Fear G-d and keep His mitzvos, for this is the whole of man."

If this is true for every individual, it is all the more so for one whom Divine Providence has placed as a mayor in Israel for decades. Surely, it is his privilege and his duty to utilize all his influence, in action and in practice, so that the city in Israel may be worthy of its name. This means that it is not merely located in a specific geographical area, but that its entire essence and reality is *Yisrael*—for the concept of *Yisrael* is as the Zohar states: "Israel, the Torah, and the Holy One, blessed be He, are all one."

Moving from one subject to a related one, I have the pleasant duty to express my gratitude upon receiving the news that the esteemed Rabbi, a man of stature and character, Rabbi Axelrod, has been appointed to succeed his late father in your city, and that you have decided and resolved this matter. I am certain that he will fulfill his role faithfully—the role of a Rabbi and teacher of Torah in Israel—in accordance with the Torah of Israel, given by the G-d of Israel.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I wish you and all yours to be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing,

***

**Rabbi Axelrod:** Rabbi Gedaliahu, son of the late Rabbi Moshe Axelrod. See above, Vol. 19, Letter 7165, and the references in the notes there.

## 7,448

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the first day of Selichos, in which you write about your desire to do teshuvah and how to bring it into action, noting that there are several matters that cause confusion.

You should contemplate very carefully what our Alter Rebbe—the author of the Tanya, who is the final arbiter in the hidden dimensions of Torah, and the Shulchan Aruch, who is the final arbiter in the revealed dimensions of Torah—writes in his holy Tanya, at the beginning of Chapter 41. It would be excellent to learn by heart from the beginning of the chapter until the second page, the word "the King" (HaMelech). It is well known what our Sages of blessed memory said: "If only your fear of Heaven were like your fear of flesh and blood" (Tanya, page 57a). Likewise, you should contemplate the themes of these days, which you should study in the Igeres HaTeshuvah of our Alter Rebbe and elsewhere. It is my hope that you will firmly resolve that you, as part of the collective of Klal Yisrael, must return to Hashem our G-d. Especially during these days, when the influence extends over the entire year, "one who comes to purify himself is assisted" even more. Enclosed is my general letter for Rosh Hashanah, which also discusses this matter, though not specifically this point.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you may need.

With blessings for a *chasimah tovah* and a *gmar chasimah tovah*.

#### ***7,448***

**General letter:** See above, Vol. 19 - 7,441.

## 7849

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs, etc., R' Yehuda, may he live.

*Peace and blessing!*

*Transcribed herein is the text of the telegram-telephone message that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to convey in connection with the seudas mitzvah for the benefit of the mikveh:*

In response to your invitation—I join with those who keep Your precepts, the activists in the construction of the mikveh in Neot Deshe, and I participate in the seudas mitzvah in connection with its completion.

This is in keeping with the theme of these days, and as the Mishnah rules (Chapter Yom HaKippurim): "Fortunate are you, Yisrael... and you shall be purified." "Fortunate are you" specifically—a teshuvah out of ahavah, as it is stated in the parsha of the week: "Fortunate are you, Yisrael... and your enemies shall cringe before you"—intentional sins become as merits.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon the conclusion of the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And you shall dwell in the land that I gave to your fathers," with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with the blessing of a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Enclosed is a check as a symbolic contribution to the above.

I am sure you will inform me of what is done regarding the above. Thank you in advance.

With respect and with the blessing of a *gmar chasimah tovah*,

Secretary

## 7550

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

Agudas HaShochtim, Tel Aviv-Yafo
May Hashem preserve them.

Peace and blessing!

It was a pleasure to receive your regards through the member, the esteemed Chossid, man of fine character and accomplishments, Rabbi M.M. Raskin, along with your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Atem Nitzavim.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as we find ourselves in these days regarding which our Sages of blessed memory taught us that the power of the individual is like the power of the community during the rest of the year (Rosh Hashanah 18a), how much more so is the power of the community and the association during these days of favor.

Behold, the Almighty does not despise (Berachos 8a; see Chiddushei Aggados there), and He will accept the prayers and requests, within the prayers of all the children of Israel, for a good sealing and final sealing, for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

And in this regard as well—in your holy work, in accordance with the teaching of Chazal, "The word *v'shachat* (and he shall slaughter) implies *v'mashach* (and he shall draw)," which implies two things (Chullin 30b, end; and Tosafos there)—also in your spiritual avodah: to draw the "animal" (within the person) until it is rendered fit to become blood and flesh of the person's own flesh (in the language of our Alter Rebbe in the Tanya). "You are called 'Adam' (man)," because you resemble the One Above, to serve Him, may He be blessed, with all your heart, with both your inclinations—the man and the animal, the nefesh elokis and the nefesh habahamis together.

With respect and with a blessing for a good sealing and final sealing.

#### ***7550***

**Agudas HaShochtim:** Another letter to them—below, 7643.

**In accordance with the teaching of Chazal:** See also above, Vol. 15, letter 5511, and the references in the notes there.

## 751

*[6 Tishrei, 5721]*

In accordance with the well-known instructions of our Sages regarding one who has caused a stumbling block to his fellow, and especially in accordance with what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 25, even those who have been insulted must take upon themselves to be extra careful and meticulous in the mitzvos of Hashem. It goes without saying that they must root out and eradicate any resentment from their hearts, chas v’chalilah, as is written in the parsha of this week: when the tribes of Israel are united, they bring about the gathering of the heads of the people, and they bring it about that "He became King in Yeshurun." As is explained in Likutei Torah, this is the greatness of the level when Bnei Yisrael are in the state of "Yeshurun."

#### ***751***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 598.

## 7552

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the congregants and the administration of the Chabad Shul and Beis Medrash in Meah Shearim, in Jerusalem, the Holy City—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It gave me pleasure to receive regards from the congregants of the Shul and Beis Medrash through the guests, shlita.

May it be the will of Hashem that all the days, Bnei Yisrael should always bring each other good tidings—only good, in true goodness, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "Good to Heaven, good to people, and good that bears fruit" (Kiddushin 40a).

And since in all matters of holiness, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room to add—for we are connected to Hashem, who is Ein Sof—my hope is strong that you will strengthen yourselves not only in matters of tefillah, but also in the study of Torah in public, both in nigleh and in Chassidus, every single day. And on Shabbos Kodesh, with an addition in the study of the teachings of Chassidus, as is explained in this regard in the writings of the Arizal.

For our Sages of blessed memory have ruled that a name is significant, and for a Beis Medrash and Shul to bear the name Chabad with integrity—for praise, for a name, and for glory (see Likutei Torah by Rabbeinu HaZaken, Parshas Tavo, end of the maamar beginning "Hayom Hazeh Hashem Elokecha Metzavecha... with all your heart and with all your soul").

May it be the will of Hashem that it should serve as a living example and influence all the aforementioned upon all shuls and batei medrash, until the prophecy is fulfilled: "The shuls and batei medrash in Bavel are destined to be established in Eretz Yisrael," with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with blessings for a Chag Sameach.

## 753

[13 Tishrei, 5721]

In response to your letter from Erev Yom Kippur,

At a time of favor, I will mention you once again at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. The instructions of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, and their words endure forever: "Think good and it will be good." May you be able to share good news regarding the contents of your letter, as mentioned above. Regarding the mitzvah in which one should be especially careful—to disseminate the Torah of Hashem wherever your hand can reach—for all of this, one requires a healthy and whole body, which is one of the ways of Hashem.

I look forward to hearing good news, and with blessings for a happy holiday.

P.S. Your second letter has been received—sharing good news regarding the above. And the ruling of our Sages is that anyone to whom good is done, it is a sign that they are worthy of good (Bava Basra 12b).

## 7,454

B"H, 19 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and learned, who engages in the needs of the community and sits in judgment, leading his congregation with integrity, R' Shlomo, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 27 Elul, in which you write regarding the public study of Torah, specifically *aggadah* and *mussar*.

It is well known what our Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya—who is the *posek* in the *nistar* (hidden) dimension of Torah, just as he is in the *nigleh* (revealed) dimension—writes in his *Iggeres HaKodesh* (Tanya, Part 4, Epistle 23): that the *aggadah* contained in the *Shas* contains the majority of the secrets of the Torah, and it atones for a person’s sins, as explained in the writings of the Arizal—these are wondrous and guarded matters.

May it be G-d’s will that you continue to add to the aforementioned, doing so with joy and a glad heart, in accordance with the instruction of the great teacher, our Rabbeinu the Rambam, in his *Yad HaChazakah* at the conclusion of *Hilchos Lulav*.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevgam, zya*, in accordance with the content of your letter, and the merit of your aforementioned activities will stand you in good stead to bring you good tidings in all these matters.

With blessings for good news.

Due to the holiness of the *moed*, the Rebbe *shlita* did not sign personally, and I am signing on his behalf.

As per your request, a copy of the *Sefer Tanya Kadisha* and other items are being sent to you separately.

***

**R' Shlomo:** Azyag, Dubdo. Another letter to him—see Vol. 15, 5,450.

## 7551

B"H, 26 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Bereishis, and by way of introduction, it is understood and simple that there is no place here for requests for forgiveness or the like, for the letter speaks of words of Torah, and especially of matters that pertain to practical application. You are also correct in the conclusion of your letter, that this is a matter that concerns many, since it is visible to many.

Regarding the content of the question or observation: the practice you describe—namely, not to touch the side-locks (peios) at all—is not one I have seen within Chabad; on the contrary.

Several reasons can be suggested for this, perhaps including the reason you hint at in your letter, so as not to mix the illuminations of two of the thirteen *tikkunim* of the *Dikna Kadisha*. In any event, it is **explicit** that the Arizal would cut and shorten them with scissors (*Shaar HaMitzvos* and *Taamei HaMitzvos*, Parshas Kedoshim).

Based on the above, the clear instruction of Chazal applies to this, in the tractate from which we derive our practice (Sukkah 32b):

"Rav Acha bar Rava **would turn** [his lulav] to the two [sides], and one [side], since it emerged from the mouth of Rav Kahana." See Rashi there.

And if you would say [that this applies to a statement], how much more so and with a *kal v'chomer* in our case, where we are dealing not only with the speech of the Rav, but with the *maaseh rav* (the actions of the Rav).

With respect and blessing.

Based on the above, it is explained that the question—**and a great one at that**—is actually directed at those who do not touch them at all, which is the **opposite** of the *maaseh rav* of the Arizal. See also *Darchei Teshuvah* to Yoreh Deah, subsection 181, that these are laws, etc. And in *Darchei Chaim V'Shalom*, subsection 465, [it states] not to tuck the peios behind the ear. (Indeed, what the compiler references there regarding *Zohar Chadash*, etc., requires study, for as it is understood simply, *Zohar Chadash* etc. speaks of hair that **grows** behind the ear.)

Your letter was received, as well as the disclosure following the above. Thank you.

## 770

B"H, 26 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., R' Shmuel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter and the enclosure.

It is well known in Chassidus how we interpret and analyze the statement of our Sages: "If a person intends to perform a mitzvah but is prevented and does not perform it, Scripture credits him as if he had performed it" (Berachos 6a). In such a case, there is actually an even greater merit.

For when one performs a mitzvah, a personal motive or the like can sometimes interfere. However, when "Scripture credits him as if he had performed it," the action is performed by Scripture in its entirety and perfection, and this is understood.

May the merit of tzedakah stand by you and your wife, may she live, for the fulfillment of your heart's desires in all the matters you write about.

With blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***770***

**R' Shmuel:** Lyubashitzky. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 18, p. 527, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 7557

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In accordance with the declaration customary in Lubavitch of old at the conclusion of Simchas Torah — the order now begins: **"And Yaakov went on his way."** And it is highly probable that this declaration also intended to include the conclusion of the matter: "And the angels of Elokim met him" (as per the Sages in Tanchuma, end of Parshas Mishpatim; Zohar Vol. III, 290a; see there).

And to illuminate that in the Midrash Tanchuma—

Whereas regarding the Zohar this is the revealed aspect of Torah, and especially given the connection of Midrash Tanchuma and Midrash Yelamdenu, which is as its name implies—the teaching of halachos—

The matter of "And the angels of Elokim met him" is interpreted as referring to angels, whereas in the Zohar, the inner dimension of Torah, it is interpreted as referring to the Holy One, blessed be He; and note this carefully.

With blessings for good tidings in general and in particular,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7558

B"H, 2nd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Noach, along with the enclosure.

It is understood that you and your wife, may she live and be well, should not move your residence from [location], as both your material livelihood and your spiritual livelihood are available to you there. Thank G-d, and with Hashem’s help, you and your children, may they live and be well, have succeeded in spreading Yiddishkeit and spreading the wellsprings in your surroundings and in your good camp, and you are currently in the midst of this work.

Therefore, you should continue in this with joy and a glad heart, especially through the Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad. This follows the principle explained regarding the Giving of the Torah: that it was only through the precedence of "Thus shall you say to the House of Jacob"—these are the women—and only afterward, "and tell the Children of Israel"—these are the men—that the Torah was established. May Hashem grant you success to share good news regarding all of the above.

We have just emerged from the month of Tishrei, the general month for the entire year. The point is to draw from its themes and activities throughout the entire year, and especially from the conclusion and seal of the themes of "joy of a mitzvah" during the time of our rejoicing in general, and the "joy of Torah" on Simchas Torah in particular.

With respect and anticipation of good news in all your affairs.

It is customary, as is well known, that one does not postpone the date of a wedding once it has already been set, especially when there is no reason to do so.

If holding the wedding here is connected with additional expenses, it is worth looking into arranging it in the place of your residence in [location], as there are several advantages to that.

#### ***7558***

**One does not postpone the date of a wedding:** See also Igros Kodesh of the Alter Rebbe, Letter 89, and the references in Bitaon Chabad, issues 38–39, p. 12, note 4. See below, 7596.

## 7559

7559

B”H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday,

It is a well-known instruction of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, that just as one is obligated to know one’s own shortcomings, so too is it necessary to know one’s own virtues. This is also a famous saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in particular—though it is common in the mouths of many of the great figures of Israel—that the prohibition against *lashon hara* applies to oneself as well. This applies to every single person, for every individual possesses a *nefesh elokis*, a literal part of Hashem from above, and even at the time of sin, it remained faithful to him (see in the *Tanya Kadisha*, according to the subject index at the end, Kehot edition, under the entry for *simcha*; from there it is understood that this does not contradict the *avodah* of *teshuvah*. It is also explained there that the *hisbonenus* which leads to the aforementioned true *simcha* is something that is relevant to everyone).

Furthermore, a primary point that we see tangibly is that one of the tactics of the *yetzer hara* is to instill in a Jewish person a feeling of despair, *chas v’shalom*. Afterwards, it comes with the argument that since there is no hope, *chas v’shalom*, he has no reason to abstain from the pleasures of this material world and its vanities, etc., etc.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, and also that every weekday morning, before *davening*, you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. After *davening* each day—including on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*—you should recite the daily portion of *Tehillim*, as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

Regarding what you wrote about people “snatching” *Torah* and *mitzvos*, etc.—see *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, chapter 4, paragraph 3.

P.S. As you requested, this letter is being sent quickly, without waiting for the regular turn.

#### ***7559***

**It is a well-known instruction of our Rebbes:** See also above, *Igros Kodesh* Vol. 18, letter 6131; 6359, and elsewhere.

**Saying:** See also above, *Igros Kodesh* Vol. 18, letter 6835, and elsewhere.

## 7660

B"H, 4th of Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday:

The prohibition of davening in a mixed-gender setting and the prohibition regarding a microphone (even if it is prepared before Shabbos) are brought in many places, and are also simple matters; it is surprising that there is even a question about this.

I have a strong hope—even though you do not mention it—that you have set times for studying the teachings of Chassidus in addition to your study of the revealed Torah. The necessity for this is explained in many places. May it be the will of Hashem that you continue and increase in this, in accordance with the directive to "increase in holiness," and may you do so with joy and a good heart.

With blessings for good tidings.

It is understood that I, too, have seen several articles that have been published seeking various **leniencies** regarding the microphone, etc.—and the reader can see that the author of the article lacks proper knowledge of the structure of the microphone and how it operates, or lacks knowledge of the halachic side, or lacks knowledge of both.

#### ***7660***

**The prohibition of a microphone:** See also above, Vol. 17, Letter 6495; Vol. 17, 5793, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7661

B"H, 5th of Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, R' Reuven, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your regards through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished R' M. Yaroslavsky, along with your book researching names and titles in the Talmud, as well as the offprint regarding the students of Rabbi Yehuda HaNasi.

May his strength be bolstered in Torah to continue adding more and more, as the hand of Hashem is good upon him, to clarify hidden matters, etc. He should examine the Tanya of our Rebbe HaZaken, in Kuntres Acharon, page 150b, and elsewhere.

I cannot restrain myself from expressing my bewilderment—requesting your forgiveness in this—which is that, as is apparent from several of your books from long ago, you are of the Chassidic community (how could it be otherwise?). Based on this, my hope was strong that you would dedicate your time and knowledge to the teachings of Chassidus, its greats, its subjects, and their matters—especially in the year we are concluding, the bicentennial year of the passing and hillula of our master, the Baal Shem Tov. I have searched and inquired, and as of now, I have not found anything of the aforementioned, even though you are apparently a prolific writer.

It is understood that my intention in what is said here—and in general, this is not a matter of delivering mussar, Heaven forbid—is only regarding the future. Since the time for matters of Torah is every hour and every moment, my hope is that in the near future you will increase your work in this area, and not only for your own benefit, but, as is your custom, to publish for the public in the aforementioned field. This is especially true according to what is brought in many places from the Arizal (cited in Iggeres HaKodesh of our Rebbe HaZaken, Epistle 26) that in our time, it is an obligation and a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom. For one such as you, elaboration on all this is surely superfluous.

With respect and blessings.

#### ***7661***

**R' Reuven:** Margalit, Tel Aviv. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 9, 2949, and in the references noted there.

## 7662

B"H, 6 MarCheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn.

...Regarding what you wrote, that all your life you have davened with Sephardic pronunciation, and [you are asking] whether you should change to Ashkenazic pronunciation, having heard that there are advantages to davening with that pronunciation.

I have not heard this rumor, and I see no reason why you should change from the pronunciation you have been accustomed to, as you wrote, all your life. And although the Chabad *nusach* is the most choice—it is not relevant to the matter of pronunciation.

#### ***7662***

**To change to Ashkenazic pronunciation:** See also above, Vol. 18, Letter 6969; Vol. 19, Letter 6746; below, Letter 7777.

## 7,563

B"H, 9 MarCheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Tishrei,

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote, "From where will my help come?"—the answer is already stated in the verse and in the explanation of our Sages, of blessed memory, regarding this: "My help is from Hashem, Maker of heaven and earth." And the end of the matter will be, "And the man spread out exceedingly," in the manner of our Sages' teaching regarding the concept of "Ufaratzta" (and you shall spread out).

It is surprising that you do not mention anything about your activities during Zman Simchaseinu (the time of our rejoicing), for these days are foundational for the entire year and are central to the matters of the month of Tishrei, as is explained in many places, and you will understand. I am certain you will complete this in your next opportunity.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 7658

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, I am replying to its contents without waiting for my turn.

You write regarding the relationship between a husband and his wife, etc. In accordance with the ruling of Chazal regarding bringing peace between a husband and his wife—the fruits of which a person enjoys in this world, etc.—it is understood that every effort and endeavor in this matter is worthwhile, and this is self-evident.

It is also understood that in such matters, one cannot set rigid rules, as it depends on the character of the husband and the wife, as well as the nature of the environment in which they live. However, it is certainly possible for every person to be approached and influenced through contemplation and by seeking the appropriate path for that specific individual, time and again, in ways of pleasantness, yet with firmness and words that come from the heart. This is not at all difficult to speak of with warmth, since the matter concerns the individuals involved and the future generations of their children.

The common denominator that is effective in any such situation is along the lines of what is brought in Avos D'Rabbi Nosson, Chapter 12, regarding the conduct of Aharon, who loved peace.

May it be the will of Hashem that he succeeds in establishing a home in Yisrael, and that it be founded upon Torah and mitzvos, extending into day-to-day life.

You do not mention anything regarding the month of Tishrei, the month that is satiated with all good. My hope is that it was utilized in the appropriate manner, as this serves as a principle for the entire year—that is, to draw the hisorerus and hispaalus of the days of the Yomim Tovim into the entire year. If this is the requirement for every person, how much more so for a man whom Divine Providence has privileged and enabled to lead a holy congregation in Yisrael on the path ascending to the House of Hashem.

With blessings for good tidings in both personal and general matters.

If it is possible given the business affairs of the aforementioned couple, there is room to suggest that their traveling together for a few weeks to a vacation spot or the like, as a "second honeymoon," would rectify the entire situation.

## 7771

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Moshe HaKohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, I received your regards through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a man of many accomplishments, R' Tzvi Shusterman.

Regarding your question conveyed through him concerning the *gabbai* position in the *beis medrash*, where you wrote that I had previously expressed my opinion that you should continue in this role:

It is well known that the essence and inner dimension of this matter concerns the order of *davening* and the *shiurim* in Torah that are studied. Since this concerns a Chassidishe *beis medrash*, the *shiurim* should also include the teachings of Chassidus. Furthermore, since you will continue to oversee that the *shaliach tzibbur* leads the *davening* in an appropriate manner—and all the more so on *Shabbos* and *Yomim Tovim*—as well as ensuring that after *davening* the monthly *Tehillim* *shiur* is recited (as per the *takanah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory), and that *shiurim* in *nigleh* and Chassidus are held at appropriate times—this is the true continuation of the aforementioned role. It is revealed before Heaven that the name and title are of no consequence at all, and certainly, for one such as yourself, further elaboration on this is superfluous.

Based on what is explained in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, that everything occurs through *hashgacha pratis*, your question arrived and this response is being written on the eve of the 20th of Cheshvan. The 20th of Cheshvan is the birthday of the Rebbe Rashab, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and this year marks one hundred years since that event. The significance of this is understood based on what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the beginning of this *parsha*, "And the life of Sarah was one hundred years, etc." See the *Zohar* there, and the explanation in *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek.

See also *Shelah*, beginning of *Parshas Toldos*.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

## 772

772

B.H., 20 Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

Today, as this letter is being written, marks one hundred years since the birth of the Rebbe, the founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, 64 years ago.

Sixty years ago, at the beginning of the fourth year of the Yeshiva in Lubavitch, the Rebbe said at the Simchas Torah farbrengen:

"I am *muvtach*—there is *batuch* and there is *muvtach*; I assume everyone knows the difference between *batuch* and *muvtach*—I am *muvtach* that the talmidim of Tomchei Temimim, wherever they may be—and they will be in the four corners of the world—will carry out with *mesiras nefesh* the *kavanah elyonah* of *nisaveh HaKadosh Baruch Hu lihyos lo dirah betachtonim* (the desire of the Holy One, Blessed be He, to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds)."

To create a "dwelling place" for the Ribono shel Olam in this world means to spread the Divine light of Torah and mitzvos and to bring *kedushah* into daily life, both for oneself and in one's entire surroundings.

There cannot be any doubt for anyone that these holy words of the founder of the Lubavitcher yeshivos have been completely fulfilled. The *talmidim temimim* have carried out and continue to carry out their *shlichus* with the greatest *mesiras nefesh*, regardless of the difficult experiences, decrees, and *nisyonos* that Yidden in general, and the *talmidim temimim* in particular, have endured throughout all these shocking and tumultuous years. In all parts of the world, they have brought about a great revival, *Yiddishkeit*, and *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, and everywhere they have created a "dwelling place" for the Ribono shel Olam.

And precisely today, when the uncertain and precarious situation in the world casts a great fear of the dangerous means of destruction that the discord and fragmentation of the nations could, *chalilah*, provoke—precisely today, more than ever, it is a matter of life and death to create a "dwelling place" for the Ribono shel Olam, the *Melech shehaShalom shelo*, the true Ruler of the world, the *Baal HaBayis* of peace, through the spreading of Torah and mitzvos, which bring peace, through *talmidim temimim*, for *talmidei chachamim marbim shalom ba'olam*.

All those who take part in the support and expansion of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei-Temimim Lubavitch, throughout the entire year, and especially on the occasion of this annual endeavor, possess an eternal *zechus* and create the *tzinoros* and *keilim* for the Ribono shel Olam’s blessings—especially the blessing of true peace, which is the *keli* for all blessings, in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*, for themselves and their families, may they live.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

***772***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 490.

**Said:** See Likkutei Dibburim, Vol. 4, p. 1568.

## 773

773

B"H, 20 Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Centennial of the birth of the Rebbe (Rashab)
To all those gathered at the annual
celebration of the
"Beis Rivkah" in Montreal
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

In response to the news regarding the upcoming dinner celebration on Tuesday, 3 Kislev, I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants and friends of the "Beis Rivkah" in Montreal. May Hashem grant that this endeavor be met with great success in all respects, to strengthen and expand the activities of the Beis Rivkah school to the desired extent.

Today, as this letter is being written, marks one hundred years since the birth of the Rebbe Rashab, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. The Rebbe Rashab laid the foundation for the far-reaching educational institutions that were further expanded under the leadership of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and which have brought about a great revival of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh* in various parts of the world, up to this very day.

It is unnecessary to emphasize that the Beis Rivkah schools in various parts of the world, including the Beis Rivkah school in Montreal, are among the main pillars of this *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*. The Rebbe, my father-in-law, the founder of the Beis Rivkah schools, always emphasized the supreme and vital necessity of *chinuch habanos*—to educate Jewish daughters, the future builders of the Jewish home. His words are well known:

"Everything that is holy to the G-dly people of Avraham—the foundation of the Jewish home, the raising and education of Jewish children, the kashrus of food, the loftiness, purity, and holiness of Shabbos—Hashem has handed over and entrusted to Jewish women to guard and carry out." (Hayom Yom, 26 Adar Rishon, 5743).

To educate Jewish daughters in this spirit is the task of Beis Rivkah, and it goes without saying that those who participate in the support and expansion of the Beis Rivkah in Montreal become partners in this mission.

And this will surely bring down the Divine blessing into their homes, with *nachas* from children, health, *parnassah*, and all good things.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7744

7744

B.H., 20 Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the venerable Rabbi and Chassid, a man of stature and accomplishment, engaged in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan, shlita

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 13 Cheshvan, in which you ask regarding my position on the question of the Chief Rabbinate in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), regarding which my opinion was published in the press in my name.

I must preface this by stating that the publication in the press was done without my knowledge—which is to say, also against my wishes. For this is not a matter that requires public debate by the entire nation, from the youngest to the oldest, children and women; and certainly not to create a platform for public debate in the newspapers of idle bystanders. It is a disgrace, regardless, to the honor of the Rabbinate and the honor of the Torah.

When I do express my opinion on matters such as this, it is only in a place where it has a practical consequence. This is also one of the reasons why, until now, I refrained from expressing an opinion on the aforementioned matter, since the date of the elections was still far off, and I surmised that many changes would occur until the days closest to the election date.

When a certain individual visited me—and this was just a few days before the official election date—and during our conversation asked me for my opinion on the question of the Chief Rabbinate, and since this individual has access to the circles that determine this issue, I found it my duty to express my opinion openly, as it was a matter of practical concern.

In setting these words down in writing now, I must preface another point: that which follows is based on the current situation. I mean to say that my fundamental attitude toward the entire institution of the Chief Rabbinate is based on the stance of all the Gedolei Yisrael who preceded us—that such a matter is negative. As is known to all the public activists in Russia, the Rabbis of Israel and the true leaders opposed the establishment of such an institution in Russia and its surroundings. They opposed it with all their might, to the point of battling the Czarist government—naturally, in the ways possible at the time—until they abolished the entire plan. The reasons are well-known, and if there was ever any doubt regarding their concerns as to whether the danger was distant or near, the reality of the years of the Chief Rabbinate in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) has proven that their concerns were entirely justified, and even more so.

However, unfortunately, given the current situation, while abolishing the entire institution of the Chief Rabbinate would be a good thing, it is not currently feasible. The secularists will not listen to this, nor even those to their right, even though everyone has witnessed over the past years the damage brought to religion and its affairs by the aforementioned institution—and a word to the wise is sufficient. This is despite the fact that those who served in this position had desirable intentions, and perhaps even their actions would have been different had they been able to act as they wished. Their possibilities and capabilities were constantly diminishing, and between ourselves, they did not always stand up to the test. But our Sages said, "Do not judge your fellow," etc.

Since, as stated above, it is not possible to abolish the entire institution, it is at least necessary to minimize the damage caused to our religion and to the honor of the Torah and those who bear it. Every single day that the time until the elections is extended is exploited by various factors in a way that further degrades the status of the religious and the honor of the Torah and its bearers. The reactions from ordinary Jews in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) in letters and conversations, etc., regarding everything transpiring around the elections for the Chief Rabbinate, are beyond belief.

B. It is understood that it is not enough to set an election **date** as soon as possible unless there is a candidate ready and there is a chance he will be elected. Based on all the above, I told that individual that my opinion is clear on three points, which are interdependent:

(a) It is imperative that the elections take place at the earliest possible date. Anyone who works to delay them takes upon himself the responsibility for further disgrace to religion and its affairs in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and from there also abroad, as experience has shown in recent months.

(b) According to the current situation, the candidate who has a chance of being elected is Rabbi S. Goren, shlita.

As for those who are conducting debates regarding others, it is clear even to them that some of those being spoken about will not accept the position, some are not suitable for the position, and some have no chance of being elected. The entire debate is only for peripheral reasons, which obviously have no place at the expense of disgracing religion, as mentioned above.

(c) It is imperative that Rabbi Nissim, shlita, remain in his current position, for there has never been such a thing in Israel where secularists, and even ordinary laymen (a significant part of the electing body is comprised of them), would remove a Rabbi from his position. It is understood that I am aware that, officially, the position was given to the aforementioned for a fixed term. But this does not at all negate the matter of the honor of the Torah and the honor of a Rabbi in Israel, the principle of *chazakah*, etc. And surely, for one such as you, elaboration on this is superfluous.

I emphasized above that the aforementioned points are, in my opinion, interdependent, because they are all founded on one basis: safeguarding religion in the current situation in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). Contradicting any one of them will cause further disgrace in the most distressing way.

As I stated at the beginning of my letter, the above words are directed to those who have the power to influence the course of the aforementioned matters. And here, too, my reasons and arguments are as stated above, because public debate (as opposed to expressing an opinion at the appropriate time and in the appropriate place) on such matters in the pages of a newspaper and the like degrades the status and condition of the Rabbinate wherever it may be, and especially in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). And this is well understood.

- Here I have the pleasant duty to express my satisfaction with your article regarding the Baal Shem Tov, z"l, and surely your hand is still outstretched [to do more].

With respect and blessing.

## 7776

B"H, 20 Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Rav, the Gaon, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing, the man of action, who engages in public needs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi R. Sh. Y. Shlit"a

May it be the will that you be a good messenger and bring good tidings regarding every single item in the memorandum. Seemingly, your influence and ability are greatest regarding items (a) and (f).

On this occasion, I would like to raise the matter of "a decree whose reason has been nullified—the decree itself is also nullified." Naturally, I turned immediately to the Talmudic Encyclopedia, but to my surprise, I found nothing on this subject, at least not under the entry for "Gezeirah" (decree).

It is unnecessary to add that my comments regarding the Talmudic Encyclopedia in my letters to your honor are certainly not intended to be critical, Heaven forbid, but rather with the hope that you will add them to the comments you surely receive from many different places, and that from time to time you will publish a booklet or a supplement of corrections for the volumes that have already appeared.

For it is obvious that one should not wait for the above to be addressed in a second edition of all the volumes.

Enclosed is a letter asking me about the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, with my notes in the margins.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

7727

B"H, 20 Cheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, involved in communal needs, full of energy, etc.,
Rabbi Yaakov Yehuda, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

On the joyous occasion of the thirteen-year celebration of your rabbinical position at the holy congregation of the Beis HaKnesses and Beis HaMedrash "R' Meir Simcha HaKohen" — this coming Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh,

I send you, the esteemed president, the gabbaim, and all the members, may they live, my greetings and blessing.

The events of the week, as is known, have a connection to the weekly parsha. Since the celebration takes place at the beginning of the week of Parshas Toldos, one can find a horah (instruction) immediately in the first verse of the parsha: **"Yitzchak, son of Avraham; Avraham begot Yitzchak."**

The repetition, "Yitzchak, son of Avraham; Avraham begot Yitzchak," in the holy Torah—and Torah is from the word *horah*, an instruction and lesson for daily life—emphasizes the perfect bond between Jewish generations, parents and children.

Very often we hear that children identify with their fine fathers and grandfathers; however, that is merely the aspect of "Yitzchak, son of Avraham." There must also be "Avraham begot Yitzchak," so that the father and grandfather can have true Jewish pride and nachas from their children and grandchildren. Not only should the children have the "merit of the fathers," but the parents should also have the "merit of the children."

This is, in essence, the inner purpose of a Beis HaKnesses and Beis HaMedrash: it should serve not only as a holy place to daven and learn, but that this holiness should be carried over and connect the shul with the homes of the members, from the very young to the very old. And this is also the task of the Rav and spiritual leader of a kehillah: that the entire kehillah—from young to old, children and women, both in shul and at home—should be permeated and unified by the light of Torah and mitzvos, and should grow as a **complete** kehillah, in the full sense of "Yitzchak, son of Avraham; Avraham begot Yitzchak." And this is realized through the full cooperation of the Rav, the leaders, and the members of the kehillah.

May Hashem Yisbarach bless you all, that the success of the previous years should grow and ascend for long, good days and years, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing.

## 7778

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

100 years since the birthday of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Michael Yehuda Aryeh Leib, may he live, HaKohen

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, bringing the news of your return to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and of your delivering the regards, etc.

Surely, after this beginning, each of the guests, may they live, will continue in a manner of "increasing and adding light," and as our Sages of blessed memory said, "A guest brings a blessing." We must walk in the straight path that he taught us—"and we shall walk in His ways"—that is, the path taught to us by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Yosef Orech* [Joseph the Guest], whose level includes the life of the Chai [18].

We have been privileged that our Sages of blessed memory have provided us with guidance in all matters of life and its events, and these have been explained thoroughly by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, in the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, in a manner of understanding and explanation.

In this regard, the work of our great Rebbe in the expansion of Chassidus was done in a wondrous way, with great wisdom of organization; he would send shluchim in secret to awaken others to approach and draw near to the ways of Chassidus, and he would send his students even to distant lands.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that the deeds of the Tzaddikim and their instructions exist forever and continue to exert their influence. Our Nasi awakens great mercy, so that the deeds of his children—the works of his hands—will bring forth good fruits in the true sense: good for Heaven, good for the creations, and good for the one who produces the fruits.

This is also the channel and vessel for the blessings of Hashem in personal matters, in both material and spiritual respects alike.

Awaiting good news regarding all the above, and signing with a blessing.

**M. Schneerson**

 *Good... fruits: Kiddushin 40a.*

## 7779

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To Mr. Chaim, may he be well, known as Dr. Shaskes,
Peace and blessing!

Rabbi R.M.A. Hodakov, may he be well, conveyed to me the news regarding your upcoming trip together with your wife, may she live. I wish you a successful journey. In the Jewish sense, success means that wherever a Jew goes, he fulfills the mission of the Creator of the world and its Guide—a mission of exerting influence on a way of life according to the Torah of life and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them," life in the literal sense, even in this world.

Surely you have heard that it was the Lubavitch custom on Motzaei Simchas Torah—at the conclusion of the Yomim Tovim of the seventh month and in preparation for the mundane days—to proclaim, "And Yaakov went on his way," which means on his way, the path appropriate for him from Hashem, who oversees each and every person with Hashgacha Pratis. For then, one merits the conclusion of the verse, "and the angels of Elokim met him," to guard him on the way and bring him to his desired destination.

May it be the will of Hashem that you convey words of inspiration to our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be. Especially after your visit to the countries behind the Iron Curtain, you can teach them a *kal v'chomer*: If, under those conditions, Jews struggle to remain faithful to Hashem and His Torah with literal mesiras nefesh, then all the more so is it the duty and privilege of every Jew who merits living in countries that enjoy freedom of religion to utilize these possibilities to their fullest in the aforementioned direction, and to have a "good eye" regarding others as well, to the extent that one's hand can reach, and in a manner of "increasing and continuing."

With blessings for success, with respect, and for good tidings.

**Surely you have heard:** See above, letter 7757.

## 7784

[From the month of Tishrei, 5721]

Even if this is the case regarding one’s **personal** conduct, it is a matter of significant inquiry (*tzarich iyun gadol*) whether this applies to what one does to fulfill the obligation for others (at the very least—**also** for others), in the performance of a mitzvah from the Torah, and in public. **And all the more so** regarding *tekios* (and not in the *beracha*), **where each person is fulfilling** the mitzvah, and the listener is hearing the *shevarim* in a certain manner, etc. And this requires further study (*kal v'chomer*).

Ultimately—how did they conduct themselves in Chabad *batei knessios* **everywhere** regarding the *shevarim*?

***

#### 7784

Written on the margin of a copy of a letter from Rabbi Y. Landau dated Sunday, *Parshas Lech Lecha*, 5721 (additional letters to him—above, Vol. 19, 7697, and in the notes indicated there; below, 7844)—a response to a question from the Rebbe (via his son, R' Eliyahu, who was then in the Rebbe’s court) as to whether he remembered how they would blow the *shevarim* in Lubavitch.

In his aforementioned letter, he writes: "I heard *tekios* in the Rebbe’s court only from the Rebbe himself, and there were several things that were difficult even for a simple person to understand. I once spoke with the *gaon* and Chassid, R' Yaakov R.S.L. of Riga, and he replied to me: 'What do I care? *Er blazt doch* (he is blowing, after all),' and furthermore, it is not our custom. I thought that the matter of the *shevarim* was also something that belonged only to the Rebbe, and that I should do as is written in the *Shulchan Aruch*."

Regarding this, the Rebbe writes here that from the *tekios* that the Rebbe would blow to fulfill the obligation for others, one can also derive a lesson for the many. And he asks again how they were accustomed to blow the *shevarim* in Chabad *batei knessios* everywhere. To this, Rabbi Y. Landau replied:

"My father, the Rav, of blessed memory, would blow four *shevarim*, but in our *beis knesses* there were several things that my father’s father-in-law, the Chassid R' Zishke, of blessed memory, instituted, which were not practiced in other places. And to imitate what our holy Rebbe, of blessed memory, did—that certainly never crossed my mind... even regarding things that can be done according to the *Shulchan Aruch*, but are not explicitly mentioned as required, yet the Rebbe did conduct himself that way—such as, for example, the *shevarim*, where the Rebbe would blow more than three."

## 7775

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 21st of MarCheshvan.

Since we are now at the beginning (and the entirety) of the month of Kislev, the month of redemption and miracles, this is a propitious time to invoke the blessing of Hashem that all matters—matters of Torah and mitzvos, both personal and communal—be redeemed from anything that hinders or distracts.

It should also be noted that Rosh Chodesh Kislev is the final time for the descent of rain, even in a late year. For the concept of rain is an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) that is brought about by an *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below), as it is written: "And a mist would go up from the earth and water..." and as our Sages of blessed memory taught: "A mist went up from the earth, and immediately it watered."

May it be the will of Hashem that all the things for which you have prayed, beginning from the start of the year and culminating in the prayer for rain—which includes everything—will, at the very latest, all come to fruition. May they descend below and be fulfilled in their entirety, beginning from this Rosh Chodesh, and may they come for blessing, for life, and for plenty.

With blessings for good tidings, both specifically and generally.

#### ***7775***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 15, p. 506, and completed based on a copy.

**Final time:** See *Taanis* 6a; *Nedarim* Chapter 8, Mishnah 5, and *Tosafos Yom Tov* there; and see also *Bava Metzia* 106b.

**As our Sages of blessed memory taught:** *Bereishis Rabbah* on the verse; *Yerushalmi Taanis*, beginning of Chapter 2. See also *Likutei Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, beginning of *Parshas Haazinu*.

**Which includes everything:** See *Bereishis Rabbah* 13:16: "And it watered all"—everything is blessed.

## 780

B”H, 1 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter. As you requested, I will mention you once again at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your request.

Despite the tone and content of your letter—and even more so, despite the fact that the situation is repeated in almost every letter from you—I have not, Heaven forbid, lost hope. I am confident that, in the end, you will not only see the good in life, including your own life, but that this vision will also be accompanied by a feeling in your heart. This is especially true according to the teachings of Chassidus, which explain that in this world of ours, everything is a mixture of good and evil. It is up to the person to choose what to emphasize, what to contemplate, and what to take an interest in. For in the life of every individual, there are two paths: to see the good that surrounds them, or, Heaven forbid, the opposite. If this is true for everyone, it is all the more so for the sons and daughters of Yisrael, who possess absolute faith in the eternity of the soul—that is, the eternity of spirituality—which means the victory of the good, an absolute victory. For it is impossible that something fleeting and transient would not be absolutely conquered by that which is enduring and eternal, as there is no comparison between them.

We are taught by the story of our Sages that Adam HaRishon, even before his expulsion, while he was still in Gan Eden, complained about his circumstances, and he was called an ingrate. Yet, among the sons and daughters of Yisrael who were in the concentration camps of the Germans—may their names be blotted out—during the most horrific period, may we be spared, there were those who recited the morning blessings, offering thanks and praise to the Creator of the world and its Guide. Ultimately, every person stands **between** these two extremes.

It is understood and simple that the above is not, Heaven forbid, a matter of justifying judgment upon anyone, especially [in your situation], but rather an emphasis on reality as it is. The point is that the manner and quality of a person’s life—whether it is a life filled with satisfaction and substance, or the opposite—depends to a significant and great extent upon the will of the person, who has the power to direct the vision of their intellect to look toward the right or toward the left.

Since we are now in the month of Kislev, a month of success for the members of the family, may it be His will that the aforementioned change begins immediately.

With regards and blessings.

## 7787

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding the order of davening and the improvements that are still necessary.

It is clearly observable in such matters that when students themselves are appointed to oversee the order—assisting, distributing the Siddurim, etc. [similar to the standard practice in a shul, with a Gabbai, a guide, a shamash, etc., naturally with the appropriate adjustments]—it succeeds not only in ensuring proper behavior during davening, but also afterward and in the preparation for davening. Of course, for several reasons, the appointees should be rotated from time to time. The duration of the appointment depends on the nature and character of the students; in case of doubt, it is best to begin with a short period, which then leaves the option to reappoint the suitable person or replace them with someone more suitable.

Regarding what you wrote about a student who is short in stature, etc.: several methods of treatment have been developed in recent years for such cases, although it is understood that not everyone is the same in terms of treatment and its success.

At an auspicious time, I will mention her at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever she may need.

In any case, it is worthwhile for the parents to ask the attending physician from time to time whether anything new has developed in this field recently regarding their daughter.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 7788

B”H, 2 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Gaon, who engages in the needs of the community, etc.,
Rabbi M. S. Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

Following up on your letter regarding the proposal to edit and restyle a commentary on the Tanach—a traditional commentary that would simultaneously be understandable to the new generation—and the suggestion that I participate in this project, and furthermore, that I share responsibility for the project, etc., and following the conversations I had here on this matter with Mr. ... [may he live], I have come to clarify my position on the aforementioned, and the substance of my oral response during those conversations.

I will begin regarding my participation in the aforementioned project. By way of introduction: a project of such great responsibility is such that if a part of it is disqualified, the whole is disqualified. Even if a commentary that is inappropriate were to be included in only a few places and printed as such, it would cast a blemish upon the entire project. From this, it is understood that one can only be responsible if he has the time and leisure to dedicate as much as is necessary to go over the entire commentary from beginning to end, and to review it with the appropriate diligence, in order to rule out any deviation from the path of tradition, which is the straight path.

It is also understood that in a project such as this, there is no room for appointing a shaliach or a representative, for such a responsible matter cannot be done by trusting others and relying upon them. This is especially true in light of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, that a word spoken is for the many, a word in writing is for the entire generation, and a word in print is for generations to come.

Therefore, I am compelled to decline the aforementioned proposal, and not only to decline it regarding the responsibility, but also to not allow my name to be associated with the project, since the use of one’s name is synonymous with participating in the responsibility, as is understood.

2) Regarding the project itself, my opinion is that it is a correct endeavor, but **only** if it is carried out by trustworthy individuals, and subsequently reviewed by several authorities who possess absolute reliability in matters such as these. I will explain my words:

Although the words of the Tanach were essentially explained by the early commentators and those who followed them—beginning with *Parshandasa*, which is the commentary of Rashi, and continuing through to the *Metzudos David* and *Metzudos Tzion*—who possess a unique authority because they engaged in the commentary of the Tanach as befits its nature, meaning, as a holy task, interpreting the Torah of Hashem, the Book of Books, without any ulterior motives or personal agendas, even spiritual ones, and certainly without the desire to assert one’s own opinion or to show that nothing is hidden or concealed—as Rashi expresses in many places, "I do not know," and the like. Furthermore, their authority is emphasized by the fact that they possessed a tradition passed down from generation to generation regarding the true interpretation of the Scriptures, and it is highly probable that there are many interpretations that were transmitted from generation to generation since the writing of the books of the Tanach. The words of the Rambam are well-known regarding the Holy Tongue, how, due to the distance of the generations, many matters and details were forgotten, which makes understanding the language difficult; thus, there was a tradition regarding this.

Nevertheless, since there are changes in style, and many matters that were previously simple interpretations are now not simple, and so on, it is good that the aforementioned commentary be edited. After all, we have the precedent that the great leaders of Israel in previous generations permitted the translation of the aforementioned commentaries into Yiddish (*Ivri-Teitch*), and endeavored to distribute them among those who, for whatever reason, could not learn from the commentary of Rashi and those who followed him. However, it is simple that the primary condition for the entire project is that it be, in the language of Chazal, "old wine" in a new vessel; that is to say, only the style and the language should be new. And the "old wine"—this refers to those commentaries upon which the great leaders of Israel in previous generations relied, as mentioned above, from the commentary of Rashi to the *Metzudos David* and *Metzudos Tzion*.

3) In the same way that we find in the ancient commentaries—that they added precision to their interpretation by bringing expressions from other languages, as in Rashi’s language, *b'la'az*—so too, in the aforementioned commentary, this method should be incorporated.

4) It is also understood that one should add comparisons to other languages, in the manner of the statement of Chazal, "Anochi is an Egyptian word" (*Tanchuma* on the verse). Likewise, one should cite archaeological discoveries in appropriate places, and also add illustrations. In this, too, we find a precedent in the accepted commentaries, such as in the Rambam’s commentary on the Mishnah, the *Aruch*, etc. (even though later printings omitted some of the illustrations, apparently for technical reasons).

5) Since the project will be carried out by human beings, and every person has unique traits, and since, as mentioned, a primary and **absolute** condition in editing the commentary is that it must be "old wine" as stated above, it is necessary that the commentary be edited by people who are not "innovators," but rather possess the sense and talent for collecting and arranging matters. Especially since we see tangibly that in most individuals, these aforementioned traits contradict one another; one who has a talent for innovation usually lacks the ability to collect and transmit the words of others as they are, because it is **impossible** not to mix in innovations of his own, and eventually, the innovation takes over the old.

6) It is also understood that the entire project’s purpose is to transmit the accepted interpretation of the Tanach in the clearest and simplest style. The first result of this is that there is no place in the aforementioned commentary to cite opinions that contradict [the tradition], even for the purpose of decisively refuting them; rather, one should simply present the interpretation as it is. Anyone who specifically wishes to fulfill the Mishnaic instruction, "Know what to answer," can look for a platform elsewhere.

7) Furthermore, a primary question: is there a place in the aforementioned commentary for the *drashos* of Chazal, at least in some places, as is customary in Rashi’s commentary? For the purpose of studying the Tanach is not only to understand the text as it appears, but "also" to know the Giver of the Torah. This requires further study. Perhaps the most appropriate solution is that the aforementioned *drashos* should appear on the side of the commentary, in the margins or below it, not within the text itself.

8) There is more to elaborate on regarding the aforementioned, but I have come only to outline the main points and the issues which, in my opinion, are essential. If it is impossible to fulfill them (all of the aforementioned conditions **in their entirety**), the entire project is liable to cause great harm instead of the hoped-for benefit, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

I would be happy to receive your comments, and in the appropriate detail, regarding all of the above, and I thank you in advance.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**
