## 790

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos.

Many thanks for the good news regarding the improvement in your health.

Regarding what you wrote about rectifying your character traits (*midos*), you should discuss this with your *mashpia* of *Chassidus*. This is how a student of Tomchei Temimim—founded and directed by our Rebbes—should conduct himself.

Regarding your question about rectifying the well-known matter: you should divert your attention from it entirely. This diversion of attention is not a matter of battling the negative thought, but rather of shifting your mind to a different subject. It is best to anchor and occupy it with the letters of Torah and *tefillah*, for if a little light pushes away much darkness, how much more so does a great deal of light.

Regarding your question about the time for reading *Shnayim Mikra V'echad Targum*, it is surprising to ask about a matter that is explained in *Shulchan Aruch*, with additional instruction provided in *Hayom Yom*.

Regarding your question as to why the trait of "the bashful" (*baishanim*) is not mentioned in the end of Chapter 1 of *Tanya*:

This is because the discussion there concerns the good traits that are naturally inherent in all Jews by birth, whereas the trait of bashfulness was acquired at the Giving of the Torah (see *Chiddushei Aggados Maharsha*, *Yevamos* 79a).

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that the general order is to increase in *hasmadah* and *shekidah* (diligence and persistence) in the study of *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. Engaging in various questions and inquiries, especially those that go beyond the limit, is only an exception to the order, and the wise will understand.

With blessings for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 7,791

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned man, a man of character and great energy,
Rabbi Yitzchak, known as Dr. Levin

Shalom u’Bracha!

Upon receiving your book, *Late Summer Fruit*, for which I extend my thanks—and I trust that you will also send other publications of yours that are not currently in my library, for which I thank you in advance—

I have found occasion to express here an idea that has been on my mind for some time. From time to time, my wonder and astonishment only grow as to why it has not yet been implemented. It is this:

The compilation of a history of the decrees and the Holocaust, reflecting the reality as it pertains to those who are G-d-fearing and observant of His word.

While several publications have appeared over these years describing various periods from the days of the decrees and the Holocaust, aside from a very small number—which a child could count—they either omit entirely the portion pertaining to the G-d-fearing and their institutions, or at the very least, allocate to them a portion far smaller than what is required, or—what is even worse—distort the facts.

Now, among the few aforementioned publications, it is understood that collections such as *Eleh Azkarah* and the like stand out. But surely, for one such as yourself, it is unnecessary to emphasize that this is not sufficient at all, especially in comparison to the publications of the opposing side, in which matters are recorded in a distorted manner.

I was particularly moved to write this to you upon seeing in your book, which I received, articles whose content falls within the aforementioned framework.

It seems to me that some years ago there was a discussion in some of the Chareidi periodicals regarding this. Likewise, in my conversations with visitors from Eretz Yisrael who visited here, they also touched upon this idea. But as of now, the fruits have not been seen—or at the very least, I am not aware of any fruits. And, as is human nature, many details are lost and forgotten; and if you would say not only details, but even essential matters—especially since in our era, new things and problems arise every day that capture our attention, demand study, and consume our spare time, even when we have any.

It would be pleasant for me to know that there are those who are occupied with documenting the aforementioned period, and that the project is progressing at the necessary pace.

May it be the will of Hashem that the situation will soon change, so that we may record in a book of history chapters filled with joyous content, in a good that is visible and revealed.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7,791***

**Dr. Levin:** Another letter to him—see below, 7,853.

## 7,792

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and energetic individual, Rabbi Chaim D., may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 Marcheshvan. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring us good news regarding your health and your organizational affairs—"good" in the sense explained by our Sages: good for Heaven, good for people, and good for the one who produces fruit (Kiddushin 40a). This, of course, includes your lofty project of continuing the publication of your commentary on Tanach, *Da’as Sofrim*, which synthesizes the traditional commentaries on Tanach, as in many chapters and parshiyos they complement one another, and you explain them in clear and accessible language.

This is especially relevant in light of the story told by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that his father, the Rebbe Rashab—may the memory of the righteous be for a blessing, may his merit protect us—had a set daily shiur in the study of Tanach. This was in addition to the takkanah he publicized wherever his influence reached, for all who listened to his voice to study each day a portion of the Chumash of the weekly parsha with the commentary of Rashi.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

Because of the interest of the subject, I am transcribing here some notes on the commentary of the 20th [chapter] in this week’s parsha, Parshas Vayeitzei:

**At the beginning.** You explain that Yaakov left the place where his father resided for Be’er Sheva. Now, although this is indeed the *drash* of our Sages (Bereishis Rabbah 68:5), the *peshuto shel mikra* (the literal meaning of the verse), according to the flow of the verses from the *preceding* parsha and also in terms of time (26:23-25), indicates that Yitzchak had pitched his tent *at that time* in Be’er Sheva. As for what is written later (35:27), "Hevron, where Avraham and Yitzchak sojourned" (and as the Tanchuma questions here)—the intent of that verse is to designate the place of their *permanent* residence, as it says that both Avraham and Yitzchak lived there. And understand this. See also Ramban on our parsha (28:17).

**In the commentary at the end of the parsha:** The greatness of Yaakov, that he immediately recognized the angels, etc., "Machanayim"—a camp of people with a camp of angels. In the notes, the source is not cited—it is the commentary of the Ibn Ezra and the Ramban. One should add to this: "Machanayim" is a dual form (and not the plural form, as is written later in the continuation of the story: [for the two] "machanos"), which emphasizes a greater belonging and connection between the parts, that they are *one* pair. And in this, too, is hinted the greatness of Yaakov and the people with him, that the camp on earth is like the camp of the angels, blessing Hashem, etc. (see Ramban), or that the camp of the angels came not to fight, but to join the camp of Yaakov (see Targum Yonasan ben Uziel and Targum Yerushalmi).

***

**Rabbi Chaim D.:** Rabinowitz.
**His commentary on Tanach, Da’as Sofrim:** See below, letter 7,798.

## 7,793

7,793

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

The Administration of Yeshivas Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch
in Melbourne
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

I have received the news regarding the incident, may we be spared, that occurred in the old building of the Yeshivah.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon, the tradition from the holy ones of the supernal—as recorded in the holy handwriting of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya (who rules in the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who rules in the revealed aspects of Torah)—that after a fire one becomes wealthy, will be fulfilled in its entirety. He explains that this corresponds to the attribute of Yaakov: "an inheritance without boundaries," "extending from one end to the other," etc.

In particular, based on the need to add precision to this: seemingly, two opposites are mentioned here—"an inheritance without boundaries" and "extending from one end to the other," which implies being limited by two ends.

Therefore, it must be that the intention is the unification of these two matters: an inheritance without boundaries within a limited space. As is well known, the example of this is that "the place of the Ark is not included in the measurement"—it is two and a half cubits long and one and a half cubits wide, **specifically**, and it is precisely in that place that the concept of "not being included in the measurement" is drawn down.

And similarly—in all times—within the four cubits of Torah, the batei medrash and yeshivos: in a limited space, beyond the fact that the boundary is blessed with the greatest possible measure, "from one end to the other," there is also drawn down the concept of "an inheritance without boundaries." [And therefore, this is only in the attribute of Tiferes, and in the inwardness of the attribute—which ascends into the inwardness of the Keter, where "the impossible becomes possible"], and this is understood.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

Since regarding the above, one must elaborate and explain: the practical takeaway is that in the physical matters of fundraising, etc., which by their nature are limited, the limit of the sums should be the greatest possible, and through this, the matter will be influenced to be utilized in a way of abundance.

## 7,794

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 24 Mar-Cheshvan and the subsequent one.

1) The manner of davening in your current situation:

On Shabbos and Yom Tov, you may lengthen your davening (initially, to a small degree). On weekdays, for the time being, focus only on the meaning of the words, as you are bound by the schedule of the yeshiva. You should also take note of what is written in your letter regarding the *Kuntres HaTefillah* on this matter.

2) The manner of *hisbonenus* before davening, and specifically how to enable yourself to lengthen your davening as mentioned above:

Since this matter concerns *hisbonenus* (and not the study or acquisition of new knowledge), it is more appropriate to contemplate a subject that you have already studied several times and are familiar with. The *hisbonenus* should consist of either deepening your understanding, reviewing what you know, or expanding upon the practical application of these concepts, or regarding *midos*, etc. In this, there is a variation in human nature: there are those for whom *hisbonenus* is absorbed better when they review the subject using the Rebbe’s original wording, and conversely, there are those for whom it is better to review the content rather than the specific phrasing.

3) Bringing the *hisbonenus* to impact good *midos*, etc.:

In addition to the fact that in the vast majority of cases, every *hisbonenus* results in a specific good *midah*, there is a point common to all: since the *hisbonenus* is on a subject of the Torah of Hashem, it always results in an awareness of the greatness of Hashem, and likewise, in the second point—the lowliness of man (see *Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim*, beginning of *siman* 98). As mentioned, this is a point common to all; one can find in every *hisbonenus* a specific *midah* as well.

4) Connecting the mind to the subject for a significant amount of time:

As with all matters of Torah and holiness, regarding this too it is said, "Little by little I will drive them out." That is to say, one should begin by training oneself to connect one’s thoughts for a short while, and gradually increase the time. To facilitate this, keep the *sefer* or *Siddur* open before you to the specific passages and topics you are contemplating.

5) The *avodah* of *Krias Shema* before retiring:

In addition to the rule common to all—a reckoning of the thoughts, speech, and actions of the day that has passed—there are details specific to each individual, depending on the nature of their soul and their status in *Torah u'mitzvos*, etc. Sometimes one needs to encourage and uplift the spirit, and sometimes the opposite is required, and so on with more specific matters.

6) How to divide one’s dedication and time between the study of *Nigleh* and *Chassidus*:

It is understood and simple that first and foremost, one must study according to the yeshiva’s schedule—hours for *Nigleh* separately and hours for *Chassidus* separately. During the times outside of the schedule, in addition to the three known *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, and the study of necessary *halachos*, it depends on what your heart desires, especially regarding in-depth study (*iyun*).

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires regarding the matters you wrote about. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings,

P.S.
The above, even after this breakdown, are only general instructions. Regarding the specifics and the details of the details, you should present your matters to your *mashpia* of *Chassidus*, who will advise you in accordance with the tradition of the *mashpi'im* of *Chassidus* of Tomchei Temimim from generation to generation.

## 7,397

With blessings for good news regarding all of the above.

## 7,799

7,799

B”H, 8 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby confirm receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos. As discussed, we will be in contact from here with the friends in Antwerp regarding the matter you wrote about, and it is understood that once the situation becomes clear, they will inform you. May it be His will that it turns out for the best, as the Sages say: “Good for Heaven, good for people, and good for the one who produces fruit” (Kiddushin 40a).

Since everything is by Divine Providence—especially as explained in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov [which is also established and necessitated by the words of our Sages, as is known from the proof of Rabbeinu HaZaken from Chullin 63a: “Your word is established in Heaven,” etc.]—and since your letter was received a few days before 19 Kislev, it is my duty (and privilege) to awaken and remind you of the significance of this day. Its inner intent for generations, in the words of the Rebbe, is that of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Rebbe Rashab—may the memory of the righteous and holy be for a blessing, and may his merit protect us [whom you, my dear friend, have told me several times that you merited to see].

“This is the beginning of Your works, etc., to draw down the revelation of the light of the inner dimension of our holy Torah, which is drawn down on this day as a general influence for the entire year. It is incumbent upon us to awaken our hearts on this day, etc., so that the light of our soul may be illuminated by the light of the inner dimension of His Torah.”

If these words are directed to everyone, how much more so to one who heard words of Torah from him, and especially one who has influence over many others, where the merit of the many assists him and also demands of him, “Give me to drink,” etc. Surely, for you, my dear friend, there is no need for elaboration on this.

With respect and blessings.

P.S.

There is a slight discomfort in writing about both of the aforementioned matters in one letter, but my hope is strong that you will not suspect me of implying any condition, Heaven forbid. And if one were to say that there is some connection between the two matters, it is solely in accordance with the emphasis of Chassidic teaching in general, and Chabad in particular, on the concept of Ahavas Yisrael—to the point of the statement that Ahavas Yisrael (and “Love your fellow as yourself”) and Ahavas Hashem are one and the same. Consider the Mishnah in Sanhedrin, Chapter 6: When a person suffers, what does the Shechinah say? “My head is too heavy,” etc. See also Rashi on Shabbos 31a: “Your fellow” refers to the Holy One, blessed be He, etc.; another interpretation: your literal friend.

## 7101

B"H, 11 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write your thoughts regarding the responsibility in connection with the shidduch, etc.

As is evident from your letter, the entire concern is whether your level of yiras shamayim will suffice for the requirements of the young woman’s parents, at least regarding practical conduct, attire, etc.

If so, the entire matter is in your hands; if you so desire, you can certainly suffice even in this, to fulfill their requirements. On the contrary, this is an additional reason to bring the shidduch to fruition as soon as possible, since this will assist in elevating your standing in matters of yiras shamayim. Our Sages have informed us that "one mitzvah leads to another," and it is highly probable that as time goes on, there will be further additions in the aforementioned matters of Yiddishkeit. It has already been said (if one only reaches the level of) "Taste and see that Hashem is good" (Tehillim 34:9)—which includes, of course, the simple command of Hashem and His instructions to the Bnei Yisrael, His close people, in His Torah and mitzvos.

Since everything is by Hashgacha Pratis, it is my duty (and privilege) to awaken you to the absolute necessity and personal obligation to set times for the study of Pnimius HaTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If this was necessary at all times and in all places, it is certainly so in our era, and especially in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and also that every weekday, before the morning davening, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

May it be the will of Hashem that through the study of Torah with explanation, and the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur* in general, all the matters alluded to in this portion—as explained in the discourses of *Dipei Sichatan* etc. (Likutei Torah, ibid.; *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, etc.)—and in their inner point, as expressed in the language of the Likutei Torah there, will bring about a revelation and *hemshech* from the *Atzmus* of *Chochma* from above.

This is also the concept of the miracle of Kislev, which we have now entered—a miracle involving oil, and olive oil is the concept of *Chochma*, as is known.

With blessings for an increase in soldiers in Torah and its mitzvos for long, good days and years, in health and joy.

## 7503

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Chaim, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of Thursday was received. Regarding your question as to what you should study during the full day and night of the auspicious day, the upcoming 19th of Kislev—the Rosh Hashanah of the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus:

Based on the essence of this day, it is understood that the study should be in the teachings of the Baal HaSimcha and the Geulah—namely, the teachings of Chassidus Chabad—whether in his seforim (such as Sefer HaTanya, Torah Or, and Likutei Torah), or (together with the explanations that have been added) in the maamarim and sichos of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, may their merit protect us.

However, since all parts of our Torah are a "Torah of life," and "great is study that leads to action," one must also follow the guidance and conduct of the teachings of Chassidus.

It is most appropriate and good that during the course of the day and night, you should endeavor to "spread the wellsprings outward." For the movement of one’s lips is an act (albeit a minor one), and one should not be satisfied with this alone, but should also engage in a major act—doing good for fellow Yidden. And there is nothing that can stand in the way of will. May it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding all of the above.

## 7104

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Kislev, along with the enclosure and the *pidyon nefesh* which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what was written in my letter to the *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* (sent separately), which is understood and simple that it is the primary focus in this matter, and relying on our Sages’ teaching that "one who causes [a mitzvah] to be done is greater than the one who does it"—surely, much more than this will come to you. However, the channel, the vessel, and the manner for receiving the blessings of Hashem is through *simcha* and a good heart, as explained in many places.

As for what you wrote regarding the events during the *krias haTorah*, the dream, etc.—you should completely divert your attention from this. Especially since the words of Torah are, on the contrary, meant to gladden the heart, and the essence of Torah is to draw down goodness in a way that is visible and revealed, below ten *tefachim*.

Regarding the above, the opinions on this are well-known in the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Alter Rebbe, *Siman* 288, *Seif* 7. The conclusion and final word of that *seif* is that there is **no** instruction from Heaven in such things at all. You should also gladden the hearts of others; I mean that you should set aside 18 *lirot* for *tzedakah* during the days remaining until the conclusion and final day of the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption, in addition to the *tzedakah* on the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the upcoming *Yom Tov*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and with blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 7,507

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Kislev, in which you write regarding a position being offered to you, detailing the positive and negative aspects of it, and asking for my opinion:

Regarding the institution itself that is being established, you are surely aware that there were differences of opinion concerning it in general, though as you write, a decision has now been reached.

2) Every new institution, until its form is consolidated in the natural course of events, will certainly have various differences of opinion regarding its details and its general direction as well.

3) On the other hand, the institution is greatly needed, and this is already recognized, as is proven by the aforementioned decision. Therefore:

4) If you are **independent**, and you wish to work for the strengthening and dissemination of Yiddishkeit without being deterred by the difficulties involved [for as is explained in the holy seforim, the greater the matter in holiness, the more the distracting elements increase], and you possess the **strength** to begin the matter and also to continue it until it reaches completion—and as mentioned, in a way that you will not be deterred by differences of opinion, provided that the goal is realized—

It is highly appropriate that you accept the aforementioned offer and act within it with energy befitting the importance and magnitude of the matter.

5) If, on the other hand, you are looking for matters that are not taxing, or, to put it more **clearly**, you want to have your time free for matters of holiness as a **private** individual, such as studying Torah for yourself with peace of mind and body, without distracting matters—which also includes entering into debate with some of those involved in the true needs of the community, even though their opinions are not in agreement, etc.—

Then it is understood that it is not in such a position that you will find a path to the aforementioned lifestyle.

I do not know your character or the character of the people who have influence over you, but you are surely aware that according to the ways of Anash, the aforementioned position is one of those matters viewed as a beautiful opportunity—to fulfill the will of the Creator who gives the Torah and commands the mitzvah, and it is also based on the explicit law that a mitzvah which cannot be performed by others takes precedence, etc.

On this occasion, since every matter is by Divine Providence, it is my duty (and privilege) to awaken you to the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If in all times and in all places this was a necessity, how much more so in our era, and particularly in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily.

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S.
As per your request, the letter is sent not in the regular order.

## 7508

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and Blessings!

Transcribed below is the text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to send today in anticipation of the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev:

To all participants in the Chag HaGeulah farbrengen, may they live:

I am participating in your farbrengen on the festival that redeemed our souls in peace and gave us the light and vitality of our souls. May it be the will that this hisorerus reveals the inner and essential desire and will within every one of the Bnei Yisrael, until it permeates daily life and actual deed, and may the maayanos be spread outward, and may Malka Meshicha come very soon.

L’chaim, l’chaim v’livracha.

**Menachem Schneerson**

The telegram was surely received in due time. You will certainly inform us here, with the necessary detail, of everything that took place. Thank you in advance.

With respect and with blessings for Chag HaGeulah,

Secretary

## 7510

This is especially true since it also concerns the well-being of her daughter and the grandchildren, may they live and be well. We are commanded in our Torah—and this is emphasized particularly in the teachings of Chassidus, and specifically in the well-known sicha of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—that man was created with a right eye and a left eye, and the right eye is the "kindly eye." This teaches that a Jewish person must look at things in a way that sees the beauty and the good, etc. And since we have been commanded regarding this in our Torah, the Torah of life, it is certain that the strength and the possibility to fulfill this command have been granted, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

## 7,511

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the students of the Chabad School in Zarnoga,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 17 Kislev, and may it be Hashem’s will that you share good news among us.

We are now approaching the days of Chanukah. As the text of the *Al HaNissim* prayer states, Hashem delivered the impure into the hands of the pure, the wicked into the hands of the righteous, and the wanton into the hands of those who occupy themselves with His Torah.

This is true for every single Jew, in all times and in all places. When one stands with *mesiras nefesh*—as instructed by our Torah, the Torah of life—Hashem delivers the *yetzer hara* within the human heart (which is impure, wicked, and wanton) into the hands of the *yetzer hatov* (which is pure, righteous, and yearns for Torah and *mitzvos*). Thus, every person can kindle the candle of a *mitzvah* and the light of Torah, within themselves, within their soul, in their home, and in their surroundings.

May it be Hashem’s will that all of this be fulfilled in each and every one of you.

With blessings for a happy Chanukah and for good tidings.

## 7712

B”H, 22 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Kislev, in which you write about your acquaintance, whose intentions are for the purpose of a *shidduch*, and the positive aspects of this as well as those that are to the contrary, and in this you also mention that there is seemingly opposition from the *avreich’s* family, though you do not explain why they are opposed or the reasons for their opposition.

Regarding your question as to my opinion on the reasons you write: the family connection between them is something we see tangibly, especially in recent generations, that there is no room for concern in this regard, provided that the young man and the young woman are healthy.

2) Regarding your writing that at your current age you need to wait about a year or more until the marriage: it is understood and simple that this does not align with my perspective, for this is not the outlook of our Torah, the Torah of life, in general, and especially among our brethren the Sephardim, to which you both belong. Furthermore, and this is the main point, it is not desirable at all to be acquaintances and friends with the intention of marriage, and at the same time to decide that it is necessary to wait several months, or perhaps even longer, until the actual marriage. As stated, this is not desirable at all, and young people who are *yirei shamayim* and *chareidim* to the word of Hashem should only become acquainted, etc., and become friends **once** a decision has been made that the time has already come to marry in practice. It is clear that the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, are not only for the sake of good in the World to Come after one hundred and twenty years, but that this is the good of a Jewish person in this world as well, to live a happy life in both material and spiritual matters.

3) Regarding your writing on how to bring the matter closer to the *avreich*—it is apparent from your letter that he certainly understands your serious attitude toward the matter, and since he continues the meetings, this is surely a sign that he also has a serious attitude toward it, even if perhaps not as much as you do. These details should be clarified through friends of both of you, such as those you mention in your letter.

Based on the style of your letter, it is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the necessity of living according to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life. I will only add that when one is in a state of confusion and is in need of an additional blessing from the *Ribono shel Olam*, who gives the Torah and commands the *mitzvos*, one should increase in matters of Yiddishkeit, even in daily life. In matters of goodness and holiness, no matter how good one may be, there is always room to add, since we are connected to the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is *Ein Sof*.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

***

**7712**

**To wait about a year:** See also above, Vol. 11, Letter 3736, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7513

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, which was delivered by the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi Sholom Chaim שי' Kesselman.

Regarding what you wrote concerning *emunah peshutah* (simple faith):

It is explained in the holy books, and especially in the books of Chassidus, how it exists in **perfection** within every single man and woman of the Jewish people—for every man and woman is called a son of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah. However, at times the *yetzer hara* disturbs the power of thought and misleads a person into thinking about other matters, and sometimes even about contrary matters. To remedy this, as explained in the holy *Tanya*, one must become angry at the *nefesh habehamis*, etc.—"You are evil and wicked, detestable, abominable, and vile," etc. (*Tanya*, Chapter 29, and in other places as noted in the index at the end of the *Tanya*).

There is another way to approach this, which is even more excellent—and I believe I have already written this to you—which is to completely divert one’s attention (*hesech hada'as*). When the *yetzer* comes with its temptations, one answers it that one is not currently available for such things, because one must study, one must fulfill a *mitzvah*, one must *daven*, etc. Along with this, one should set aside a few coins for *tzedakah* every weekday morning before *davening*, and maintain the three well-known *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. Furthermore, and most essentially, one must maintain diligence and persistence in accordance with the *yeshiva* schedule. After all, even a little light pushes away a great deal of darkness.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 7,515

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the distinguished Chassid, G-d-fearing and upright, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi R. Sh. Y. (may he live)

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you describe the sequence of developments regarding the Chief Rabbinate, and my letter on this matter.

Since there have been contradictory reports in the press regarding my position—and according to the letters I receive here, my stance is still not clear to many—in my opinion, it would be appropriate to publish at least an excerpt from my letter, in order to remove any doubts.

[By the way, and in continuation of the above: I was visited these past few days by some of the leaders of the Mafdal, and we spoke, of course, also regarding the above, to clarify the position, etc. To my regret, it seems that some of them still prefer dubious party gains at the expense of the honor of the Chief Rabbinate. I took the opportunity to reiterate the position in my letter, with an addition and a preface:

That the party gain they anticipate—it is highly doubtful they will achieve it, for it seems they do not accurately assess the political situation and the balance of power as it appears from the outside. Recent developments have brought about a fear that is **growing**, that if the time of the elections is postponed, the influence and opinion of those who wish to separate religion from state will only strengthen and increase.

In my view, this is contrary to the fundamentals of our faith, for it is impossible for any matter concerning the Children of Israel to be separated from our faith and religion, and certainly not to do so officially.

It is obvious that regarding the Mafdal, the party would then lose its very right to exist. And to my astonishment, I must add—though of course I did not say this to them—that it seems they do not even perceive this danger!]

By the way—I believe I also wrote in my letter that although I am not comfortable with public debate in the press, I explicitly emphasized that this does not preclude a clear expression of opinion, without entering into a back-and-forth debate.

Another point was highlighted in our aforementioned conversation: even though the authority of the Chief Rabbinate is not accepted by many circles regarding its rulings and halachic decisions, the defamation and degradation of it are exploited to diminish the standing of all religious matters in any circle whatsoever, and the wise will understand.

With respect and blessing for a happy Chanukah and for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

I received your letter regarding the participation of both candidates (may they live) together at the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen at Kfar Chabad.

I am sure you will inform me of the developments regarding the above since your letter. Thank you in advance.

## 7516

7516

By the grace of Hashem, First Night of Chanukah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the eminent Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, possessor of refined character traits, etc.,
Rabbi D. HaKohen, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of the 6th of Kislev, and subsequently the offprint of *Ma'areches Musar HaKodesh*, etc.

Many thanks for the gift and for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me. It is my strong hope that you will continue to send me future publications from your hand, and certainly those that are the fruit of your own pen.

We are currently in the time of Chanukah, the mitzvah of which involves oil—the "secrets of the secrets of the Torah," as explained in the Zohar and in books of Kabbalah in many places. Yet, it is in a manner that its light shines, and furthermore—at the entrance of one’s house, from the outside.

This is especially true in our generation, the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, the final generation of our exile, which is characterized by double and redoubled darkness. As the Zohar states (Vol. I, 118a): "When the days of Moshiach draw near, even the children of the world will be destined to discover the hidden secrets of wisdom."

And since Chazal have taught us, regarding the study of Torah, that the order must be: "When I would raise a difficulty, he would resolve it for me... and the subject matter would become clarified... did I not know that I was speaking correctly?" (*Bava Metzia* 84a)—

I will take the liberty of offering a few notes in the margins, especially since I am aware of your influence within your circle and environment, and if these points are correct, they carry a special importance. As it has already been said, "And Vahev in Suphah."

Best regards to your son, the Rabbi, shlita, HaKohen. With honor and blessing to each and every one of your household, in a manner of "increasing and continuing," as is the instruction of these days, that the Halacha follows Beis Hillel.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

**General Note.**

Seemingly, the subject of *Musar HaTorah*—which is *Musar HaKodesh*—has as its foundation and its ultimate purpose the actual deed, "deed" in the broad sense, which in its particulars consists of thought, speech, and action. As it is written: "Fear G-d and keep His commandments, for **this** is the whole man."

The matter of the inspiration of *Ruach HaKodesh*, or even more than that—the spirit of prophecy—is at most in the category of a reward for *avodah* and action. This is evident from the fact that it is not within human power to command. As the Rambam phrases it: "Even though they direct their minds, it is possible that the Shechinah will rest upon them, and it is possible that it will not" (*Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 7, Halacha 5; see there in *Lechem Mishneh*). How much more so that it is not commanded for every person to be a prophet, or even to possess *Ruach HaKodesh*. See also the Rambam at the end of *Hilchos Teshuvah* and the end of *Hilchos Melachim* regarding the reason why all of Israel yearned for the days of Moshiach.

In addition to all the above, which in my opinion is necessary in every place—there is a double and redoubled importance to what has been said, specifically in our current era, which requires an emphasis on the necessity of fulfilling practical *mitzvos* in day-to-day life. These have no substitute in any other matter whatsoever, even though "the Merciful One desires the heart," etc.

It is understood that there is no contradiction at all in what has been said here to what is explained in the Rambam there, and which is emphasized especially in the teachings of Chassidus: that the purpose of man is "Know the G-d of your father and serve Him with a whole heart." For this is, in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (*Kuntres Acharon* of the Tanya, 156b), "a great and lofty mitzvah," etc.—only that this is **one of the 613 mitzvos**, and a person must fulfill all 613, etc. Therefore, one must increase the study of all 613 and their fulfillment in actual practice through thought, speech, and action, etc. See there.

Beginning of the offprint, page 367:
"The spirit of prophecy or *Ruach HaKodesh*."
Apparently, this booklet does not enter into a detailed breakdown of the levels, and includes them together. For there are three levels: prophecy, which ended in the days of Chaggai, Zechariah, and Malachi; *Ruach HaKodesh*; and then *Bas Kol*. The term "prophecy" (in practice) and *Ruach HaKodesh* mentioned regarding the periods thereafter—this is a borrowed term and belongs to the level of *Bas Kol* (see *Shaar Ruach HaKodesh* of the Arizal, who is the final authority in such matters).

Page 383, at the end:
"The choice in its fullness is given to Israel."
See *Likkutei Torah* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Parshas Emor*, 38, end of side b.

Page 34, at the end:
"The foundation of prayer... unity with the general cosmic will... which is the Divine desire," etc.
Seemingly, one can find support for this in the directive of Chazal to recite the prayer in the plural. However, it is more correct to say that the essence of prayer is to be included in the Divine will and desire (from below to above), and through this, the power of prayer can influence matters in the world (from above to below)—**after this**—and also upon the general will, or in the words of the booklet, to create a revolution.

At the end, page 49:
"For *Ruach HaKodesh* in Israel is not a lack of perfection, but rather," etc.
Based on what was said above, this is highly questionable (perhaps his intention is if the deficiency is in the nation as a whole, and not regarding each individual)—except after the coming of Moshiach, which is the time of the promise: "I will pour out My spirit upon **all** flesh, and they shall prophesy," etc.

Citations and references to the above were brought in the introduction (by Rabbi Margaliot, shlita) to *She'eilot U'Teshuvot Min HaShamayim*.

And in the essays of A. J. Heschel, shlita, who quotes your honor: "Did the Rambam believe that he merited prophecy?" (*Safer HaYovel* for L. Ginzberg).

## 7517

B"H, First Night of Chanukah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Chanukah gathering
of friends and supporters of Yeshivas Achei Temimim
in Newark, N.J.
May Hashem keep them alive.

Shalom u’vracha!

It was with satisfaction that I received the notification regarding the upcoming Chanukah gathering, organized in connection with the founding and opening of the new branch of Yeshivas Achei Temimim in Newark, N.J.

This gathering takes place during the days of Chanukah, when we celebrate and recall that when the kingdom of Greece aimed to make Jews forget Torah and mitzvos, the mesiras nefesh of the Jews of that time—their study and observance of Torah and mitzvos—brought them the victory that "the strong were delivered into the hands of the weak, and the many into the hands of the few."

This is also a lesson and a directive for our own time, in this country and regarding the issue of children’s education—where there are no decrees, chas v’shalom, against studying Torah and fulfilling mitzvos.

However, the situation is currently, unfortunately, such that the students of yeshivos where one learns Hashem’s Torah and is educated to fulfill His mitzvos are not the majority of all Jewish children, nor are they from the most influential families in material life.

Chanukah reminds us and calls upon us that, just as in those days, so too at this time, through mesiras nefesh for authentic Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos, the few in number will eventually attract the many, until the "few" will have the complete victory and raise a generation educated in the spirit of chinuch al taharas hakodesh—and through this, bring about the redemption (geulah) of the entire Jewish people.

Yeshivas Achei Temimim, in all its branches, is dedicated to the aforementioned goal and chinuch. Therefore, I am strong in the hope that the call of Chanukah will evoke in all participants a strengthened activity for the maintenance and expansion of the yeshiva.

And this will bring them Hashem’s blessings in both material and spiritual matters.

With respect and with a wish for success and a happy Chanukah.

**M. Schneerson**

7108

By the Grace of Hashem, First Night of Chanukah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, man of action and many accomplishments,
Rabbi Ch. Y. L. Shlita,

Peace and Blessing!

On the eve of Chanukah, I received your letter from the first day of the week, in which you write that the tenth volume of your sefer, *Taharas Yom Tov*, is nearing completion at the printers.

There is a connection to be found in this to these days [as emphasized in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, that every matter and detail is through Hashgacha Pratis from the Ribono shel Olam, who oversees each and every one], and as the text of *Al Hanissim* states: "You delivered the impure into the hands of the pure... and they purified Your Sanctuary and kindled lights..."

This corresponds to the words of the prophet regarding the future, true, and complete Geulah: "And I will sprinkle upon you pure water, and you shall be purified... and you shall dwell in the land..."

For one thing is dependent upon the other, as purity leads to Chassidus, and Chassidus leads to Ruach Hakodesh, and Eliyahu Hanavi, who is the herald of the Geulah.

Despite the multitude of preoccupations, I will fulfill your request to provide at least some notes on the sefer *Zera Yitzchak* which you published, and on your sefarim.

May it be the will of the One who grants man knowledge that He grant us, in the midst of all Klal Yisrael, Chochma, Binah, and Da’as to study His Torah, both the revealed and the inner dimensions—which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—so that they may walk together, for it is one Torah, to learn and to teach, to observe, to do, and to fulfill with love, and as we are commanded, with joy and goodness of heart.

With respect and a blessing for success in your endeavors to increase purity, in a manner of "adding and increasing," as is the instruction of these days, that the Halacha follows Beis Hillel.

P.S.
I desired to do your will, and I have transcribed herewith some notes on the sefer *Zera Yitzchak* which you published, as well as on your sefer *Taharas Yom Tov*—the volumes I received recently—and as time permitted, in haste.

**Zera Yitzchak, at the beginning.** *Berachos* 1:1: "And if you say, why did it not teach Pesach..." It may be answered that the Mishnah follows Rabbi Elazar ben Azaryah. This is similar to the Gemara later (9a). It is puzzling that it is not mentioned. It should be noted that the Yerushalmi here (end of Halacha 1) suggests that some have the version in the Mishnah including the eating of the Pesach offering, in one clause together with the burning of the fats (and not with those eaten for one day). If so, they share the same law, and they did not say in this case (according to the Rabbis) "until midnight" (according to the commentary of the *Baal Hachareidim* in the Yerushalmi). The reason must be that the members of the *chaburah* are zealous (*Pesachim* 85a).

The *Zera Yitzchak* assumes simply that the Rabbis decreed regarding Pesach as well—this must be because he holds like the commentary *Mareh Hapanim* in the Yerushalmi there. And his question regarding the burning of the fats—it is because women and minors also eat.

**Regarding the term *Adam*—*Megillah* 3:3:** The Mishnah says "a person"—it refers to a Yisrael, for Yisrael are called *Adam*. This proves the author holds that even in the language of Chazal, *Adam* excludes a non-Jew. This is also stated in *Tosafos Yom Tov* on *Bikkurim* 2:7 (and it contradicts what he wrote in his commentary on *Avos* 3:14), and it is not like the *Tosafos* in *Dah* "Mah" (*Bava Kamma* 9a, bottom). As noted in *Sdei Chemed*, *Klallim* 1, 276. I have since seen that you, too, in your notes at the end of the sefer, addressed all of the above. I have since seen that it is surprising to say the above, for it is explained (*Yevamos* 61a and *Tosafos* there) that in a place where it also writes "beast," then when it mentions the name—*Adam* includes even a non-Jew. In the aforementioned cases, it is similar to this, and if so, it does not belong to the rule that non-Jews are not called *Adam* [in *Megillah*, *Adam* comes in contrast to land. In *Bikkurim* and *Bava Kamma*—to beast and ox. In *Avos*—to Yisrael]. It remains difficult. It should be noted that the *Malbim* in his commentary on the Torah, beginning of *Vayikra*, discusses all of this at length.

**At the end of the sefer, p. 397.** "The five letters are doubled..." and so it is in the *Zohar*. Its source requires study.
The reason is according to the order of the verse: "Hashem is King, Hashem is King, Hashem will be King..." Seemingly, this is not understood, as this is not one verse but three verses, and their order begins with "Hashem will be King" in the Torah, and the two that follow are in *Tehillim*.
It can be explained simply that it is based on the words of the *Zohar Chadash* (34a): "It is written: Hashem is King, Hashem is King, Hashem will be King forever and ever."
And so it is in *Sefer HaBahir*, sections 111 and 127. And in *Shaar HaKavanos* (in its place): "Hashem is King... forever and ever, this verse, its matter is..." And so it is in the writings of the Arizal and in many places. And in *Emek HaMelech*, *Shaar* 6, *Perek* 2: "This verse... is *Atzilus* of *Atzilus*... Rabbi Akiva said: Every single day an angel stands in the firmament and says: Hashem is King... forever and ever."
See there their combination **in prayer**—he calls them one verse and is precise about their order in prayer, even though in the Tanach they appear scattered and in a different order.
We find the same regarding the Rambam in his commentary on the Mishnah (*Zevachim*, at the end): "Jerusalem is called an inheritance... that he said at the beginning of his words... afterwards he said... and he said..."—for they are arranged in the **prayer** *Yehi Kavod* (and like the aforementioned "Hashem is King... forever and ever"), even though they are three scattered verses and the last one is earlier in the order of the verse (as in the case at hand).

**In the writings it is stated... and so it is brought in *Emek HaMelech*:** See *Emek HaMelech*, *Shaar* 1, *Perek* 56; *Megaleh Amukos*, *Ofan* 152; *Koheles Yaakov*, p. 132.

**"All Yisrael have a share in the World to Come... the Holy One will cause every tzaddik to inherit..."** The author must mean that just as peace is necessary for the reward of a share in the World to Come, as per the *Shelah*, so too is it necessary for the reward of 310 worlds. But he does not mean to say that having a share is the matter of 310 worlds. As is proven also by the condition: "to every **tzaddik**," and not like the Mishnah, which says "all Yisrael" have a share.

***Sefer Taharas Yom Tov*, Vol. 5.** At the beginning, p. 11 (and there, p. 90). That their children should not follow their bier, etc., to ban with the blowing of the shofar, etc., and they should remain at home. It is surprising that you did not explain in your notes the law and the custom in this regard **in practice** among G-d-fearing congregations. For *Maaseh Rav* (the practice of a great person) is significant. Surely it is an honor for the deceased (and an honor for the living) when the children accompany him. And they delay the burial, even though it is a negative commandment, so that his relatives may come—and who is closer than a son, who is like the thigh of his father? See *Bava Basra* (159a) that they are one and the same. Surely it is in the category of honoring one's father, for he honors him in his death. It is explicitly mentioned in many places that children accompany their father. See *Maavar Yabbok*, *Imrei Noam*, chapter 23.
On the other hand, many of the greatest of the world, in the revealed and the hidden, and in many communities, have accepted and practiced (for the reason in this sefer) to announce (and some—with a ban) that they should not accompany, etc.
Among them in Eretz Yisrael and in Jerusalem—may it be rebuilt—"the *Baal Shulchan Gavoha*, the *Baal Ohr Hachaim*, the *Baal Admas Kodesh*, Rabbi Yisrael Yaakov Algazi, the *Baal Shoshannim L'David*, the *Baal Batei Kehuna* (student of the *Pri Chadash*), the *Chida*, the *Maharit Algazi*, and the Kabbalist Rabbi Shalom Sharabi... also among the great Ashkenazic rabbis who were in Jerusalem and Eretz Yisrael throughout all these times." The custom of Jerusalem in particular: "Before they take the deceased male (no less than 13 years old) out of the house, they announce with a ban," and the children say Kaddish inside the house before they take him out (*Gesher Hachaim*, Vol. 1, Ch. 12). And in the text of the ban in the will of the *Sdei Chemed*: "Not before his bier and not after his bier... and not from any of his sides" (and it is explained there that the intent is—to sons and daughters, grandchildren, etc.).
And it seems many are accustomed—(and perhaps in order to mediate between the aforementioned reasons, and also because many disagree with saying Kaddish before the burial—see *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe, *Orach Chaim* 271; see also *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah*, end of 376)—to change the text of the announcement (generally, and not with a ban and not with the blowing of a shofar—so as not to cause stumbling?), and the children, etc., leave the house before the funeral begins and wait at the cemetery and say Kaddish there after the burial.
I have seen one author who wrote that "we are not permitted" to tell the children of Yisrael based on "such secrets of Torah," "and even though it happened that some holy or righteous person commanded to announce a ban, etc., they did so specifically to their children after them," "for it is explicit in the Torah: 'And his sons carried him to the land of Canaan,' etc."
It is obvious that one who is unaware of all the aforementioned Rabbis, of the custom in many congregations, and above all—in Jerusalem and Eretz Yisrael—is not at all the master to give an opinion on this.
Regarding his note that it is explicit in the Torah, etc.—this is the measure of all those who wish to separate, G-d forbid, between the children of Yisrael and the inner dimension of the Torah, and who touch upon the secrets of Torah—he stumbled in the revealed Torah, and in his own style—in what is explicit in the Torah, that Yaakov said to Reuven, "My strength and the beginning of my power" (a matter that even school children know, for it is brought in Rashi in the Chumash), and the reason not to accompany does not apply to him.
Regarding the essence of the matter and the seeming surprise, that in the sefarim before the aforementioned, the matter of the announcement and the ban, etc., is not found, and on the contrary, in many places it is brought that the children do accompany—it can be said that it is like many laws, "decrees, ordinances, and customs" of the great men of Yisrael who innovated and decreed in their generation and from their generation onwards. It can be said that they found a breach and made a fence for it.
For they saw that after a time, people began to marry—whether to study Torah until there is no millstone on their neck, whether to plant a vineyard first and then build a house (and the vineyard and the house—not specifically five vines and four cubits by four cubits), and afterwards to take a wife. And in the footsteps of Mashiach, "Behold, He is standing behind our wall, He is watching," etc.—they are delaying the Geulah through this sin. Therefore, they instructed to announce, etc., in order to "strengthen the religion and repair the world." And the aforementioned great men of Yisrael were lenient with themselves to announce at their own funerals, so that all the people would follow and know. Similar to *Kesuvos* (8b, bottom). This still requires study.

**At the end, p. 184.** (The Arizal at the time of his purification when they brought his body to the mikveh) "He lowered himself with his head to immerse by himself." This is in the introduction to *Nagid U'Metzaveh* and in *Shivchei HaArizal*. From the stories of the early Chassidim, that at the purification of the great Maggid of Mezeritch, according to the lot, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe merited the "head of fine gold," and "they led the Maggid, of blessed memory, to the mikveh to immerse, and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe said: Behold, our Sages said, 'The righteous are great in their death,' etc., therefore they should leave our teacher to immerse by himself, and so it was, that they left him and he immersed three times" (*Beis Rebbe*, Vol. 1, p. 10, note 2).

**There, p. 188, at the end, section 37.** "My father-in-law and my uncle"—the intent is to our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*) and his brother, author of the sefer *She'eris Yehuda*. And our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe was then seven years old, and his brother—three years old.

**Vol. 7, at the beginning, p. 9.** Crumbs of *Hamotzi*. Note from *Zohar Chadash* (244a): "He who is careless with crumbs of bread, etc., all the more so he who is careless with crumbs of the intellect, etc." And there (245a): "The householder, etc., completes the blessing and afterwards breaks, etc., like an egg, etc., like an olive's bulk, etc., and these correspond to the drops of seed, etc., and crumbs like an olive's bulk are in the tzaddik, etc."

**There, at the end of the sefer, p. 293.** The *Zohar*, *Parshas Noach*: A tzaddik is called one who does not sin in this sin. This is similar in many places and sefarim. I have always wondered about this, for specifically in the *Zohar* there it does not seem so, for he opens there: "And your people are **all** tzaddikim," for **all** Yisrael guard the covenant, and *Ohr Hachama* explains there that it is as our Sages said (*Bava Basra* 165a) that it is a minority of a minority who follow after forbidden relations. But—is everyone like Yaakov our father regarding the sin about which he discusses in this sefer?
And even though it can be answered and distinguished regarding the calling of the name "tzaddik" between the individual and the many, as written in *Ohr Hachaim* there—in any case, proof cannot be brought from here.

**There, at the end of the notes, p. 292.** I was alarmed to read what is printed there regarding the ordinance of a mikveh on top of a mikveh, the *otzar* (reservoir) which is a repair that is from the holy of Yisrael and his glory, the Rebbe Rashab (father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe), of blessed memory, who sacrificed his holy soul for the matter of mikvaos, as is known to all who came to our country in the past. And the great men of his generation, a generation of knowledge, debated with him in these laws of *halacha* in particular, etc.
And anyone who knows the nature of mikvaos will understand how many advantages there are in a mikveh on top of an *otzar*. And the concern he writes that the *otzar* will fill with mud, etc., because there is no measure of when to check the *otzar*—this is also in an *otzar* from the side.
I am very surprised that you printed such a letter. And not enough with the above—you go back and print also what the writer writes, to remove tzaddikim from the heavenly academy after they have sat there for three hundred years. Are we truly responsible for such rumors? And the wise will understand.

**Vol. 8, at the beginning.** Among the repairs of *Keri* is to be careful in the mitzvah of *Tefillin*. Note from our Sages, *Megillah* (16b): "And precious"—these are *Tefillin*. And in the glosses of R. Chaim Vital to *Zohar Chadash* 197b: "The drop is called precious." And in *Meorei Ohr*, *Maareches Kuf*, 546: "The drop is drawn, etc., and when it goes to the *Nukvah* of *Nogah*, it becomes in the place of *Yakar* (precious), *Keri* (nocturnal emission)." See the *maamar* of the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek, *D.H. Vayifga Bamakom* (in *Sefer Ohr HaTorah*, *Parshas Vayetzei*).

**There, p. 93.** Regarding the laws of *Tefillas Haderech*. According to our Sages, "A matter of clothing is precious," I will inform you of the conduct of the Rebbe, father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, when he traveled from his home, even though he remained in one place for several months, he would say *Tefillas Haderech* every day after prayer—without the Name and Kingship.

**There, at the end, p. 192.** "A hair's breadth." Note from our Sages that to the wicked, the *Yetzer Hara* appears like a hair's breadth (*Sukkah* 52a). And with the righteous—the Holy One, blessed be He, is exacting like a hair's breadth (*Yevamos* 121b).

**Vol. 9, at the beginning, p. 110:** To sleep at night in the four corners of the *tzitzis*. See *Piskei Dinim* of the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek to *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, section 11.
For it is a repair for the eyes. Note from the language of the Rambam, *Hilchos Deos* (Ch. 4, 19): "Sexual intercourse is... the light of the eyes... all who are immersed in it... his eyes become dim."
Sight brings a person to improper thoughts, and through improper thoughts, etc. Seemingly (see *Tosafos* *Dah* "V'Yayin", *Berachos* 41b), we find greater than this in our Mishnah, that even if he saw, he did not have improper thoughts (*Zavim* 2:2). From this is an instruction for the greatness of the caution in the definition of the sense of sight. See *Kuntres HaAvodah* (by the Rebbe Rashab), Ch. 2.

**There, at the end, p. 214:** The miracle of Chanukah, etc., "He who comes to purify," etc. It is known the precision of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*) (see *Likkutei Torah*, *Devarim* 89d) "to purify" (and not "to be purified")—others. And similarly regarding *Ner Chanukah*, that its mitzvah is specifically at the entrance of his house from the outside. And even in his house—specifically if the members of the household are awake. And if not—the ruling of our Torah is that even for himself he does not recite a blessing (see *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, end of 672). And the wise will understand.

**Vol. 10, at the beginning, p. 33:** Among the repairs, etc., "To love peace and pursue peace," etc., "Turn from evil and do good." Since you, in the continuation to the end of the previous volume, and in what you concluded, to illuminate outside and to purify others, you opened. See *Sefer Zera Yitzchak* at the end (brought at the beginning of these notes).
And especially according to what is brought that the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, interpreted "Turn from evil and do (the evil) good."

**There, at the end of the sefer (in the margins I have), p. 50:** To connect *Geulah* to *Tefillah*, etc., "And I have done what is good in Your eyes" (according to *Berachos* 10b). In this sin he blemishes the ten *Sefiros*, etc., he shall repair the ten *Sefiros*. See above in the note to Vol. 8 from the words of the Rambam.
Note from *Zohar Chadash* (128b): "And I have done what is good in Your eyes, that he connects *Geulah* to *Tefillah*, etc., at that time, etc., this tzaddik awakens to connect in the place that is needed, etc., and all the limbs are connected, etc., in this tzaddik who is called 'good,' etc."
See the *maamar* of the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek, *D.H. Hamalach Hagoel* (in *Sefer Ohr HaTorah*), an explanation of the matter of connecting *Geulah* to *Tefillah*.
And he concludes there—in the *Zohar*—regarding those who make themselves wicked, "And if a person knew how much benefit and merit (they cause the righteous) and they merit because of them, when they merit them, they would go after them and pursue them like one who pursues after life."
And before this—and it is relevant to the note at the beginning of the sefer: "A righteous person should pursue the wicked and acquire him, etc. Anyone who holds the hand of the wicked and strives with him to leave the evil path, etc., causes the whole world to stand in its existence above and below, and upon this person it is written: 'My covenant was with him, life and peace,' etc., 'His seed shall be mighty in the land,' etc., 'Light shines in the darkness for the upright,' etc."

## 7,519

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Kislev, in which you write about a practice you observed in a certain yeshiva that, in your opinion, is undesirable and inappropriate:

It is understood that regarding the above, one should approach the yeshiva administration and clarify the matter with them. If the verdict of our holy Torah is to judge even an individual favorably, how much more so does this apply to a yeshiva where the Torah of Hashem is studied.

2) Regarding your question about what the approach and path of Chassidus is: These matters have already been explained in many places. Furthermore, and most importantly, in these generations, the study of this Torah is a necessity; moreover, the lack of such study, Heaven forbid, delays the Geulah. This is according to the words of the Alter Rebbe on this, and the words of the Gra on this **as well**, and it is founded upon the statement of Moshe Rabbeinu, the *Ra'aya Mehemna*. These matters are written in the Zohar and Tikkunei Zohar, and the matter is understood.

3) Regarding caution in one’s personal conduct: You should turn to a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah*, and he will instruct you on what is forbidden and what is permitted. Regarding the category of the permitted that is nonetheless repulsive—even though it is technically permitted [for in truth, even this is forbidden by the Torah, as brought in the commentary of the Ramban on the Torah, beginning of Parshas Kedoshim, that there can be a "scoundrel with the permission of the Torah." This is especially true according to those who count the mitzvos, for "sanctify yourself in that which is permitted to you" is a commandment from the Torah].

In general, refrain from searching for difficulties, refutations, and questions. Anyone who walks straight on the straight path—which is the path of the Torah, and not for the sake of contention, Heaven forbid—will succeed in the study of Torah, the fulfillment of mitzvos, and in his affairs in general. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**And the words of the Gra:** See also above, Vol. 16, Letter 5,785, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7520

7520

B”H, 27 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding the rationale for moving to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, to settle there yourself, or at the very least for your wife, may she live and be well—[and I believe we also spoke about what follows during our meeting, which is that] the current situation in the United States, and especially among the youth and young adults, is that there is a palpable awakening toward matters of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos. However, there is a lack of guides—those who will awaken and encourage them in this, and show them the way. From this, it is understood, and it is also simple, that anyone whom Divine Providence has graced with the talents to act in the aforementioned direction has a most holy obligation and a privilege to work in this with the necessary vigor. You have already seen your success in this area in practice, and you will surely succeed in your work in this regard in the future as well, especially when you do so with added strength compared to your past efforts, and without fearing at all that this falls under the category of "you have grasped too much" [which, to my regret, is an unjustified fear that prevents and hinders one from acting and doing].

From what is written, my perspective is understood: not only is the rationale for your relocation to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, negated regarding yourself, but even regarding your wife, may she live and be well, it is neither advisable nor appropriate at all. This is not only because it would certainly interfere with your work in the aforementioned area, but also because it would prevent your wife’s influence in the place where her reach extends. The instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, is that "the poor of your city come first"—meaning, the dissemination of traditional Yiddishkeit in your own city [even though, naturally, there is also the possibility to act in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established]. Furthermore, to add what is essential: my perspective on the aforementioned—that both of you should continue your activities specifically here—is founded and based upon the outlook and instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in similar cases, even those where the activity was less important than your own.

On this occasion—and everything is by Divine Providence—I must awaken you, and I am sure you will forgive me for this. It follows from the above that my hope is strong that **you will increase** your demands to strengthen conduct in yiras shamayim among the Jewish youth, and to add to this. As I witnessed in my meeting with the directors of various branches and the center as well, now is the opportune time to awaken them in this regard, and not only will the words be accepted, but they will even thank and praise you for awakening them to this.

With respect and blessings for good tidings and a happy Chanukah.

## 7,521

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write about becoming acquainted with the Torah of Chassidus Chabad, and—no less importantly—its guidance and conduct as applied to daily life, in accordance with the ruling of the Mishnah that "the deed is the essential thing."

It would be appropriate to first familiarize yourself with the content of the *Likutei Diburim*—collected *sichos* from various occasions—of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from which one can gain an understanding regarding Chassidus and the life of a Chossid according to the Torah and guidance of Chassidus.

And since reading in *sefarim* is not the same as speaking in person (as the Alter Rebbe expresses in his introduction to *Tanya*), it would be good for you to become more closely acquainted with the Lubavitcher young men in Boston and speak with them. Surely you know some of them, and through them you can also become acquainted with the others.

May it be Hashem’s will that you fulfill your good resolution about which you write in your letter, and do so—just as with all matters of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and *mitzvos*—with joy and a glad heart. This also serves as a channel and vessel for the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in all that you and your family are in need of.

With blessings for good tidings, also regarding that which we spoke about in our conversation, and a happy Chanukah.

## 7,522

7,522

*[Days of Chanukah, 5721]*

The words of the Mitteler Rebbe are well-known regarding the advantage that business people have over those who sit in the "tent" [of Torah study] concerning the tangible perception of Elokus (Hashgacha Pratis).

And if in those generations not all of those who sat in the "tent" perceived Hashgacha Pratis so tangibly, in this generation of ours—the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, the final generation before the redemption, where the darkness is doubled and redoubled, and yet simultaneously the generation in which the springs have been revealed—

The springs of Chassidus, the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, the teachings of Chassidus in general, and subsequently the teachings of Chabad Chassidus,

And in the language of the Zohar, that "the gates of wisdom above and the springs of wisdom below were opened... [until] close to the days of Moshiach, even the children of the world are destined to find the hidden secrets of wisdom"—

In this generation, even those who sit in the "tent" have seen Hashgacha Pratis with their own physical eyes.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that from here on, they will discern and also see Hashgacha Pratis only in matters of revealed and manifest good. And through this—as is understood and is also simple—there will be success in matters of Torah and mitzvos, permeated and illuminated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, both regarding oneself and regarding one’s fellow Bnei Yisrael.

#### ***7,522***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 10, p. 219. The letter was written to several individuals between 9 Kislev and 16 Teves.

**The words of the Mitteler Rebbe are well-known:** See Kuntres Toras HaChassidus at the end.

**And in the language of the Zohar:** Parshas Vayeira, 117a–118a.

## 7523

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter from the eve of Chanukah was received. I will begin by acknowledging the first part of your letter, thanking you for your impressions of the farbrengen on the day of the tidings, the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, in Kfar Chabad—which was founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Your writing about this caused me satisfaction and *nachas ruach*. It is my hope and prayer that the impression of the farbrengen will be consistent with the purpose of the farbrengen—namely, that it will have an effect regarding matters of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and its *mitzvos*, extending into the daily life throughout the days of the year.

Regarding what you wrote about the differences of opinion among the doctors concerning your wife, may she live, and the appropriate treatment:

It is known that in a place of doubt regarding any surgery, "sit and do nothing" is preferable. May the Healer of all flesh, who performs wonders, heal and strengthen her in the appropriate manner and fulfill the requests of your hearts for the good.

Regarding what you wrote about a new apartment—in general, it is understood that the matter is appropriate and correct, for the customs and sayings of Yisrael are Torah: "Change your place, change your luck—for the good and for a blessing." This is especially true as it is based on explicit statements of our Sages to this effect. However, this applies only if your wife, may she live, agrees to move to this apartment of her own free will, without any pressure. In that case, the matter is good, but you should not pressure her; rather, explain the above once or twice, etc.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you and all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding the above, as well as, of course and simply, regarding your activities for the strengthening and dissemination of Yiddishkeit, and also regarding the internal matter of *hafotzas hamaayanos* until they reach the outside.

With blessings for good tidings and a happy Chanukah.
