## 7524

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Monday, in which you outline what you have been through and your current standing and situation.

It gave me particular pleasure to read in your letter that you are not at all satisfied with your achievements thus far in Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos, but rather hope to ascend and increase in holiness. For a good desire in such matters will surely strive to bring itself into actual practice, and regarding this bringing into practice, our Sages have taught us that when it comes in the manner of *yegiah* (toil), then there is the promise: "You have toiled and you have found."

May it be the will that you do as stated and succeed even more than you anticipate. It is surely superfluous to emphasize that among the primary mitzvos is "Love your fellow as yourself," which is a great principle in the Torah. My intention is that you should strive to influence your friends and your environment in general, so that they, too, will stand and act in the aforementioned direction of ascending in holiness. Regarding you, them, and all the above, the saying of the wise is known: "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

Regarding your writing that you study only a little Chassidus: this is surprising, for we see tangibly that the warmth and vitality of Chassidus add to one’s persistence and diligence in the study of the *nigleh* (the revealed Torah) and in the meticulous performance of mitzvos. As mentioned above, there is nothing that can stand before the will. Especially since you surely meet from time to time with those who study and have studied this part of Torah, and you can speak with them about that which is difficult or about something new in this area.

Regarding your writing about a young woman who appears to you to be modest, and the thought has arisen in your mind about marrying her, and you ask how to conduct yourself and how to speak with her regarding the good ways of the daughters of Israel:

Concerning the conduct—which I assume refers to the *shidduch*—you should act in this matter according to the custom of the Bnei Yisrael and the *bochurim* in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), who are G-d-fearing and fulfill the mitzvos properly. It seems to me that in such matters, this is done through an intermediary and not directly. Even with sound logic, this is the correct approach, since in such a way it is possible for the young man and the young woman to express their wishes without infringing upon anyone’s honor, etc., and the rest is understood.

Regarding the "good ways," etc.—this, too, should be done through the intermediary. It is certain that it is appropriate for the intermediary to speak in ways of pleasantness and agreeableness. However, there is also room to explain more during their meetings, although, naturally, not immediately at the beginning of their meetings.

As for your concern that perhaps because of your request they might consider you an extremist—actually, in recent times, a spirit of purity and *yirah* has been awakened in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) among the youth to return to the custom of their fathers, for it is Torah.

When you write your mother’s name as well (as it is customary to mention it in prayer), I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be the will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for a happy Chanukah.

7525

B"H, Days of Chanukah, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 22nd of Kislev, along with the enclosure.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news regarding yourself and all your affairs. We are currently in the days of Chanukah, having just come from the day of tidings and *segulah*, the 19th of Kislev—the Rosh Hashanah of *Chassidus* and the ways of *Chassidus*.

Regarding this: the proximity in time surely points to a proximity in substance.

One may suggest (at the very least, as a possibility), by prefacing the well-known difficulty brought in many places: seemingly, according to *halacha*, since *tumah dechuya b’tzibur* (ritual impurity is set aside in the context of the community), it would have been permissible to kindle the *Menorah* in the *Beis Hamikdash* even with oil that had become impure.

One of the explanations for this is to demonstrate the affection Hashem has for *Yisrael* and for their *avodah* in the Sanctuary. For the sake of *hiddur* (beautifying) the *avodah* to its ultimate degree—even though the *avodah* would be valid even without this *hiddur*—Hashem performed a miracle and suspended the laws of nature, and they kindled the oil from the cruse for eight days.

Based on this, it is also explained why the miracle of Chanukah occurred specifically with the oil of the *Menorah* and not with another matter of the *Beis Hamikdash*. Even if one were to say that it had to be oil, there was also oil available for the *menachos* (meal offerings).

According to the above, it is also understood that since the miracle was to demonstrate the affection Hashem has for *Yisrael*, it happened specifically with the *Menorah*, for its entire purpose is to be a testimony that the *Shechinah* rests among *Yisrael* (*Shabbos* 22b).

From this miracle, a mandatory *mitzvah* was established for every individual and for all generations: to kindle the Chanukah lights. As the *Midrash* explains—and as is clarified in the *Ramban* at the beginning of *Parshas Beha'aloscha*—these lights shall never be nullified.

(Incidentally, it should be noted that based on this, we can also explain why the *mitzvah* of the Chanukah light is unique among all *mitzvos* in that it includes the levels of *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*.)

The reason is that when the Chashmonaim kindled the lights in the *Beis Hamikdash* at that time, the requirement to beautify the *mitzvah* certainly applied to them—and from that, the definition of *mehadrin min hamehadrin* was drawn down into the *mitzvah* of Chanukah.

The same applies to the "oil of the Torah"—the part of the "secrets of secrets" within it, which was revealed specifically in the final generations. As is explained in many places, including the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe, *Siman* 26, that specifically in these final generations it is permitted and a *mitzvah* to reveal this wisdom, etc. Some ask regarding this: either way, if the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (the oil of the Torah) is essential, then it should have been a mandatory study in the earlier generations just as it is in these generations. Therefore, one must conclude that it is only for the *bnei aliyah* and their peers, as the language of the *Iggeres HaKodesh* there suggests.

According to the above, this too is understood: that the matter of *hiddur* and *bnei aliyah* (which indicates the affection Hashem has for *Yisrael*, as in the Alter Rebbe’s parable of how the King gives the precious stone upon which the entire importance of his crown depends to his only son, etc.)—after the giving, it becomes a mandatory, fixed, and essential matter (as is also understood from the parable, that now, the salvation of the only son of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He—who, as it were, has no King without a people—depends upon this).

Based on the aforementioned logic, another matter is understood, as well as the answer to the difficulty regarding *Chabad Chassidus* in particular: If one were to say that study through *havanah* and *hasbarah* (understanding and explanation) is essential, why did not all the students of the Baal Shem Tov and the Maggid hold to this path? As is known, there are differences in this, for "every river has its own course"—yet even here, there is an example of the aforementioned: there are *mehadrin* and there are *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, and this is well understood.

From this, there is a further example and instruction: just as the practice of *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min hamehadrin* were both present several generations ago, but after that, in the words of the *Rema*, the simple custom became that of *mehadrin min hamehadrin*—so too regarding the study of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov and his students. If in earlier generations, as mentioned, "every river had its own course" and both were *Chassidus*, now that we have seen with our own eyes the absolute necessity of study specifically through *havanah* and *hasbarah*—as is prevalent now regarding the *nigleh* (revealed) part of Torah—the custom must become simple, widespread, and ever-increasing, that everyone should study *Pnimiyus HaTorah* in this manner as well.

With blessings for a happy Chanukah,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your writing about the time of the creation of the souls—it is surprising that you bring this from afar. You should have asked from the explicit verse, "And He breathed into his nostrils" (on the sixth day), regarding the Sages' statement that they preceded the world, and the Sages' statement that "the spirit of G-d hovered," which refers to the spirit of *Moshiach*, and the like. Similarly, regarding the Sages' statement that they are "hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory" (*Beriah*), regarding what is explained that it is "pure"—meaning in *Atzilus* (before the creation of time entirely). And even more so in many places in *Chassidus*—that they are rooted in the *Atzmus* (Essence), etc. The answer to all the above is understood according to what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 2.

Regarding your writing about the attribute of *Chesed* (kindness), which is also for one who is not worthy, and the contradictions to this from various places—there are several levels of "not worthy": whether one is not worthy according to the attribute of *Gevurah*, or also according to the attribute of *Rachamim* (mercy), or even according to the attribute of *Chesed* that is born of intellect (*Chesed* of *Tikkun*). As the examples are brought in many places, according to the context: "Twenty-six generations were sustained by His *Chesed*," etc. (on one hand, they were **provokers**, and on the other, there was **abundant** goodness); "If Yishmael lives," *Chesed* to the Arabs, and "Say 'Bless the One from Whose [food] you have eaten'," etc.

## 7526

7526

B"H, days of Chanukah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, prominent, and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Dober 
May he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure for me to learn of the generous contribution of his pure heart, and that of his colleagues—a group dedicated to purity—to awaken the hearts of the Children of Israel.

[This is based on the fact] that each person, at the beginning of their day, upon awakening from their sleep, says and blesses, "My G-d [Who is pure, and Whose dwelling is pure, and Whose servants are pure], the soul You have placed within me is pure."

[You have emphasized] the great importance of immersion and the purity of the body—a vessel of holiness and the property of the Ribono shel Olam—[a concept] established by the early and later authorities by whose words we live.

And this is not merely immersion from impurity to purity in the literal sense, but also immersion from purity to a higher level of purity, for there are many levels and ascents in this, similar to the five degrees enumerated by the Sages regarding one who immerses for *chullin* [and is then] impure for *maaser*, and so on.

As the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, indicate: the time of immersion for purity is not the same in all instances—the weekdays in general, the days of Torah reading on Mondays and Thursdays, fast days, Erev Shabbos and Yomim Tovim, Erev Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, and Shabbos and Yomim Tovim themselves.

And it is understood that there are many ascents in this [concept] also from the Rambam, whose every word is of the utmost precision. At the conclusion and seal of the tenth book, which is *Sefer Taharah*, he explains that immersion and entering into water alludes to bringing one's soul into the waters of *Da'as*. 

And as the Mishnah states at the end of *Maseches Yoma*: "Just as a *mikveh* purifies the impure, so too does the Ribono shel Olam purify Israel."

See also the *maamarim* of Rabbeinu HaZaken (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) regarding the concept of the *mikveh* and the *kavanah* of the *mikveh*. Study them well.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that all those who strive to increase purity among Israel succeed, for it is promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted." And purity leads to *kedushah*, *chassidus*, etc.

—until the fulfillment of the promise, "And I will sprinkle pure water upon you and you shall be purified... I will purify you," and "the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea." 

With blessings for success in the aforementioned.

***

 Rabbi Dober: Teitelbaum.
 That the time is not the same: *Sichas* *Chag HaPesach* 5703, section 61.
 That his every word: *Klalim* of the Rambam (see *Yad Malachi* and elsewhere).
 *Maamarim* of Rabbeinu HaZaken: Printed in his *Siddur*.
 And the earth shall be full: See Rambam, end of *Hilchos Melachim*. Note that in *Hilchos Teshuvah* the end of the verse, "as the waters cover the sea," is not cited, whereas it is in *Hilchos Melachim* at the end of his work. See Radbaz there.

## 7528

7528

*[Kislev 5721]*

In our times, **many** of those who have chosen life, the path of our Torah, the Torah of Life, face confusion and obstacles from family members who want them to turn back from this choice.

The most appropriate path, and the one most conducive to peace, is: 1) To not enter into any debate or argument at all, and to avoid conflict regarding this. Write only about family matters and the like—[after having stated once that you have **definitely** chosen the path of Torah. And this has already been stated]. 2) Do not be unsettled by the disparagement and the like in their letters (as, mentioned above, many others in your situation receive such letters). Especially since you know that this is done in the hope that perhaps, through this, they will force you to deviate from the path of Torah and mitzvos. 3) Study with consistency and diligence. Your success in this will be the best answer to the arguments they write to you. And eventually, this will be accepted even by those who are arguing.

Regarding Pesach—consider this when the time approaches.

Regarding the beard and peyos—determine the style of if and how to inform them after you receive responses to all your letters and have replied to them, etc.

Written on the margin of a letter dated 25 Kislev 5721.

## 7529

B"H, 2 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Shalom Yehuda Leib, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following a pause, I received your letter of 26 Kislev, in which you inform me—albeit very briefly—of the delivery of the *pidyon nefesh*, etc. While the surprise is understandable—that in a place where one is instructed to detail matters for several reasons, you have been so brief—nevertheless, may it be the will [of Hashem] that these matters achieve the hoped-for results. As we spoke here, and in accordance with the ruling of the Mishnah, "the deed is the essential thing": an increase in the hours of learning *Torah Nigleh* and *Chassidus* (since speech is considered a minor deed, at the very least), and an increase in the beauty and care (*hiddur*) with which you perform *mitzvos maasiyos*.

At a time of favor (*eis ratzon*), please mention all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding your question as to when to perform the haircut (*upsherin*) for your son, Levi Yitzchak, may he live: although it is clear to me that one should not do it before he reaches three years of age, regarding the matter of waiting three days—as in your specific case, where his birthday is 13 Nissan—if you wait those three days, it will naturally be postponed, and you would perform it at the *tziyun* of Rashbi. You should consult with the *rabbanei anash* in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, regarding this.

Regarding what you wrote about a raffle for a trip here, you are surely asking this on behalf of several other *anash* as well.

This was a matter of *hargashah* (feeling/intuition) from the outset, and it remains so now. In such matters, there is no place for me to offer an opinion.

With blessings for good tidings in both general and personal matters alike.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,700

[2 Teves, 5721]

...And since we are currently in the days of Chanukah, and we recite *Al HaNissim*, etc., and all matters of our Torah and mitzvos are eternal and relevant to every member of Bnei Yisrael in every generation—may it be the will of Hashem that He be a helper to each and every one. Consequently, there will be the "delivery of the mighty into the hands of the weak, and the many into the hands of the few, and the impure into the hands of the pure, and the wicked into the hands of the righteous"—specifically, into the hands of the one who is *oske b'Torah* (engaged in Torah) within each and every one of us. 

That "mighty one" mentioned above (which is the *yetzer hara*, who is mighty due to his "preceding" us, etc.) shall be delivered—as the precision of the language implies, **"delivered"**—in such a way that there will be "abundant produce by the strength of the ox," serving Hashem "with all your heart," with both of your inclinations. May there be an increase in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and in the dissemination of the *maayanos* (the wellsprings of Chassidus) in particular, until we reach the point of "and you shall spread forth," etc., and the King Moshiach comes, and "they purified Your Sanctuary, and they gave thanks and praised Your great Name."

#### ***7,700***

## 7131

B"H, 4 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a pause, your letter of 26 Kislev, the second night of Chanukah, was received.

It is understandable that there is wonder and astonishment at your writing as if there is no way to rectify the situation, etc., for this is the opposite of the foundation of our faith and our Torah—Torah of life—which teaches that there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah. The verse explicitly states, "No one cast away shall be cast away from Him" (Shmuel II 14:14), and these words apply even if a clear sin has been committed, and even if it was done intentionally, Heaven forbid, etc. This is certainly the case regarding the matter you write about, which does not fall into that category at all, Heaven forbid.

Furthermore, and this is the main point: it is obvious that the rectification for an undesirable matter is through something desirable, good, and holy. One must not, Heaven forbid, add another undesirable matter. Feelings of sadness, and certainly feelings of despair, are things that are absolutely negated in the seforim that discuss the avodah of Hashem Yisbarach, and especially in the holy Tanya. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter.

Regarding practical action, you should endeavor to explain the laws and statutes of Taharas HaMishpacha in your surroundings, among your acquaintances and friends—both through speech and by distributing printed material and the like. This should, of course, be done in a pleasant manner, albeit with appropriate energy. Likewise, you should engrave in your mind and heart the concept of bitachon and the hashgacha of the Ribono shel Olam, who oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis, and who is the essence of good, whose nature is to do good.

Above all, you must know that a Jewish man and woman must be in a state of joy and goodness of heart. This is also proven by the fact that we are commanded at the **beginning** of every single day to thank and bless Hashem, Creator of the world and Fashioner of man, as in the text of "Modeh Ani," etc., and all the morning blessings that follow.

As is known, the story of the holy Tzaddik, the holy Gaon, the holy Chassid, etc., Rabbi Levi Yitzchak of Berditchev, who was found in the morning dancing and rejoicing while reciting the blessing, "Who has not made me a gentile," etc. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

Regarding the content of the letter, it is sent without delay.

With blessings for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 7,332

[5 Teves, 5721]

I acknowledge receipt of your letter and the enclosed.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

I hope it is surely unnecessary to explain that every Jew—man or woman, young or old—must be strong in *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach, who watches over everyone with *hashgacha pratis*, over every detail of their life, and especially in matters of health. This should provide strength and courage, to be certain that in the end, everything will be for the good.

And since Hashem Yisbarach desires that one should do everything that depends on oneself in a natural way, one must therefore seek the opinion of a medical specialist—in your case, a neurologist and a specialist in moods—and follow their instructions. Hashem Yisbarach will grant His blessing for success, and special success at that; the stronger one is in *bitachon*, the more one sees the blessing.

It would be appropriate to have the *mezuzos* in your home checked to ensure they are *kosher* according to the *din*, as well as the *tefillin* of your husband, *shichyeh*. Also, every weekday morning, before putting on *tefillin*, give a few *prutos* (a small amount) to *tzedakah*. You should do the same each time before lighting candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*, as is the good custom of Jewish daughters.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned above.

#### ***7,332***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 11, p. 296, and Vol. 21, p. 466.

## 7333

B”H, 6 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the sixth night of Chanukah.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukullehah*, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

2) The surprise and wonder expressed in your letter is understandable. According to the established schedule, you were supposed to speak as part of your work every two weeks, yet you requested and were granted an exemption, reducing it to once a month. The reasons for my surprise are clear, especially in our current era, where the emphasis is on *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*—spreading the wellsprings outward—particularly to people of the type mentioned. As you yourself wrote, this is a unique and special opportunity. According to the demands of the hour, one must seek out and create such opportunities; when Divine Providence arranges one for you and places it ready in your hands, to view it as a burden or a struggle is, in truth, an act of supreme *chesed*, even if it is perceived as such in a tangible, physical way.

It is understood that this is not intended as a moral rebuke *at all*, but rather regarding the future. May it be Hashem’s will that He be with your mouth and guide the listeners to the straight path—the path of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and *mitzvos*, illuminated by the light and vitality of Chassidus. May you do this with true joy and *harchavas hada’as*, as it is written, "And I will walk in a broad place," which also adds to the success of these matters.

3) Although it is naturally regrettable that you missed the full measure of the *farbrengen* on the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the *Rosh Hashanah* for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, it is nevertheless known that there is nothing in the world that does not contain a mixture of good and evil. Thus, "out of the strong came forth sweetness"—that you finally recognized how your participation is required, and through this, your self-confidence will increase. That is to say, confidence in the fact that the *shlichus* of our Rebbes is successful, provided one is willing to act upon it. As is known, the ruling of the Heavenly Court is that because of the *mesiras nefesh* of the Alter Rebbe for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those connected to him and those who follow in his footsteps shall be on top (printed in *Sefer Kitzurim Ve’he’aros Le’Tanya*, end of page 122). Here, too, the intention is not to dwell on the past, but regarding the future.

4) Regarding your writing about establishing a Chabad foundation in your location now—it seems the place is not yet prepared for this, and your description of the location and the individuals involved confirms this. If so, there is room to say that establishing the aforementioned foundation before the time is right would have an undesirable effect on the Chabad activities that have already been established there, including *hafatzas hamaayanos*.

5) Regarding a Chabad *shul*—it must be clarified whether it is connected to controversy or the like. In a case of doubt, the rule is "sit and do nothing" (*shev v’al taaseh*) is preferable. Especially since it is logical to argue that when there is no dedicated Chabad *shul*, one should pursue Chabad-related matters in every *shul*, whereas if there is a dedicated building, others might say that these matters are restricted to that specific building. Furthermore, it requires consideration whether it is worthwhile to divide the community into separate locations.

#### 7333

Printed in *Sefer HaShlichus*, p. 175 and p. 180.

## 7334

B"H, 7 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Moshe, may he live.

Shalom and Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the third night of Chanukah.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

As is explained in many places, the channel and vessel for the activity and awakening of the *ratzon* (will) of the one at the resting place is to walk in his ways and follow his conduct. Therefore, my hope is strong that in addition to the fixed times you have for studying the teachings of Chassidus, you will surely continue to increase this from time to time, as per the directive to "ascend in matters of holiness." This will increase the awakening of *ratzon*, and you will share good news regarding yourself and your family, may they live, for there is nothing that can stand before *ratzon*. May it be His will that you also exert influence in this direction upon your surroundings, friends, and acquaintances.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

Regarding your questions:

a) The source for the statement of our Sages cited in the *Hosafos* to *Torah Or*, end of *Parshas Ki Sisa*, regarding the difficulty they had in permitting the speaking of *divrei Torah* on Shabbos—I have already noted, as you wrote, that it is also cited at the end of *Sefer HaYirah* by Rabbeinu Yonah. It is well known that many statements of our Sages (especially from the Yerushalmi) were before the *Rishonim* but are not found in the texts available to us. See also *Yerushalmi Shabbos*, Chapter 15, beginning of Halacha 3 (the source was noted here by the Gaon of Rogatchov in *Responsa Tzafnas Paneach*, Vol. 2, Section 6). *Zohar* Vol. 3, 94, bottom of the page. It should not be interpreted as referring to studying *divrei Torah*, because in all the aforementioned sources, the **emphasis** is on speaking with the mouth.

b) *Birchas HaGomel* for women—The *Acharonim* have already written at length on this, as you noted in your letter. See *Ketzos HaShulchan* by Rabbi Naeh, beginning of Section 60. It is worth noting the most unusual custom of the Sephardim in London, where she recites it separately (cited in *Sefer Kesser Shem Tov* by Rabbi Gagin).

c) Regarding the phrase "with the threefold blessing in the Torah"—the *beis* in the word *baTorah* proves that the meaning is that the triplication is within the Torah. See *Kesser Shem Tov* regarding your notes on this.

7334
Partially printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 484; partially in Vol. 22, p. 239; completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

**R' Moshe:** Halberstam, Jerusalem.

**Source for the statement of our Sages:** See also above, Vol. 1, Letter 99.

## 7,135

B"H, 8 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I confirm receipt of your letter from Sunday, as well as the previous one. Thank you for the good news regarding the success of the medical treatment. May it be Hashem’s will that you soon return to full strength and bring good news yourself.

Regarding what you wrote about the institution and the thought of handing it over to a certain organization, etc.:

It is understood and simple that for every head of an institution, one must clarify the authority of the recipient regarding the primary objective—namely, education on the foundation of holiness. For ultimately, this is the main point: that those being educated will grow up on the foundations of our Torah and mitzvos. Even though, on the face of it, there is no way to set a fixed limit, in such a case, it must be ensured that the education will not be reduced or diminished from what it has been until now. I do not know if there is room to guarantee this in the contract of transfer or sale, but we see clearly that in matters of spirit and outlook, even things that are signed upon only have endurance if they align with the spirit of the signer, for the gates of excuses are never locked.

If the aforementioned condition is in order as it should be, then it is worth considering once again whether the matter is advisable.

It would be best for this consideration to take place after the prospects for the budget for the coming school year are clearly known. I refer to assistance from various offices and organizations, etc., which will surely discuss budgets in the coming weeks, and consequently, clarity will be reached on the aforementioned matter as well.

In accordance with these two points, you and your wife, *tichye*, should decide on the matter. May it be the will of Hashem, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, that everything will be for the good in all details, both for the affairs of the institution and for yourselves.

So much for the practical side.

Now, I have the duty—and perhaps it is also a privilege—to explain my opinion on the points contained in your letter as an explanation for the aforementioned thought, and their inner meaning: that you have invested much toil, energy, time, and health, etc., into the institution, and when you see the current state of the institution, it does not encourage you to continue, etc.

The wonder and astonishment at the phrasing of the matter as above is understandable. For the purpose of the institution is the education of the sons and daughters of Israel. When one takes a total and wants to reach a conclusion as to whether all the energy and toil, etc., were worthwhile, one must first examine the fruits of the education—that is, how many *bochurim* and *avreichim* put on *tefillin*, daven, etc., thanks to the education they received, and likewise regarding the young women. Since a significant number of them have certainly already married and built, or are building, homes in Israel, one should clarify the establishment of their homes on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, and estimate what would have been had they not been educated in your institution. It is surely easy to estimate this, at least to some extent, through statistics regarding students of other institutions. If our Sages ruled that saving one soul of Israel is as if one has sustained an entire world, how much more so when we are speaking of tens of souls, and perhaps even more—as mentioned, dozens of homes in Israel whose state in Torah and mitzvos affects them for their generations and the generations of their generations until the end of all time.

All of the above is according to what is explained in the *Shulchan Aruch* alone, and if you will, also in *Sifrei Mussar*.

Especially if we contemplate the illumination of the matter according to the teachings of Chassidus, the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and our *Alter Rebbe*, etc., and their foundations. I will mention here only two: 1) The saying of the Baal Shem Tov, that a *neshamah* descends below to be clothed in a body for seventy or eighty years, just to do one favor for a fellow Jew, in material or spiritual matters. 2) The saying of our *Alter Rebbe*, that the performance of any *mitzvah* whatsoever is a *yichud* above that is **eternal forever** (*Tanya*, Chapter 25). That is to say, if you find in any place a single *bochur* or young woman who recites blessings, reads *Krias Shema Yisrael*, etc., then for this alone, the descent of all those *neshamos* who brought him to this—from the highest peak to the deepest valley for seventy or eighty years—is worthwhile. Furthermore, they have caused thereby a matter above that is eternal forever and ever.

Even if we were to assume that you and your wife, *tichye*, are for some reason not in a state of *marah levana*, I am certain that even by your own estimation, hundreds of souls of Israel have been saved by you from total assimilation, *r'l*, to a lifestyle according to Torah and mitzvos—at the very least from time to time—and tens of thousands of actions as mentioned are performed thanks to your efforts and toil. Since both of you are believers, children of believers, is it believable that you have any doubt as to whether the toil and effort were worthwhile? And if the conclusion is that they were certainly, definitely worthwhile, then you must immediately change your perspective on your work in the institution, and be in a state of immense joy and true goodness of heart for having merited and succeeded in work in this field. With (even slight) contemplation of the above, the argument that in matters of livelihood, now both of you must toil and exert yourselves, etc., while in other fields of livelihood only one person labors—this discussion has no place at all. For the matter of your livelihood is spiritual; it is "set upon the earth, and its top reaches the heavens" (and precisely as the term *shomayma* implies—above the heavens, and *mutzav artza*—that it is below the earth, meaning from the lowest of the low to the highest of the high). If your wife, *tichye*, has merited to have all these actions as her own, in addition to her share in her husband’s actions, there is no portion more beautiful than this.

It is possible to elaborate on all of the above at length, but for you, I have only come to present the points. If you contemplate the truth of the situation, there is no need for a lengthy letter across the ocean; on the contrary, being on the spot, you can add much more.

It is understood that the most immediate answer does not escape me—that one should engage in matters of Torah and mitzvos and their dissemination without the difficulties you encountered in the aforementioned institution. But [in addition to the main point, that such a matter does not happen every day, and as you yourself wrote, it is beyond nature that this is the only institution of this type found among private individuals], every *neshamah* has its task and ability, and it is not always in a person’s power to switch from one task to another [even though it is always in his power to fulfill the task or not, etc.—for everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven, and permission is given, and the choice is free for the children of Israel, etc.].

And from here to another point that you write and which appears between the lines: the thought that the state of health that necessitated surgery and medical treatment came, as it were, from the toil and exertion in the institution, etc. Even though we do not know the ways of Heaven, since the verse explicitly states, "If you walk in My statutes," and Rashi explains that you should be **toiling** in Torah, "then I will give," etc., as all the blessings listed in the *parsha*, it is more likely to say the opposite: that the success of the medical treatment and the fact that you will return to full strength, etc., should be credited **to** the toil and effort in the institution and its affairs. And if, as it seems from your letter, you are certain that your setting aside money for *tzedakah* institutions certainly has a connection to the success of the treatment, then to the extent that the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah* with money is great, it is not comparable to *tzedakah* with body and *neshamah*, when one invests the powers of the *neshamah* and the powers of the body in *tzedakah*—I refer to the matters of which it is said, "And *tzedakah* exalts a nation."

I believe I have already written in my previous letter that, in general, it is not my way to preach morality or to complain about the past, but only regarding the future. In this case as well, my intention is only to show the total of your work in the institution as I see it (which, in my opinion, is clearly the case), which consequently should lead to, as mentioned, true joy and goodness of heart, etc., etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He—which is measure for measure, only many times over—you will derive true *nachas* from all your children, *shichyu*, which is Jewish, Chassidic *nachas*, and likewise *nachas* as mentioned from the students, *shichyu*, whom you brought to the life of the World to Come. In our generation, this also applies to the life of this world, for without this, *ch'v*, one deteriorates even regarding physical life, etc.

I hope to hear good news regarding all that has been said, and may it be with health, joy, and goodness of heart.

With blessings.

## 7,336

*[The tenth of Teves will soon be transformed into joy and gladness, 5721]*

...This reminds me of a saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—who related that when he began dealing with business matters, he requested—in the form of a *pidyon nefesh*—from his father, the Rebbe, that "he should not have the *ba'alei-batische* (layman-like) perceptions." He added in his story to me that these *ba'alei-batische* perceptions are, of course, subtle, for the matter concerns *ba'alei-batim* who are observers of Torah and *mitzvos* **in their entirety.** It is just that, as *Chassidus* explains, they are found in *Mitzrayim* (Egypt)—in limitations and boundaries—throughout their entire lives. For throughout their entire lives, today is like yesterday, and tomorrow is like today, and even the tomorrow that comes after a long time. Furthermore, the very aspiration for change is, in their eyes, the hallmark of a madman—that is to say, outside the framework of "healthy" logic.

And how illuminating are the words of our *Alter Rebbe* in his *Tanya*, where, regarding the language of the *Mishnah* that "in every generation a person is obligated to see himself as if he went out of *Mitzrayim*," our *Alter Rebbe* added the words, "and in every single day."

#### ***7,336***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 12, p. 166.

## 7,737

B"H, 13 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the farbrengen in connection with the Day of Besorah and the Day of Redemption—our redemption and the salvation of our souls—19 Kislev, 5721, who are taking part in the completion of the Shas in Rishon LeTzion, in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

For the words of the tzaddikim stand forever and accomplish their effect—in all the matters mentioned in the aforementioned Iggeres HaKodesh.

And surely, for you, it is superfluous to emphasize the connection between the matters mentioned there, in the words of the Rebbe, and that each of the aforementioned learners should complete for themselves each week the *tamanya api* of Tehillim 119.

This connection is also alluded to generally in the words of our Sages regarding the verse in Tehillim, "Hashem loves the gates of Tzion more than all the dwellings of Yaakov," [which is interpreted as] "I pray where I study" (Berachos 8a).

May it be the will [of Hashem] that through the combination of these two matters—Torah and tefillah, eternal life and temporal life—the blessing of Hashem will be drawn down in matters of eternal life, and likewise for health, peace, and sustenance (as per the language of Rashi, Shabbos 10a)—for them and for their households, may they live and be well.

And just as they have begun this mitzvah, may they merit to complete it with tranquility, joy, and a good heart.

And in the words of Rabbeinu, in the aforementioned Iggeres: "Be strong and let your heart take courage, all you who wait for Hashem."

With respect and blessing.

## 7,338

B"H, 14 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yehoshafat, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following a hiatus, I received your letter of 7 Teves, in which you write the rationale for organizing a large celebration for the students of the upper grades in the area for the upcoming Purim, and the benefit of this.

In general, any such initiative is correct, but this is specifically true when one can ensure (ba’varenen) appropriate participation by the students. After all, on the days of Purim as written, there will certainly be several celebrations, and furthermore—and this is the main point—surely many of the families hold celebrations in private homes, family gatherings, etc.

Seemingly, it would be worthwhile to look into the possibility of organizing the aforementioned for the upcoming 10 Shevat. Since this year it falls on Erev Shabbos, it would be on the eve of that day—that is, the eve of the Yom HaHilula. Then, the aforementioned concerns would be removed, and there would certainly be an echo to the matter, as several schools have become accustomed to visiting Kfar Chabad in connection with that day. Recently, the activities of the Baal HaHilula in the country of Russia regarding the education of children, etc., have been publicized in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

Regarding the expenses connected to the above, you are surely aware of the state of the treasury in the Reshet. Nevertheless, if the matter is brought to fruition—and the main thing is that there be appropriate participation as mentioned above—my hope is that the treasury will contribute up to one hundred and twenty-five—125—lirot.

It is surprising that you do not mention your activities in the month of Kislev, and especially regarding the students, as you surely explained to them the narrative of the redemption and the miracles of this month (in order): 9, 10, 19, and the days of Chanukah.

With blessings for good tidings in general matters and in private matters.

***

**R' Yehoshafat:** Alpert, Jerusalem. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 15, 5,220.

## 7,339

7,339

The remedy is teshuvah: complete regret for the past, a resolution for the future, and conduct **in practice** that aligns with this.

## 7540

[14 Teves 5721]

...And based on the story we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

When the Tzemach Tzedek was a young boy and was studying the verse, "And Yaakov lived in the land of Egypt seventeen years," his teacher translated it for him—following the commentary of the Baal HaTurim—as, "Yaakov Avinu lived his seventeen best years in Egypt" (the choicest years of Yaakov’s life were these seventeen years that he lived in Egypt). When he came home from cheder, he asked his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe: "How can it be that Yaakov Avinu, the choicest of the Patriarchs, had the choicest years of his life be the seventeen years he lived in Egypt, the 'nakedness of the land'?"

The Alter Rebbe answered him: It is written, "And he sent Yehuda before him to Yosef, to prepare before him to Goshen," and it is stated in the Midrash—cited by Rashi—that Rabbi Nechemiah said, "To establish a house of study for him, so that Torah would be there and the tribes would be occupied with Torah." "To prepare before him to Goshen" (lehoros lefanav Goshnah)—when one studies Torah, one becomes closer to the Ribono shel Olam, and thus, even in Egypt, there was "vayechi" (he lived). (When one studies Torah, one approaches—becomes closer to—Hashem, and then he truly **vayechi**, even in Egypt.)

May it be Hashem’s will that for each and every one, even in his own "Egypt," his life should correspond to this explanation of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, so that it may be rightfully said of these years that in them he **vayechi**—the choicest years of his life.

And this is achieved through the study of Torah, both the revealed and Chassidus, and the greatness of Torah study that leads to action—the fulfillment of the mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "And he shall live by them," true life.

And this, too, will hasten the redemption from everything that distracts, from all boundaries and "Egypts," as it is written, "To save him from the hand of Egypt and to bring him up," etc.

## 7,501

7,501

B”H, 15 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Teves and those preceding it, in which you write regarding the problems and your current work in the field of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh* at the institution founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisroel*.

The approach to solving these problems must be that a solution is mandatory (and not as seems to be implied between the lines of your letter). This necessity is understood, as this is the "beautiful portion," as mentioned above, regarding the essence and purpose of the institution. This is especially true in light of my hope that you remember what we discussed here during the weeks you stayed here, both in public and in private with you. This is particularly relevant since, as you wrote, you hope to establish a home in *Yisroel* soon, which further adds to the need for the blessing of *Hashem* in abundance. The aforementioned *avodah* in the aforementioned institution is a channel and vessel for this, provided that it is done with *mesiras nefesh* and dedication.

Regarding the path to solving these problems, you should consult with the distinguished *Chossid*, *ish yirei elokim*, *nosei v’nosein*, *rav pe’alim*, Rabbi Chaim Sholom *sheyichyeh* Brook. It is understood that you may tell him that you are doing this at my suggestion.

In general, it appears from your letter that you feel you are in a narrow place (*meitzar*)—and you also said this to me a few times during your stay here. I am enclosing a copy of a letter I wrote to several of *anash*, which is also directed to you; in it, you will find an answer and also peace of mind.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

## 7742

B"H, 15 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Zos Chanukah, which was received in due time, I am replying immediately without waiting for my turn, because I was shaken by your writing that you expressed to a certain person your view—that one must distinguish between the government and religious matters. Even though these words can be interpreted in several ways, at least with some difficulty, the simple interpretation is a separation between religion and government offices. The reason for my being shaken is understandable and also simple, because in my opinion—and I ask for his forgiveness—this is the opposite of the formula of "I believe." Any Jew, whoever he may be—if he declares and makes it a slogan that he is separated from religion, this is the opposite of the entire essence of our holy Torah, which is, at the same time, a Torah of **life**, life in this world. And it is impossible for any Jew, whoever he may be and wherever he may be, to be separated from religion.

It is understood that I have read in the press and in letters that there are those, even among the Charedim, who strive for the aforementioned separation, with the reasoning that when those whose worldview is not Torah-based have a say in religious matters, it brings destruction, etc.

Now, even though the claim is realistic and justified, the response to this is not to add yet another sin to the transgression—to declare openly before the eyes of all the nations, and furthermore, within **many** circles in Israel, that they are separated from religion, etc. The response and the remedy is that the aforementioned [individuals] should not have any **say**. This is by way of example and *kal v'chomer* from that which concerns physicians of the body: even though there is a government ministry whose function this is, and the expenses are paid in full, etc.—nevertheless, the director of the ministry does not express any opinion regarding medical treatments and medicinal drugs. How much more so is this true regarding the healing of the soul and the health of the soul, etc. And surely, for someone like you, elaboration on what has been said is superfluous.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

It goes without saying that I was no less alarmed by the interpretation in Sanhedrin (98b) that the "new David" (as the expression in your letter goes)—that is, Melech HaMoshiach—his connection and essence is [merely] external leadership, and consequently it does not matter if he is... one of the secularists! This is the Moshiach who, in the language of the Rambam, will be "occupied with Torah and involved in mitzvos like his ancestor David, **and he will compel all** of Israel to walk in its ways"! And he is a great prophet, close to Moshe Rabbeinu (and in Tanchuma, Toldos: "and he will be exalted above Moshe").

#### 7742

**Distinguish between religion:** See also above, Letter 7715, and the references in the notes there.

## 7743

B"H, 16 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, occupied with communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Asher, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote about the timing of your travel, *b'shem Hashem tzeischem l'shalom* — I am not comfortable with those who cross the International Date Line in the middle of the days of Sefirah (unless there is an **absolute** necessity for it). For my **clear** opinion is that their fiftieth day of Sefirah — that is, their **Shavuos** — is **not** on the same days as the Shavuos of the Bnei Yisrael in the place where they have arrived, which causes confusion for those who see it, etc.

## 7444

B"H, 16 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Yaakov, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I am responding to your letter of 10 Teves—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—and as you requested, the response arrives on the day the letter was received, regarding the text for a *matzeivah*.

In general, in such matters, it is most appropriate that it be in line with the *matzeivos* in that same cemetery, in accordance with what is explained in many places—including from a halachic perspective—that the conduct regarding one who is buried in a cemetery touches upon and is relevant to all the others.

Within this same framework, it is worthwhile that those who knew the late R' B. arrange the text based on their knowledge.

Since you ask my opinion on this, I must add what I have instructed many others in similar cases: to mention in the text that he was a Chossid of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, specifying the name (of the Rebbe), and regarding the aforementioned, one should mention the years.

The basis for my suggestion in such matters is founded upon what I saw in the text of the *matzeivah* that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, arranged for his mother, the *Rabbanit* *zt"l*, where he mentioned the *tzaddikei yesodei olam*, the Admurim, by their names.

And if you would say that this is also hinted at in the *Mishnah* regarding the account of the text of the *she'eilah* (the question) until Chevron (*Tamid*, Chapter 3), [it is understood that] the entire purpose of the *matzeivah* is for the merit and the *aliyah* of the *neshamah*.

With respect and blessing for good tidings, and also regarding your health, quite simply.

***

**R' Yaakov:** Landau. Further letters to him—see above 7284, and the references in the notes there.

**Regarding the text of the matzeivah:** Of R' Boruch Duchman.

**What I have instructed:** See above, Vol. 14, 4999. Below, 7662.

## 7745

B"H, 15 Teves, 5721,
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and meticulous in his communal work, a man of character, Shear Yashuv HaKohen, may he live.

It gave me pleasure to receive your letter of 13 Teves, in addition to the news I received from Anash, may they live, and I derived satisfaction from the personal regards you conveyed; thank you for this.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matters of the Chief Rabbinate in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established:

I have already written about this to the esteemed Rabbi, the great scholar, G-d-fearing, famous for his Torah and wisdom, Rabbi Shlomo Yosef Zevin, may he live, regarding the great distress caused by the entanglement of these matters, etc., and the resulting disgrace, etc. He replied that he has already publicized my opinion on this regarding all three points that were discussed during your visit here.

Surely, it is also known to you the interpretation of Chassidus regarding Egypt and the Exodus from Egypt: that even within holiness there are "Egypts" and limitations, and the obligation to see oneself as if he personally went out of Egypt—as emphasized by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 47—applies **every single day** even regarding these "Egypts." Moreover, there is an additional dimension to this: that even before the exodus, there must be "and he lived" (*vayechi*), and furthermore, it is possible that this can be the choicest of his years and the peak of a person's activities, as is explained in the teachings of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe on this subject.

Thank you for sending the books you mentioned at the end of your letter, and surely you will continue to do so in the future.

With personal regards to your father, the Rabbi, may he live, who I am sure has already received my letter.

With respect and appreciation.

## 7546

B"H, 18 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Friday, in which you write regarding the funds raised for *tzedakah* in the camp in connection with the situation of the holy institution in the camp, with a suggestion that we should provide instructions from here on how to distribute the money.

Understandably, first and foremost, one must see how this works out according to *Shulchan Aruch*. It is a clear and explicit *din* that one does not divert funds from one *tzedakah* to another. Especially since we are dealing with *tzedakah* that was collected from others who gave it for a specific *tzedakah*, the change being made—not by the donor—is not only a matter of "one does not divert from one *tzedakah* to another," but is simply a matter of *gezel*, *r"l*.

On the other hand, since the holy institution is of the utmost importance for the city and the surrounding area, and one is making an effort and working for it with dedication, warmth, light, and *hislahavus*, it is clearly certain that there is *siyata d'shmaya* in this, so that not only should the holy institution maintain its current state, but it should also develop more and more, as per the instruction of our holy Torah: "We elevate in matters of holiness."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the example and work of the *askanim* in the aforementioned matter should add to the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, in that which they and their families *shlita* are in need of. And this is also a primary point: that this should influence many of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in your area, so that they too should act in this way, to help the holy institution to strengthen and expand it, and as stated, in a manner of "increasing and continuing, increasing and shining."

With blessings for success in your holy work.

The above-written regarding "one does not divert from one *tzedakah* to another" is, as explained in the *poskim*, regarding the **past**. However, the **heads** of those involved in this from both sides can speak together so that the funds raised **from here on** should be distributed in designated portions, in exchange for the assistance that is being provided, etc.

## 7,747

B"H, 18 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

In accordance with this week’s parsha, following the teaching of the Alter Rebbe (the teaching of our master, the Baal Shem Tov) regarding the matter of: a) "And an angel of Hashem appeared" (was revealed); b) "in a flame of fire"; c) "from the midst of the bush"—

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good tidings regarding the activities about which you write, the inner point of which is the unification of these two matters: **"a flame of fire,"** the sparks of which are the sparks of fire, the flame of Hashem (tefillah and the like—whose essence is ascent from below to above, similar to the nature of fire); and **"appeared,"** the revelation from above to below (Torah and mitzvos—whose essence, in general, is from above to below).

And may this be **"from the midst of the bush,"** this world, a narrow place (*tzarah*), to transform the narrowness (*m'tzarah*) into a window of light (*tzohar*) through the light of Torah and mitzvos.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 7,548

[20 Shevat, 5721]

In response to your letter of 13 Teves, in which you ask my opinion as to whether to distribute the funds for tzedakah or to establish a permanent endowment fund:

In general, it is more proper and better to distribute the funds, as the entire amount is then utilized in practice. This is in accordance with the instruction of Chazal that when Hashem provides an opportunity to fulfill a mitzvah, one should not postpone it for later (which, in your case, would be the result of creating an endowment fund and utilizing only the interest).

In accordance with the instruction of the aforementioned statement of Chazal, it is also understandable that you should distribute a larger portion of the funds—the larger, the better—yourself, right now. What will certainly be distributed according to your wishes is also a mitzvah that one should perform personally; one should not do so through a shaliach. Furthermore, distributing the funds yourself is a segulah for long life and good years.

It is also my duty (and privilege) to point out that it would be a very proper thing, and more than good, if a portion of the funds were given toward printing the seforim of our Rebbeim, *zatzukal-lah-ha nivgam zya*. This is an eternal zechus; every time these seforim are studied, those who made the printing of these seforim possible have a zechus and a share in that study. If the Yiddishe names are mentioned, with the addition of the parents' names, on a page at the end of the sefer (it happens that some do not wish to provide their **family** names, so as not to invite an ayin hara, chas v’shalom, or similar concerns, but this has no relevance to mentioning the names in Lashon HaKodesh, which does not specify who the person is), then the one studying the sefer mentions those names.

May Hashem Yisbarach, who oversees each and every one with Hashgacha Pratis, guide you in all of the above as is truly good—a true good—for long days and good years. May each of you act for Yiddishe matters, Torah and mitzvos, with tranquility, joy, and a good heart.

## 7449

B"H, 21 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your writing that the Bar Mitzvah boy is preparing to read the entire parsha in public:

My opinion on this has been known for some time. Unfortunately, in our generation, people have made the primary secondary and the secondary primary. This is also evident in the fact that as preparation for accepting the yoke of Torah and mitzvos, they minimize the study of the foundations and essentials—the halachos required for daily life—and replace them with matters that are, at the very least, not fundamental. Furthermore—and this is also a primary point—it was never the custom to do this. Even though Chazal said, "When you come to a city, follow its customs," every city has many different customs, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It is understood that the above is offered merely as a suggestion and a remark, for you to reconsider whether it is worthwhile. However you decide, may it be Hashem’s will that it be for the good.

#### ***7449***

In continuation of this letter—see below, 7464.

## 7550

B"H, 22 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Sunday.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter. May it be His will that you bring good news, both regarding general matters and regarding your own personal affairs.

Regarding your writing that it is as if I instructed someone to occupy themselves with the study of Kabbalah—while it is true that in our times forgetfulness is common, I am not in the habit of doing such things at all. What I do instruct is the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed through the Chassidus of the Baal Shem Tov (general Chassidus) and the teachings of our Alter Rebbe (the Chassidus of Chabad), as is well-known and publicized.

Regarding your question about amulets—I have heard nothing at all about such matters.

Naturally, I was alarmed by your writing regarding hatred, etc.—these are idle and absolutely baseless words, which stem only from a lack of order, etc., in all one’s ways, which in turn weakens the health of the body and diminishes goodness of heart and joy, etc. It is imperative that, ultimately, you organize your life in an orderly fashion (and it is known how much my father-in-law, the Rebbe, demanded this of everyone). My meaning is simple: order in eating, drinking, and sleeping, etc., all the way to order in matters of livelihood. And although it is difficult to change oneself from one extreme to the other immediately (nor is that necessary), it is essential that you resolve that this is your goal and begin immediately to improve the situation step by step. I am confident that Hashem will grant you success in this. For the practical steps, consult with your friends in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, for it is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and with tranquility, joy, and goodness of heart.

## 7551

B"H, 23 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shmuel Abba, shichyeh,

Peace and blessing!

After a pause, I received your letter of 17 Teves, in which you write about the farbrengen of the auspicious day, the day of redemption, 19 Kislev—our redemption and the liberation of our souls, the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. May it be His will that its impression be evident throughout all the days of the year, and extend into actual practice in daily life.

Regarding what you wrote about a school where both holy studies and, to distinguish, secular studies will be taught:

In general, such matters depend on the conditions of the location and the individuals involved, extending to two extremes in this regard: Under certain conditions, our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, opposed this with all their might; and under other, specific conditions, while they did not involve themselves in the founding of such schools, they assisted in the matter behind the scenes. It is understood that the latter instance was extremely rare, yet it did occur at times. Based on this, you must judge the situation on-site and make a decision.

May it be the will of Hashem—who promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted"—that you decide according to the truth of the matter and for the merit of the many.

It is my hope that you are preparing for the yom hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael. May it be His will that before then, during, and after the yom hilula, each and every one will increase in the matters for which the baal hilula sacrificed his life, and in the inner point: the dissemination of the wellsprings (until they reach) the outside.

With blessings for good tidings in communal and personal matters, and with regards to all Anash, shichyeh.

## 7502

7502

By the Grace of Hashem, 24 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Yahrtzeit of the Alter Rebbe,
Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, may the merit of his holy soul protect us.
To the participants in the annual dinner of
Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem preserve them.

Peace and Blessing!

The following *sipur-Torah* (a story that serves as a lesson) regarding the Alter Rebbe (whose yahrtzeit is today, as this letter is being written), which we heard from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, has special significance in connection with the annual dinner of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch.

When the Tzemach Tzedek was a child and was studying the verse, **"And Yaakov lived in the land of Egypt seventeen years,"** his teacher explained the verse to him as meaning that Yaakov Avinu **lived** the seventeen best years of his life in Egypt. Upon coming home, the Tzemach Tzedek asked his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe: How is it possible that Yaakov Avinu, the chosen of the Patriarchs, should have his best years counted as the years he lived in exile in Egypt, the most impure of all lands?

The Alter Rebbe answered him: It is written, **"And he sent Yehuda before him to Yosef, to direct him to Goshen."** The Midrash explains (as Rashi cites) that before Yaakov Avinu went to Egypt, he sent Yehuda ahead to establish a yeshiva there where the tribes could study Torah. When one studies Torah, one becomes closer to the Ribono shel Olam, and thus, even in Egypt, there was *Vayechi* — "and he lived."

* * *

The lesson from this is: When Jews go to settle in a place, whenever that may be and wherever that may be, the first thing must be to establish a place for the study of Torah. And not only for the older generation (Yaakov, the father), but, as mentioned above, so that the tribes—the children and the younger generation—should study Torah. And when one recognizes that this is the beginning and foundation of Jewish life and a Jewish settlement, one strengthens and expands the Torah institution, and a center for Torah is created. This ensures that *those* years will be the best years, even if, outwardly, one is in exile.

Furthermore, as stated, through this one is brought closer to the Ribono shel Olam, the Master of the world. And one receives, in increased measure, Hashem’s blessings for all needs—not only for the students themselves, but also for the supporters and *askanim* who make the study and dissemination of Torah and mitzvos possible.

* * *

The above has always been the mission of Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim throughout their long history of wandering from place to place and from country to country. The Rebbe, my father-in-law, immediately upon arriving in America, established the central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch and laid the foundation for a wide-reaching yeshiva system. The Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch has brought about a revival of Torah and Torah-life in this country. This must be continued in an increasing measure, in accordance with the growing demands of our restless times, in which it becomes ever more evident that only the light of our Torah, **Toras Chaim**, can show the way in life. And everyone who takes part in this holy mission secures for themselves the Divine blessings to make *these* times and *these* years the best and most fortunate in life, both materially and spiritually.

I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants in the dinner, to the *askanim* and the guests of honor.

Together with my request and hope that this annual dinner will generate the necessary means to strengthen and expand the work of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch to the greatest possible extent.

With respect and with a blessing for success,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7504

B"H, 28 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Mr. Binyamin Lampert
Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 10 Cheshvan and the subsequent one, in which you write regarding the initiative to organize a shipping company that would operate a vessel from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) to the United States, such that the voyage would be conducted in a manner permitted according to the Shulchan Aruch.

The magnitude of the merit in this is certainly something that, for someone like yourself, requires no elaboration, and it is understood that I am interested in this with heart and soul, as this is a matter of benefiting the many.

Regarding the suggestion that the ship be operated by a crew of non-Jews, this is a matter that is entirely impractical for several reasons, as I elaborated somewhat in my letter, a copy of which is enclosed.

In particular, according to this suggestion, it would be necessary to double the crew, and furthermore—and this is the main point—**in practice**, it would be unavoidable that several tasks and operations would be performed by Jews, and to the wise, a hint is sufficient.

Therefore, I was pleased to see that in your second letter you mention only the possibility of the ship remaining stationary on Shabbos.

Since you are knowledgeable about the operation of ships, you surely know that after a ship docks, there are still several tasks to be performed until there is a complete cessation of work. Similarly, before it departs, several preparations must be made to warm up and activate the engines, which requires a certain amount of time. From this, it is understood that the ship’s arrival must take place some time before the onset of Shabbos, and likewise, it must be established from the outset that its departure after Shabbos will be some time after Shabbos has ended.

Regarding enlisting assistance from interested parties, as far as I am aware, there is a group of Chareidi Jews who are in negotiations with shipping companies to arrange travel as well as cargo shipments in a manner that observes Shabbos. It would be worthwhile for you to get in touch with them at the address in the margin of this letter. For my part, I have also informed them of your initiative, so that if you write to them, it will not be news to them.

Considering the great value of this matter and the great necessity for it, may it be His will that you succeed in the aforementioned, and may the merit of the many assist you. May we soon see the clarification and resolution of these matters, and may we merit, very soon, the fulfillment of the prophecy that "Yisrael observe Shabbos according to its law, and immediately they are redeemed."

With respect and blessing.

#### ***7504***

**That the voyage... according to the Shulchan Aruch:** See above, Vol. 19, Letter 7040, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7505

B"H, 29 Teves, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following the longest of interruptions, your letter was received on Erev Shabbos Parshas Va'eira, in which you write regarding your settling in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), your studies, and the religious atmosphere there.

Since matters of goodness and holiness are connected to Hashem, who is Ein Sof, there is certainly always room to add. As it is said, "He who has one hundred wants two hundred" (adding a hundred), and "he who has two hundred wants four hundred" (adding two hundred), and so on. We have been promised that one who comes to purify himself (specifically, to purify others, as well as to be purified himself) is assisted.

Regarding your question as to whether it is permitted to teach Chassidus to women: there is a clear ruling on this in the laws of Torah study. For example, see the Laws of Torah Study by our Alter Rebbe, end of Chapter 1: Women are **obligated** to learn the laws that they need to know, etc., and all positive commandments that are not time-bound, etc.

The very purpose of the exclusion of time-bound positive commandments is that those commandments whose obligation is constant—never ceasing for a person, not even for a moment throughout their life—are to believe in Hashem, to unify Him, to love Him, and to fear Him [not to believe in another, not to stray after the thoughts of the heart and the sight of the eyes] (Letter of the author of *Sefer HaChinuch*).

The fulfillment of these mitzvos in their truth, and not merely lip service, comes about as the great teacher states in the Laws of the Foundations of the Torah, beginning of Chapter 2: "And what is the path, etc.? At the time that one **contemplates**, etc." This contemplation comes through the study of the teachings of Chassidus, and so on.

I hope, even though you do not mention it, that you have visited Kfar Chabad and Chabad circles in general, and specifically during times of favor, the days of farbrengens. It would please me to know your impressions from these visits.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in both general and personal matters.

P.S.
My letters with New Year blessings surely arrived.

7590

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I am in receipt of your letter in which you write about your state of mind and the problems that have arisen in your classroom, which have led you to leave your teaching position for the time being, and you ask for my opinion on the matter.

In my opinion, there are three reasons for your state of mind: a) For some reason (which, naturally, can only be known on the spot), you are extremely exhausted from your work **combined** with some other matter (troubles at home or something similar that tires the body); b) Apparently, you were given a higher grade level than you anticipated, or than one should have at the **beginning** of one’s independent teaching career; c) According to what is explained in the holy Tanya, since most people are not on the level of *tzaddikim*—meaning that there is still room for the *yetzer hara* to entice them—one of its most active tactics, and therefore its favorite, is to pull a person into a state of sadness, low spirits, and the like. It stands guard, looking for an opportune moment when a person is in a state of exhaustion or similar, when it is easier to pull them into the aforementioned state of mind.

From the above, my opinion is clear: it is certainly within your ability to continue in the field of teaching, to succeed in it, and to ascend from level to level. However, first you must nullify the aforementioned causes. Working from the last to the first: a) Resolve not to listen to the enticement of the *yetzer hara*; b) Choose from among the classes the one that is easiest in terms of discipline and also in terms of the level of studies; c) Begin teaching after a simple rest, so that the body is neither tired nor weary.

The length of time required for proper rest is not the same for everyone. For some, a few hours are sufficient, while for others, several days are needed. But the common denominator for both is that it is helpful to resolve to view the situation as it is—meaning that there is nothing exceptional here, but rather a normal situation where several causes occurred at once, which is why the result is magnified beyond the ordinary. Since the causes are separate, and each one individually is neither difficult nor great, they can be nullified with relative ease.

Since a person is biased toward themselves, they cannot always evaluate their own strengths, nor the extent to which external matters affect them, etc. Therefore, it is worthwhile that you consult with your friends who are familiar with all that has been said, and, of course, one of the main people in this regard is the school principal, Rabbi Zilberstrom, *shlita*.

May the *Ribono shel Olam*, who watches over each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*—and whose kindness and goodness you have seen in a revealed and manifest way many times in the past, including the recent past—certainly guide you on a good path. You need only strengthen your trust in the Creator of the world and its Guide, and remain in a state of tranquility, joy, and goodness of heart.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.
