7558

7558

By the Grace of G-d
6 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, who toils in Torah and wisdom, who occupies himself with the needs of the community,
Rabbi R. S. Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a long hiatus, which caused me concern—and which, as indicated by your letter, was due to extraneous circumstances—your letter from Rosh Chodesh Shevat has been received. And now, to address the matters in order.

1) Regarding the Chief Rabbinate: It is by no means certain that the matter has been postponed for many months, as negotiations are being conducted behind the scenes. Commercial proposals—"you keep yours and I will keep mine"—are being exchanged among the important factors in this affair, and who knows what a day may bring, what new developments may arise daily that will influence the course of the negotiations, etc. Furthermore—and this is also important, as I have written to several of anash to clarify my position on the matter, for to my surprise, there are still those who cast doubt upon it, perhaps due to their own leanings on the subject; in any case, they find room to attribute their own opinions to me, which are sometimes the exact opposite—the publication by your honor of a segment of my letter regarding the practical points: a) the damage caused by delaying the elections; b) the fact that this necessitates that there must be someone who is actually elected, and regarding the Ashkenazim, there is only one candidate; c) regarding the Sephardim, it is a disgrace to the Torah and the Rabbinate to remove a Rabbi from his position, etc.—would dispel the attempt to pin all sorts of nonsense on me, and perhaps it might even influence the course of events.

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning the Rabbinate in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established: I do not know the candidates about whom you write, but in any case, I am of the same opinion as your honor regarding his candidacy: it is not a matter for him at all.

3) Regarding a commentary on the Tanach: As for the "scientific" commentary by Professor... and the notion that I expressed an opinion on it, this rumor is a great wonder. I believe this is the first time I have heard of the existence of such a commentary, even though it is a matter that was not on my mind, etc. But in any event, even based on the points in your letter, the aforementioned individual is not at all suited to compile a traditional commentary on the Tanach. Regarding what I said about "versions and variants," I **explained** on the spot what I meant: it is like the edition published by Professor Kittel, where in the margins he collected the variants **found in different printed Chumashim and manuscripts.** It is **understood** that there was no discussion whatsoever regarding biblical criticism or the like, **Heaven forbid.**

4) Regarding your note about what is mentioned in my letter or in my words concerning the commentary of the Metzudas Dovid and Metzudas Tzion: it is based on the fact that in the teachings of Chassidus, this commentary is cited as being among the traditional texts in which generations of children were taught, who subsequently lived their lives in accordance with Torah and tradition.

5) As for your question as to why one should not innovate new commentaries, especially since we find such things in the name of Rashi, as brought by his grandson, the Rashbam: the distinction is simple according to the words of our Rebbe HaZaken (cited by the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, in the *Hemshech* *Ta'arev*, in a section that was not copied), that all the authors from the Taz and the Shach and onwards composed their works with *Ruach HaKodesh* (this was also copied in *Hayom Yom*, 6 Shevat). Incidentally, after some time, I also found this in the book *She'eris Yisrael*, a *drush* for Sukkos by the Maharid of Viliednik, in the name of the "Ribash"—which apparently refers to the Baal Shem Tov.

6) Furthermore, it should be noted that the wonder is, on the contrary, directed at those who are not satisfied with the commentaries of our predecessors—at least regarding commentaries on the *peshat*, in which they studied the Tanach and explained it as much as was necessary. And even if one takes into account new discoveries, etc., a note in the margin is sufficient for that; there is no need to compile a new commentary. And when one observes the situation in our generation, etc., it is a wonder that it is precisely the younger generation that wants to return to the sources, but those who fought against the *Maskilim* in their youth imagine that the new generation also wants to fight, and consequently, they hold onto tactics and weapons that are not needed at all. And if regarding physical weapons, "that which is not needed is not becoming" (*Shabbos* 63a), then regarding spiritual matters, it is also harmful. This is clearly seen in all the literature; in the new style, they call this "apologetics," and we have had nothing but trouble from it to this day [including the *drush* *Ohr HaChaim* by the author of *Tiferes Yisrael*, the books of Rabbi Hirsch, and others, and even generations ago—the commentaries of Philo of Alexandria, who wanted to harmonize, albeit with good intentions, with the "beauty" of the Greeks, etc.—but it is irrelevant and untrue in such matters], and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Regarding what is cited in the name of the Zohar, *man d'nafash mitochei nafash* ("he who exhales, exhales from within himself") (in *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 2; *Iggeres HaKodesh* 15; and elsewhere)—I believe it is not found in the Zohar and *Tikkunei Zohar* that we have before us. However, it is found in the books of the early authorities*.

I am sure you are preparing for the *Yom HaHillula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on the 10th of Shevat, in the spirit mentioned in the letter of the *Baal HaHillula* regarding the *Yom HaHillula* of my father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory.

May it be G-d's will that the preparations and activities on this auspicious day be successful, and that their influence be drawn down for the entire year, with tranquility, joy, and a good heart.

With respect and blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you and your friend, *shiyeh*, at the *tziyon hakadosh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h*, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Are you also keeping up with the *shlosha shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* as is well known?

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

Secretary

P.S. It would be appropriate to have your *tefillin* checked, and also to give a few cents to *tzedakah* every weekday morning before *davening*.

a) Regarding the question of why one sometimes feels an awakening toward *Yiddishkeit* without any prior preparation, and whether there is any concern in this: As explained by the Baal Shem Tov, this comes from the *bas kol* that goes out every day, etc., as explained elsewhere. In order for this to be a lasting thing, one must immediately connect it with an action on the part of the person, as is also explained elsewhere.

b) How to discern matters of conduct: The test for this is as explained in *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan.

c) Regarding conduct during *tefillah*: The instruction is well known if it concerns *kavanah*—since *kavanah* is an essential element of *tefillah*—one should begin with the *tzibbur*, and afterwards one may also prolong [the *davening*] so that the *tefillah* may be with *kavanah*.

d) Regarding your question about being careful in this matter: In general, a person’s conduct should be as explained in the Rambam, *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 1.

## 7601

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the Distribution Committee of the sefer *Eish Kodesh*,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter along with the sefer *Eish Kodesh*, which Divine Providence has granted you the merit to publish for the world.

If our Sages of blessed memory spoke at length regarding the importance of disseminating words of Torah in general, how much more so is this true regarding the teachings of the great leaders of Israel, by whose light thousands walked and who died for the sanctification of His Name.

The magnitude of this matter is explained in the teachings of Chassidus with a definitive proof from the request and prayer of the author himself, that he merit to die for the sanctification of His Name, and the matter that caused this request not to be fulfilled, which was considered a punishment—even though in the years that followed, he merited to write his *Shulchan Aruch*, which serves as a guide for Israel until the end of all generations.

May it be the will that through the words of this sefer—in accordance with the instruction of our Sages that "great is study, for it leads to action"—the hearts of those who read and study it will be awakened to the love of Hashem and the awe of Him,

And to their branches, which are the fulfillment of the 248 positive mitzvos, for which love is the root, and the observance of the 365 negative mitzvos, for which awe is the root (as explained by Rabbeinu HaZaken in his holy *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 4).

With respect and blessing for good tidings regarding the aforementioned.

P.S.
Regarding your question concerning the distribution of the sefer in the United States—seemingly, the beginning should be by way of the Agudas HaAdmorim located here in the United States, according to the address listed below.

## 7662

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Beshalach, 5721
Brooklyn

To the Annual Banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos "Tomchei Temimim"

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive the notification regarding your annual event this coming Tuesday, 14 Shevat.

I hope that the leadership and the members, may they be well, as well as all the participants, may they be well, will make every effort to ensure the financial and spiritual success of the event.

We are all surely under the impression of the Yahrtzeit-Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the founder and leader of the Lubavitcher yeshivos, for which he literally practiced mesiras nefesh. This is the very essence of commemorating and observing a Yahrtzeit: that every man and woman who has the great privilege of being connected to the Rebbe and his holy work should be encouraged to continue and expand all areas of the work of the Baal HaHilula, with renewed strength, determination, and mesiras nefesh.

The parsha we read this Shabbos, Shabbos Shirah, emphasizes in particular the importance of Jewish women, as expressed at the splitting of the Sea by Miriam the Prophetess and all the women, who continued—with extraordinary simcha and hislahavus—what Moshe Rabbeinu had begun. It is for this reason that the Haftorah of this Shabbos is the song of Devorah the Prophetess (and not the song of Dovid Hamelech, which is read on the seventh day of Pesach, when the same parsha in the Torah is read, as is explained at length in a sicha of the Baal HaHilula). The song of Miriam the Prophetess and of Devorah the Prophetess are not only a song of praise from Jewish women to the Ribono shel Olam, but also from the Ribono shel Olam to Jewish women.

Just as the words and blessings of tzaddikim remain and have an eternal effect, may the blessings of the Baal HaHilula stand by each and every one of you and your families, may they live—for success in all your affairs, both in gashmius and in ruchnius alike.

With blessings for good tidings,

## 7,604

B"H, 12 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Yom HaHillula, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed with it, which was read at a time of favor on the day of the *hillula* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at his holy gravesite.

Thank you for the good news regarding the success of the gathering on 24 Teves, the *hillula* of Rabbeinu HaZaken. May it be His will that, as you wrote, this will inspire every one of *anash* in your camp to increase their efforts in establishing and developing the holy institution. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since this aligns with the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the continuation of his *maamarim* of *Chassidus* for his *hillula*, Chapter 11, that from Above they open the treasures of precious wealth, etc., and distribute them through the officers of the army for the sake of the army (see there).

Regarding your question as to whether it is advisable for your son, *sheyichyeh*, to recite in public everything he has already reviewed—it seems I have already written in my previous letter the reason for my reservation regarding this practice. From this, it is understood that what has already been done cannot be undone; at the very least, one should utilize the effort and time to recite it in public for the *nachas ruach* of those who seek *nachas ruach* in such matters.

It is my hope that you gathered together on the day of the *hillula*, and may it be His will that your actions align with the letter of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the *hillula* of his father (the Rebbe Rashab), *nif'alav*, on 2 Nissan (*Kuntres* 3, 36).

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.

## 7660

B"H, 12 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, Torah-scholars, G-d-fearing men, R' Yosef Yehuda, may he live, and R' Naftali, may he live:

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of the 9th of Shevat, regarding your question as to whether there is room to shift the syllable emphasis of the words so that they conform to the rules of *milra* and *mileil*.

In general, your concern is incomprehensible, for in *nigunim* one does not adhere at all to these rules; indeed, one does not even adhere to more fundamental rules, to the point that sometimes syllables are even added, and so on.

If, for whatever reason, this specific case is one where "the law must pierce the mountain" and you feel you must change it, you may do so. However, as mentioned above, the beauty of a *nigun* lies in its independence from the rules of grammar, etc.

2) Regarding your question of whether to arrange the *nigunim* for a choir in two parts, as this would make them more easily accepted by the teachers:

Here, too, I am puzzled, for on the face of it, the opposite seems more logical. A *nigun* arranged for two parts cannot be sung by a single person (in a case where there was not enough time to prepare a second singer, or there is no second singer available, etc.). Nevertheless, since it seems you wish to fulfill the desire and preference of each person, there is no principle involved here either; since the *nigun* itself will not be altered in the slightest, you may arrange it in a way that is suitable.

3) Regarding your question of whether to note the name of the arranger, etc. — it is understood that this depends on local custom and the reaction of the public. However, I have strong hope that regarding the second point there is no concern, for the arranger whose name is written is an upright man. He has certainly begun to conduct himself in the straight path, which is the path of our Torah, the Torah of life, and in the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." Certainly, noting his name in the booklet will add strength and courage to him to overcome the *yetzer*, and the Ribono shel Olam will assist him.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned, and for the general activities of *hafatza maayanos chutzah*. We are approaching the day of the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*.

P.S. As you requested, the letter is sent without a translation.

## 766

766

B"H, 14 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, a man of fine character and great accomplishments,
R' Eliezer Zusia, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long interval, I received your letter bringing good news regarding the arrangement of the newly acquired house, which will serve as both a shul and a beis medrash.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be in a good and successful hour, both materially and spiritually. This is in accordance with the sentiment we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that Hashem gives Jews material things, and they, in turn, transform that materiality into spirituality.

This is also the theme of this week’s parsha, the parsha of the giving of the Torah. The Torah is the wisdom and will of Hashem, and it was given specifically to those who descended to Mitzrayim and have a yetzer hara among them, etc.—for it was precisely this argument that led to the ascent to the heights, to take captives captive.

May it be the will of Hashem that these two matters be united: the beis medrash (the study of Torah, the purpose of which is to lead to action—the fulfillment of mitzvos) and the shul (tefillah, the requesting of a person’s needs and their fulfillment by the One who sustains and provides for all in His goodness, with grace, kindness, and mercy—which naturally includes, quite simply, material needs as well, in a revealed and manifest good).

This is also explained in the statement of our Sages, that true good is "good for Heaven" (spirituality), "good for people" (materiality), and "good that produces fruit"—the influence upon others, both materially and spiritually alike.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

***

**766**

**R' Eliezer Zusia:** Portugal, the Skulener Rebbe.

**In the sentiment:** See also above, Vol. 18, Letter 6331, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7667

B"H, 14 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, possessor of noble character, scion of a noble lineage, etc., R’ Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...In connection with the yahrtzeit-hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding whom it is stated in the well-known Iggeres HaKodesh that a tzaddik who has departed is found in all worlds more than during his lifetime, and that "Torah scholars go from strength to strength," the soul of the baal hilula also ascends from level to level. Therefore, all matters connected with him must likewise ascend from strength to strength. And based on what is explained, that "Israel is one nation on earth," unifying all matters on earth—both physical and spiritual, both in quantity and in quality—this ascent must also be in both quantity and quality. Start with activities concerning young children in the literal sense, young in years, and continue through to activities for the benefit of those who are "small" in their quality. Enclosed is a segment of the remarks made at the opening of the farbrengen on the day of the hilula, in which I touched upon this point.

...Rabbi Gorodetsky, may he live, informed me that you are currently vacationing in Teveria. May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize these days of rest to their fullest. Since for every active person, and especially for you, a vacation is nothing more than preparation for increased activity afterward, this is the intent in the success of the vacation: to renew one's strength for increased activity, in the style of Chapter 11 of the *Hemshech* of the hilula, in this eleventh year. Regarding the attainment of the goal: "expending all the virtues of the treasures of precious wealth gathered and collected over many years, from generation to generation."

With respect and blessing for good tidings in health and joy.

## 7668

B”H, 15 Shevat, Rosh Hashanah La’ilanot 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N’shei U’Bnos Chabad Branch
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

As we find ourselves a few days from the yom hillula — the yahrtzeit — of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, and as an addition to the opening remarks at the farbrengen in connection with this yom hillula, on Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Shirah, a transcript of which is enclosed.

I also wish to emphasize in this letter the special zechus (and simultaneously the responsibility) of Jewish women in general, and of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad in particular, in implementing in practice what was said in that sicha regarding dedication to the chinuch hakodesh of Jewish children.

As we see in practice, chinuch—especially in the very young years—depends primarily, or entirely, on the woman.

And in general, the three character traits for which the Jewish people are distinguished—rachmanim (merciful), baishanim (modest/bashful), and gomlei chasadim (performers of kindness)—find expression in Jewish women to a very great degree.

These traits of rachamim and gemilus chasadim are of the utmost importance in the chinuch of children.

May Hashem grant that you should carry out the above in good health and good spirits—imbued with Chassidishe warmth and light—and may He grant you hatzlacha in this.

And surely this will also bring an increase in the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in the private matters of each and every one of you, together with your families, shlita.

With blessings for good tidings in all of the above.

## 7,660

B"H, 19 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your writing on how to prevent the undesirable expressions heard in your classroom:

You should explain to them that for every single one of the children of Yisrael, Hashem’s love for them is even greater than the love of parents for an only child born to them in their old age. This is in accordance with the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov on this matter, and furthermore—that it is said of Hashem, "He who plants the ear, shall He not hear? He who forms the eye, shall He not see?" When one speaks well of a child of the Makom Baruch Hu, He sees, observes, and listens to the content of the speech and the manner in which it is spoken. The caution that must be exercised in this is understood—so as not to offend the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He.

And all the more so, and *kal v'chomer*—would anyone dare to speak improperly about the child of a flesh-and-blood king in the presence of the king, and so on? You can certainly add explanation and emphasis to what has been said. What will be even more effective is if you hang a sign on the wall of the room where they study, with a message along the lines of: "Reflect upon what you are saying, for an eye sees and an ear hears," etc.

## 779

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a long hiatus, your letter from the 15th of Shevat was received, in which you write regarding your state of mind, etc., and conclude with your visit to the doctor and the doctor’s opinion.

It is understood that, in general, my opinion aligns with that of the doctor, based on the instruction of our Torah—Torah of life—regarding such matters. The instruction of our Sages, *maaseh rav*, is also well-known, and we see tangibly in many, many cases similar to yours that when one proceeds with *shidduchim*—and within a short time, the marriage follows—they settle into a stable and orderly life. It reaches the point where they themselves are surprised by the hesitation and feelings they had beforehand (regarding the engagement process), etc. It has already been said many times that a person’s life is not exact mathematics, where it is possible to put all the details down in black and white and, consequently, draw up a plan. On the contrary—in the vast majority of cases, the less one over-analyzes, the better.

May it be the will of Hashem, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, that from here on out you will walk your path securely, with actual trust in *hashgacha pratis*—meaning, for yourself personally. Consequently, this will at least weaken the melancholy, and you will take an interest in worthy proposals in an appropriate manner, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings,

P.S.
My hope is strong that you participated in the *farbrengens* of the auspicious day, the *yom hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. May it be His will that you draw from his essence throughout the entire year. This, in turn, adds to the blessing of Hashem in a literal sense.

## 7771

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, active in communal needs, Rav Shaar Yashuv HaKohen, may he live.

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the two books. I am writing this letter specifically because it seems that even regarding the aforementioned, the statement of our Sages applies: "Everything depends on mazal, even a Sefer Torah in the Heichal." In this context, this applies even to a printed book. I am referring to the book *Yesod V'Shoresh HaAvodah*. Although it is printed in clear, bright letters, the manner of its publication is lacking "handles for the basket"—and it is lacking significantly. Our generation has become accustomed to having everything handed to them on a platter, ready to be absorbed without any effort, let alone extra effort.

In the aforementioned book, which contains nearly **500** pages, there is **no index at all**, not even a simple one—that is to say, no indication of the beginning of each *sha'ar* and *perek*, etc. In my opinion, if the intention is, as written in the introduction, for it to be accessible to a wide circle, it is essential to have a table of contents—at the very least a general one, and it would be even better if it were detailed. And anyone who provides such detail in a work like this is to be praised.

It is understood that according to the instruction of our Sages, one does not cry over the past. I would not have written all of the above had I not seen a way to rectify the deficiency, at least in part. This could be done by printing a pamphlet of a few pages containing the aforementioned "handles" and attaching it to every book that is sent out. *Kal v'chomer* (it is certainly logical).

Enclosed is a copy of a *sicha* excerpt from the day of the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which I hope will be of interest to you.

With respect and blessings,

## 7792

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter with the good news regarding the results of the examinations, noting that they were able to answer properly and with clear understanding.

Many thanks for the satisfaction and *nachas* this news has caused. In accordance with the measure of the *Ribono shel Olam*—which is "measure for measure," only many times over—may you be the bearer of further good tidings that will bring true *nachas* in all your affairs.

The above is also connected to the *inyana d'yoma*—the *parsha* of the week and its beginning: "And these are the *mishpatim* (ordinances) that you shall set before them." This implies showing them the "inner face," etc. In the words of the Alter Rebbe (*Hilchos Talmud Torah*, end of chapter 3): "Until they (the students) understand the depth of the *halacha* and its rationale well, to set before them a rationale that settles their study and places it in their hearts, etc."

May it be the will of Hashem that this be fulfilled in the students and those who set these matters before them, as well as the interpretation of the Alter Rebbe in his *sefer Torah Or* regarding the aforementioned verse: "before them"—before their *penimiyus* (inner dimension).

With this, we can also resolve a difficulty that arises on the face of it: Surely, the obligation to "set before them" applies to all areas of our Torah study. Yet, one would think this command is primarily needed for the *chukim* (statutes) rather than the *mishpatim*, as the verse states. After all, it is easier to understand the rational *mitzvos* with a rationale that settles one's study, whereas regarding the *chukim*, it is said: "A statute I have enacted, a decree I have decreed, and you have no permission to contemplate them."

However, according to the inner interpretation—the *penimiyus* of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—that the "setting" must be before the *penimiyus* of the *nefesh*, it is resolved simply: The rational *mitzvos*, which are understood and grasped with good taste and *da'as*, do not stir the *penimiyus* of the *nefesh* as deeply, nor does it bond with them. This is not the case with *chukim* and decrees. Therefore, the Torah must specify that even regarding *mishpatim*, the "setting" must be into the *penimiyus*.

Based on this, another wonder is resolved: Why the *mishpatim* begin with the law of purchasing a Hebrew slave who is sold by the *Beis Din* due to his theft. Seemingly, this is not understood at all. Why begin with the disgrace of one who transgressed the *mitzvos* of Hashem to the point that he has nothing with which to pay for his theft? Furthermore, we have not yet learned how much a thief must pay, and this law only applies when the *Yovel* is in effect, etc.

According to what has been said, this too is understood: The effort to ensure that the "setting" reaches the *penimiyus* of the *nefesh* is an effort bound up with *yegias nefesh* (exertion of the soul) and *yegias basar* (exertion of the flesh). For although the fear of a human king is present in everyone, this is not the case with the fear of Heaven. As Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai said, "If only the fear of Heaven were upon you, etc." (*see Tanya, chapter 41*). Therefore, the "spirit of folly" that sometimes enters a person acts to "steal the mind" of the Above. But the fear of a human being is upon him—and in this, the thief is inferior to the robber, as per the words of **Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai** regarding this (*Bava Kamma 79b*).

This is the beginning, immediately following the time of *Matan Torah*, as the order of the text dictates: "Depart from evil." The *Beis Din*—the "heads of the thousands of Yisrael" (*see Tanya, beginning of chapter 42*)—will assist the one who stole, so that "six years he shall serve"—the six weekdays, the "six thousand years that this world exists"—and on the seventh day he shall go out to freedom, the *Shabbos* and rest for the life of the worlds (*see there in Torah Or*).

With blessings.

## 7793

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in Torah, R' Asher, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Ilanot.

At an *eis ratzon*, please mention the *avreich*... may he live, at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May he be the bearer of good news regarding this.

Regarding your question on behalf of a donor who wishes to write in his will that after 120 years his assets should be given to an institution in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, to construct a building there for a place of Torah in his name and the name of his family members, and he is asking for the name of the institution specifically and in English.

In general, since the time of the transfer of the assets is not clear—and may the aforementioned live long and good years—it is complicated to name an institution "specifically," as you wrote. There is another point to this: a question will arise regarding the manner of transferring the assets there if he bequeaths them to an institution located in Eretz Yisrael. It is much simpler and more convenient if he registers the assets in the name of an institution located abroad that has departments and a field of activity in Eretz Yisrael (with the addition in the will that the assets are given specifically to build a place of Torah there). If this reasoning is accepted and he wishes to proceed this way, he can register it in the name of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch or similar, with the addition of the aforementioned conditions.

Another way to do this is to register it in the name of the branch of the Merkos that is in Australia, if it has official standing there. The branch would act as the representative of the Merkos here. Similarly, it is possible to do this through the Yeshiva or Beis Rivkah, although the possibilities are more limited then, because surely a Yeshiva is not in a position to build a school for girls, and likewise Beis Rivkah regarding boys, whereas the Merkos has both matters in its scope.

If, for whatever reason, he specifically wants to write in the will the name of an institution in Eretz Yisrael, it is possible to write: "The Spiritual Committee of Kfar Chabad, under the leadership of the Rav of Kfar Chabad."

[I added the word "Spiritual" so that there would be no possibility of taking the assets to pay off the village's debts, should there be any at that time], or "The Administration of Beis Rivkah in Kfar Chabad."

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

Regarding your trip, I have already stated that I am not at all comfortable with crossing the International Date Line in the middle of the days of Sefirah. Even though, from the perspective of the *din*, my opinion is clear—that regarding the festival of Shavuos, it depends solely on the number of days, and this count is entrusted to each individual—and consequently, one who crosses the Date Line does not need to take into account at all the time of the celebration of Shavuos of the Jews in the place he arrives, but rather he should celebrate it on the fiftieth day of his own count [at which point he will be different by one day from the celebration of the Jews living in that place—assuming he does not cross the Date Line in the opposite direction in the middle of the days of Sefirah], and as I mentioned, my opinion is clear on this—nevertheless, it is a highly questionable matter [especially since, in my opinion, the distinction is from the Torah], and therefore one should avoid entering into the aforementioned situation as much as possible.

This is especially relevant in light of the words of our Sages that *ribis* draws the principal along with it, etc...

## 7505

B"H, 22 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn

To Mr. Menachem Begin,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I will begin with the good news that I was pleased to hear that the matter of the Eruv in Moshav Bar Giora is being arranged.

There is no matter greater than the Shabbos observance of the many. In addition to the statement of our Sages of blessed memory that Shabbos is equal to all the mitzvos combined, in our times, during this double and redoubled galus, there is a special value to the promise of our Sages that if Yisrael would keep even one Shabbos according to its law, they would be redeemed immediately. Since Divine Providence has granted me the privilege of taking part in this matter, I wish to participate with my own resources as well. I take the liberty of enclosing my personal check as a symbolic contribution toward the expenses of arranging the Eruv. Since I do not know to whom to send this, I thank you in advance for your trouble in delivering it to the appropriate place.

By way of thanks, I also thank you for the two books of yours that were received in my library. The acknowledgement was delayed until now because I hoped that we would meet again during your second visit. In any case, may his strength and vigor be increased.

You are surely aware of our custom to gather for a farbrengen in connection with the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, our leader, on which occasion words of inspiration are heard in light of the activities of the one whose yahrtzeit is being observed. From the opening remarks delivered at this year’s farbrengen for the 10th of Shevat, I have had a segment printed, which is enclosed herewith. It is my hope that you will find interest in it. I will admit—and I am not ashamed to say—that I have an additional intention in sending this segment to you: as a continuation of our conversation when we met, regarding the most special importance in our era of activity among the youth and young people. I emphasize "our era" in particular, not only because of the great necessity for this, but also because of the great capacity and possibility to accomplish in one hour in this generation of ours what would have required the great efforts of many years in the generation before this. True, this activity requires energy and dedication, without regard for other considerations or the calculations of cold intellect. And these two qualities are the very nature of the youth and young people. Furthermore, when one directs the youth on the straight path toward a straight goal, the organizers themselves are lifted and carried along by the energy and momentum of the youth, reaching such a peak that, due to their being of middle age or beyond, they would not have been able to reach it through their own efforts alone.

It is wondrous how our Sages of blessed memory expressed this in a brief adage in their account of the Exodus from Egypt—the redemption from the first galus through Moshe Rabbeinu and the elders of Yisrael. When they were confronted with the first miracle of the period of the redemption, namely the miracle of the splitting of the Red Sea, it was the children and the youth who had grown up in Egypt who recognized it first, even before it had its effect upon their fathers and the elders of Yisrael, as it is written: "This is my G-d and I will beautify Him, the G-d of my father and I will exalt Him."

With respect and blessing,

#### ***7505***

**Mr. Menachem Begin:** Another letter to him appears later, 7624.

**Enclosed segment:** See also above, letter 7667.

## 7760

B"H, 24 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 20th of Shevat.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good tidings regarding the matters about which you write, in accordance with the beginning and foundation of these parshios: "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell among them" (*Shemos 25:8*). Our Sages explained that it does not say "in it" (*betocho*), but "among them" (*betocham*)—within each and every one.

Certainly, according to the rule that a verse never loses its literal meaning, this is also connected to "And they shall make Me a sanctuary," for Hashem also dwells in the sanctuary, but the main point is "among them"—that the making of the sanctuary and the Divine Presence within the sanctuary are the means through which the matter of "and I will dwell among them" is achieved.

This is also understood from the continuation of the *maamar* of the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*: "I have come into My garden" (*Basi L'Gani*)—see there.

May it be Hashem’s will that everything be accomplished—both the activities in the world ("And they shall make Me a sanctuary") and the activities within oneself ("and I will dwell among them")—with health and with wealth. For our Sages have taught us that the sanctuary is a place of wealth (see *Tamid 29a*, Rashi s.v. *Aval*), that all their deeds were done with wealth and authority.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***7760***

A similar copy was sent to several others.

## 7577

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Im Kesef Talveh, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Brooklyn, N.Y.

May it be Hashem’s will that the meeting be successful in increasing your activities, and may you do so with tranquility, joy, and goodness of heart.

For Gemilas Chasadim applies to the wealthy as well, etc.

Especially according to what is understood from chapter eleven of the *hemshech* of the *maamar* for the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel,

That in this generation, the *ikvesa d’meshicha*, they expend "all the treasures of precious wealth collected and gathered over many years, from generation to generation, etc., and they hand them over through officials—for the sake of the army, etc."

As is explained in many places, that which is spiritual descends into the physical; thus, regarding the above—the aforementioned treasures will also descend into treasures in the literal sense, in our immediate time, with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu (through utilizing the spiritual treasures, as explained in the *hemshech*).

At that time, the warning and promise will be fulfilled in its entirety: "However, there shall be no needy person among you," for Yisroel will be doing the will of Hashem (see Rashi (and it is from Sifrei) Re'eh 15:4; Sanhedrin 104a; Ra'aya Mehemna, Zohar Vol. III, 125a; Avodas HaKodesh, Part II, Ch. 38).

With blessings for success.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
Enclosed is my check—my participation in your holy work.

## 7778

B"H, 27 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Shevat, in which you write about what you have heard and the reliance on pesukim and hints, etc.

In general, one should not involve oneself in such calculations, as this is a matter only for those who possess some tradition or the like. Otherwise, every single person believes in the coming of Moshiach, etc., and "I wait for him every day that he shall come." However, along with this, it is incumbent upon everyone to do everything within their power to hasten and accelerate the coming of our righteous Moshiach. Specifically, this is through the spreading of the wellsprings outward, as is known from the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov regarding the answer of Melech HaMoshiach: "When your wellsprings spread outward, he will come."

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It is surprising that you do not mention the yom hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, on the tenth of Shevat, although my hope is strong that you gathered together and that there will be results, as is explained in the letter of the Baal HaHilula regarding the yom hilula of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 7579

[27 Shevat 5721]

In response to your letter of [date]... The sources from our Sages are too numerous to count, as are the practical halachic rulings, which are all founded on the fact that the Sages were diligent in establishing safeguards for the **daughters** of Israel regarding matters of marriage and personal status, and specifically in the resolution of cases of *agunot*. If, despite this, there exists a situation where the Torah does not permit an *agunah* to remarry, it is self-evident that it is also contrary to sound reason to introduce "reforms" according to the whim of a particular individual. Whichever way you look at it: if a person **alters** a halachic ruling of the Torah—meaning that in his opinion, man is superior to the Torah—then what use does he have for a Torah that would command him what to do? And if he knows the truth, that the Torah is from Heaven, how can the limited intellect of a human being come to change a ruling of the Creator, who is unlimited and not comparable to him, and declare that one law is "right" in his eyes while another is not? Proposals of this nature have been **categorically** rejected by the great leaders of previous generations, as well as by the *Agudas HaRabbonim* here, which consists of hundreds of rabbis who have spent most of their lives immersed in Torah with diligence, and who have prohibited them.

It is my hope that from time to time you are increasing in Torah and *mitzvos*, in accordance with the command to "ascend in matters of holiness," and there is nothing that can stand before the will. I am enclosing a segment from the *sicha* of 10 Shevat, which I am certain will interest you and which you will utilize in the appropriate manner.

#### ***7579***

**Enclosed segment:** See letter 7567 above.

## 7580

B”H, 28 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal needs, R’ Dovid, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 26 Shevat and those preceding it.

Regarding what you wrote about changing the vacation schedule—in most cases of this nature, even when one succeeds in their efforts, it only serves to diminish [the learning time], meaning: it is not that they will study during the previously scheduled vacation and take time off at a different time, but rather that they will not study then, nor will they study now. Nevertheless, since the matter is in doubt and it is possible that the conditions in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) are different in general, what has been done until now and what is necessary to continue should be continued. However, a new effort requires careful consideration as to whether the results are worth it. It is understood that this applies if the change in vacation would only be in some of the schools, but if there is room to say that it would apply to all schools—at the very least to all the state-religious schools—then the aforementioned concern is nullified...

I look forward to hearing good news regarding general matters and your personal affairs. As we stand in close proximity to the month of Adar, whose central point is the days of Purim—which represent *v’nahafoch hu* (and it was turned around), where all the obstacles, concealments, and obstructions are turned into sources of assistance—may you be the bearer of good news regarding the aforementioned, and in general, with an abundance.

The *pidyon nefesh* was received.

With blessings for good news.

## 7581

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5721

## 7582

7582

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, R' Shalom, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Following a pause, I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, along with the enclosure.

As today is Erev Rosh Chodesh, a time when we increase in joy, I mentioned your son, may he live, for a complete and speedy recovery at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that together with his wife, you raise him—along with all your children, may they live—to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

I read with pleasure of your activities. However, it is appropriate to recall the adage of our Rebbes, whose very adages are Torah: "Good is good, and better is better." I will quote the language of the verse: "They made me keeper of the vineyards; but my own vineyard I have not kept" (Shir Hashirim 1:6)—meaning, that even though the Torah says that [communal work] is a vineyard and must be guarded, it does not compare to the guarding of "my own vineyard."

As has been explained many times, everything is hinted at even in the revealed parts of Torah, down to the practical halacha. This is the case here as well—for the magnitude of the distinction mentioned above is understood: from the halachic ruling that even **all** "matters of Heaven"—i.e., mitzvos—cannot compare to **one** word of Torah study. Yet, regarding a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others ("my own vineyard"), not only do they compare (Moed Katan 9b), but one even interrupts Torah study to engage in the mitzvah (see Rashi and Tosafos there).

It is obvious that my intention here refers to the study of Chassidus and its related matters, guidance, and conduct. Since we have been commanded regarding this, there is certainly full possibility to do so, for the Holy One, blessed be He, does not act tyrannically with His creatures, and the matter depends only on one's will.

Regarding what you wrote about the Rambam and the wisdom of Kabbalah, see *Sefer HaSichos* Summer 5700, page 41 and the footnote there.

Regarding your question about saying "Selach Lanu," although I have not heard of this, from the nature of the matter it appears to depend only on the time of saying "Selach Lanu," not on what will be afterwards.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding the number of words in *Al HaNissim*: See the *Yaavetz*—for Chanukah: 108, etc. (and this is according to the version of the Alter Rebbe); for Purim: 66. The figure brought from the *Kol Bo*, etc., of 124–125, can be explained as depending on the two opinions in the *Shulchan Aruch*, end of Siman 682. See *Shaarei HaGadol* to the *Hagahos Mordechai*, Perek 2 of Shabbos: *Al HaNissim* has 124 words, etc., **with** the concluding phrase "as You did," etc.

Regarding the enclosure in your letter: In your essay regarding the obligation of Torah study including both men and women without any distinction—even in the hints! And furthermore, you conclude with the language of the Rambam on this! It is also worth noting the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, end of Chapter 1.

The drawings of the Luchos—as is common in the "world"—are rounded at the top! I have always wondered about this, for the language of the Shas implies they were square. It is necessitated by the words of our Sages regarding the verse "on this side and on that side they were written." This is precisely noted in the *Shaar HaShmuessin*.

## 7583

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the organizers of Kupas Rabbeinu in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 22 Shevat, along with the enclosure, in which you write regarding the initiative to strengthen the matter of Kupas Rabbeinu, etc.

There is strong hope that you will translate this initiative into actual practice, for the deed is the essential thing. Furthermore, the time is auspicious for this, as we have entered the month of Adar, whose central point is the days of Purim. One of the primary mitzvos of these days is *matanos la'evyonim* (gifts to the poor), which is distinct from other mitzvos of Purim—and from mitzvos in general—in that we do not scrutinize the recipient; rather, whoever reaches out their hand to take, we give to them.

Indeed, our generation—a generation of double and redoubled darkness, the *ikvesa d'meshicha* where "insolence will increase," etc., as explained at length by Chazal—is precisely the generation in which we ask and demand the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam, and specifically that He give with a generous eye and an open hand. The way to achieve this is to emulate the principle that "whoever reaches out their hand, we give to them"—to act in a similar fashion, as is the law regarding Purim funds.

And although it is understood and obvious that there is no comparison whatsoever, and an infinite gap, between the giving from below and what we demand from above—and that the lowliness of the one below in relation to the One Above is far greater than the lowliness of a person who reaches out their hand, Heaven forbid, to take from a fellow human being—this is precisely the concept of "insolence will increase" directed toward the side of good.

As is explained in many places, it is within a person's power to transform all undesirable matters so that they are directed specifically toward the side of good (see Likutei Torah, Parshas Bechukosai, discourse beginning *Eileh HaChukim*). And we have been promised regarding such a matter: "Insolence toward Heaven is effective."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, through the fulfillment of the mitzvah of "increasing in joy"—a joy that is both true and internal.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7583***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 16, p. 634.

## 7584

*[Shevat 5721]*

... The source for what is written in Torah Or, Beshalach (61d): **Our Sages of blessed memory said** that one who wishes to accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven should relieve himself, wash his hands, and put on tzitzis and tefillin — this is found in Pri Etz Chaim and in the Shaar HaKavanos of the Arizal at the beginning. It is perhaps based on Zohar Vol. III, 120b. It should be noted that the Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch (6:8, **first edition**) cites the language of the Gemara (Berachos 15a) while omitting tzitzis. Perhaps the two aforementioned opinions can be connected with the matter of tzitzis at night and sleeping in a tallis katan. See the ruling of the Tzemach Tzedek in Orach Chaim, Responsa 8; Bach and Perisha, Orach Chaim, end of section 2.

#### ***7584***

**The source for what is written:** For in the Gemara, Berachos 14b, the word "tzitzis" is not present.

7785

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Gemara shiur
Studied at the Adas Yaakov Synagogue in Brooklyn
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to learn from the esteemed Chossid, a man of many accomplishments and great energy, R' Moshe Pinchas HaKohen, that these days you are concluding your public study of Maseches Megillah.

Certainly, in accordance with the Jewish custom regarding Torah study, you will immediately begin studying another tractate. As per the formula established by our predecessors: "May it be Your will, Hashem, my G-d, that just as You have helped me to conclude... so may You help me to begin..."

This, too, can be explained according to what is elucidated in Chassidus: that the imperative language of the Torah also implies a promise for the future. Just as "they shall read [the Megillah] each at its proper time" implies both a command and a promise (for "no one shall be cast away from Him"), so too in the aforementioned prayer: a request before Him (which itself brings about the result) is also a promise from Him—that just as He has helped me, He will certainly help me [to begin].

May all of the above serve as the conclusion to the "May it be Your will" prayer and its seal: "Hashem will bless His people with peace," the vessel that contains the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam for everything a person and his household requires.

May it be His will that the beginning and end of this tractate you are concluding—Maseches Megillah—be fulfilled as well: "The Megillah is read on the eleventh... and on the fifteenth." It is known that this alludes to the Name Havayah—its end being *Yud-Heh* (15) and its beginning *Vav-Heh* (11). The total sum of all the days of reading the Megillah, from the eleventh to the fifteenth, is 65, the numerical value of the Name *Adonai*—the Name Havayah as it is pronounced when it is concealed; that is, when Elokus is hidden within the garments of the world. This is emphasized most strongly in the Megillah, where the Name is not mentioned explicitly, but only alluded to through acronyms and the final letters of words. Therefore, we were commanded that the Megillah be **read** and that there be a publicizing of the miracle.

So too is it generally through the study of Torah, which clarifies the matters of the world, determining that this is permitted, pure, and fit to be used for the will of Hashem and His mitzvos, and that is not permitted for "heavenly work."

Through this action of the **soul** of man **in the world**, we also reveal the true content and purpose of all the days of the **year**. For every single day must "perform its work," and specifically through the unique study established by Moshe for Yisrael, that they should inquire and expound **on the subject of the day**, and in the manner of Rashi’s commentary there: to accept and fulfill upon themselves and their children, in this world and the next.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 7,780

7,780

B"H, 1 Adar, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R' Menachem Zeev, may he live, Halevi.

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 21 Shevat...

I hope you will find appropriate words to explain the command of Chazal, "When Adar enters, we increase in joy." For a command of the Torah also provides the strength to fulfill that command in its fullest measure—matters of joy and the feelings of the heart—so that there is truly something to be joyful about, to the point that it is also felt in the heart.

Regarding what you wrote about the students who were here in connection with the farbrengen of 10 Shevat, and the question of how to bring *nachas ruach* and *taanug* [to the Rebbe]:

I must say that I did not imagine that one would need to ask about this in another country, across the border, at a time when this is the very essence of Torah and mitzvos. Especially according to what is explained and illuminated in the teachings of Chassidus, and the point that "there is no good other than Torah." More specifically, that the true good is "good for Heaven, good for people, and good that bears fruit"—that all three aspects must be present. This is further explained by the maamar "Pnimius Abba, Pnimius Atik," which teaches that the *pnimius* of *taanug* itself becomes the *pnimius* of *chochma*. This is found in the *pnimius* of Torah—in understanding and comprehension, even down to the intellect of the *nefesh habehamis*—especially since these are the "secrets of the secrets of the Torah." And according to the explanation that *taanug* is the reversal and *is'hapcha* of pain—it is precisely in this generation, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, and specifically through matters of practical action and *kabbalas ol*, that true *taanug* is relevant, until the arrival of the blessed time of simple *taanug* that is not compounded by any other matter: "Shabbos and rest for the Life of the Worlds."

Regarding the students of Tomchei Temimim in particular, the first priority is the precise observance of the yeshiva's schedule, and adding to that during the time available to them. It is understood, and it is simple, that this must be done without compromising physical health, for having a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem. There is also sufficient free time afterward to engage in *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*—not only in the "outside" of one's own self, but also in the "outside" in the literal sense. May it be His will that you explain and influence all the above to all those who asked you about this, to all those who will ask you in the future, and even to those who should have asked but were prevented from doing so by their own "assumptions and self-importance."

With blessings for good tidings in both private and communal matters alike, and as mentioned, in a manner of "increasing in joy."

## 7787

B"H, 3 Adar, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven and who is full of energy, etc.,
R' Shmuel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 29 Shevat.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Thank you, thank you for your letter, particularly regarding the results of the visits, etc. It is understood that entering into arguments is not advisable at all. Aside from the fact that it is a waste of time—since the time for your visits is limited to what must necessarily be conveyed and stated —we see tangibly that in most cases, it is unavoidable that an argument will stir up the trait of contentiousness, which causes a person to lose their composure, even regarding themselves, and even regarding their Creator, Heaven forbid. The purpose of your visits is not to argue or the like, but rather to relate and explain your perspective clearly, in ways of pleasantness and, certainly, in ways of peace. Naturally, there is difficulty in the above, in order to ensure that the impression is not left upon the questioners that you are avoiding an argument due to a weakness in your position and perspective, or that there is no answer to be given, etc.

However, after having already gained experience in your visits to various and unusual places, you can surely find a style that will leave no room at all for the aforementioned. And if an argument is even necessary, it must be—and can be—limited to a minimum.

May it be the will of Hashem that as we find ourselves in the month of Adar, when the "common people" become Jews, and all the more so regarding the "commonality" within the Jews themselves—where all boundaries are naturally broken—truth will sprout from the earth, and will break forth and flourish.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, with joy and a glad heart. And since we have been commanded to increase in joy, this commandment of the Torah is also a bestowal of strength.

## 7,588

[3 Adar, 5721]

In response to your letter from the Motzaei Shabbos of Mevarchim Chodesh Adar, in which you ask regarding your future endeavors in the near term:

Since you are currently in a period of proximity and preparation for the entire duration of your life—that is, for decades to come—and it is tangibly evident that adding a day, a month, or a year to one’s preparation increases the foundation and stability of one’s future life many times over, you should do everything in your power to continue your studies in the coming year, so that you may become as fully qualified as is necessary.

Surely, based on the love of parents for their children, your parents—may they be well—will be satisfied with this decision, and they will further encourage and assist you in every way that depends on them. The addition and the *nachas ruach* that you will cause them through this completion of your preparation will repay many times over the help, effort, and even the exertion of your parents in this matter.

I assume you are engaged in the dissemination of our Torah, the Torah of life, and its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

With blessings for good tidings.

## 7,889

B"H, 4 Adar, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following a pause, your letter of 27 Shevat was received. Regarding your questions:

a) Concerning participating in the organizations of a certain movement with which the Rabbinate at one time forbade cooperation, and how one should relate to this:

In general, since a Rav, the *mara d'asra*, rules by virtue of his *semichah*—that is, *Daas Torah*—it is understood that one who comes to the place in question must uphold that ruling (unless there are several communities, each with its own specific Rav, and no *beis din* that connects and unites them). However, it is certainly within your purview—and perhaps even your obligation—to speak with the Rabbis regarding this question and clarify with them whether the aforementioned *psak din* also applies to the specific request that was directed to you, or if it is different.

b) Regarding your question of whether to register for an examination at the university:

As is evident from your letter, the question is not whether you will study at the university, as that is being done regardless, but rather regarding the examinations. In any case, in such a matter, one must examine (estimate) the public’s reaction to this, and whether it will be interpreted as giving a *hechsher* to an undesirable matter. In this, one must specifically evaluate the situation on the ground.

The emphasis I made above—that you are not asking regarding the study itself—is understood based on the well-known attitude regarding secular studies, and *kal v'chomer* (it is understood without further elaboration).

c) Regarding the proposal to cut all the gum tissue, etc., *rachmana litzlan*:

In general, it is a strange proposal, especially since the cutting is done with the intention that new tissue will grow, etc.—that is, a matter where it is impossible to be certain (one hundred percent?) that it will indeed be fully restored. Nevertheless, since you write that you received this proposal from an expert, you should turn to another expert and learn their opinion on the matter. In a place of doubt, and in general, "sit and do nothing" is preferable.

I would be pleased to receive good news regarding the gathering you write about, and in detail. Our Sages have already informed us what "true good" is: good for Heaven, good for people, and good that produces fruit. And surely, words that come from the heart are promised to enter the heart of the listener.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
Surely you participated in the *farbrengen* of the *yom hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*—the tenth of Shevat—and took from the *hisorerus* for the entire year, which is the purpose of a Chassidishe *farbrengen*.

## 7590

7590

B"H, 4 Adar, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and your wife, may she live and be well, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Regarding your questions about the apartment: As we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in matters of an apartment in the literal sense, one should defer to the wife, the mainstay of the home, in accordance with the teaching that "the entire glory of a king's daughter is within." Although, of course, one may (in ways of pleasantness and peace) explain to her reasons and arguments that differ from her own perspective—and perhaps she will be convinced—if she is not, one must defer to her opinion.

2) Regarding the names: The reasons for changing them are not understood, as your name and the name of your wife, may she live and be well, are holy names.

3) Regarding success in your work—the holy work of education on the foundation of holiness—in these matters, and in all matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, we have been promised that "he who comes to purify himself is assisted." Therefore, your decision to engage in this with mesiras nefesh will bear fruit, meaning, additional success in the aforementioned work. This is especially true in our times, when the field of education is vital and of the utmost importance.

It is my hope that you will participate in the farbrengen for the day of the hillula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, on the tenth of Shevat, and that you will draw from this hisorerus for the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings.
