## 7,629

B"H, 19 Nissan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter was received, in which you write regarding the young man [name], may he live, and his father’s question concerning how to conduct himself with his aforementioned son.

It is understood that one should not be intimidated by what he says—that if they do not let him carry out his evil scheme, Heaven forbid, he will do [harm to himself], etc. Rather, one must explain to him that, on the contrary, if he were to carry out his evil scheme, Heaven forbid, he would be killing himself in the World to Come and also in this world, as well as the person through whom this stumbling block comes, as is well known from the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, on this matter. Instead, one must speak to the aforementioned individual with words that come from the heart, time and time again, and also ask the young man’s friends to influence him as well, each in the manner appropriate for him.

Since it happens very often that such things occur with children because the parents are not complete in their fear of Hashem and in the fulfillment of His mitzvos, this should be explained to the parents so that from now on, they will conduct their daily lives in accordance with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and in the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that just as you brought this request, so too may you share good news regarding this.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

***

**That if they do not let him carry out his evil scheme:** To marry a non-Jewish woman—he will kill himself.

**Placing the emphasis:** See Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, section 472, at the beginning: "And the Torah said..." And in Rambam, Hilchos Chametz U’Matzah, chapter 7, halacha 2: "It is a mitzvah to inform the children... as it is said..." And according to this, the language of the Mechilta (cited in the Sefer HaMitzvos of the Rambam, Positive Mitzvah 157) is understood: "I only have [this] when he has a son"—which, on the face of it, is redundant language. And this requires study.

**Jewish children:** They arouse above the matter of "For Israel is a youth, and I love him," a verse that speaks of the time of the Exodus from Egypt (see Sichos of Pesach 5704; also in the Siddur of the Arizal regarding "And here the son asks").

**From every Jew:** See Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, section 489, at the beginning.

## 7330

B"H, Isru Chag HaPesach, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
of Mosad Chinuch Oholei Torah
May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Shalom u’Bracha!

On the occasion of this annual event, I send my greetings and blessing to the esteemed askanim, supporters, and friends of Mosad Chinuch Oholei Torah, and I wish the event great success in all respects.

Coming as we do from the days of Pesach, which emphasizes and places the focus on the education of Jewish children—as is proclaimed right at the beginning of the Yom Tov, that "the Torah speaks regarding four sons," meaning the Torah speaks to and concerns itself with **every** Jewish child, from the *ben chacham* to the one who does not know how to ask—and

Finding ourselves in the days of Sefirah, which express the longing and *teshukah* of every Jew for the receiving of the Torah and the *mitzvos*,

May Hashem Yisbarach grant that the influence of the aforementioned days should bring about a strengthened interest and a new vitality among all the participants, supporters, and friends of Mosad Chinuch Oholei Torah, to carry out these instructions in practice, and with increased strength and expanded activity, to strengthen and expand the institution of education *al taharas hakodesh* and enable it to educate as many students as possible in *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and the fulfillment of *mitzvos* *be'hiddur*.

And the Ribono shel Olam will surely send His blessing, in an increased measure as well, to each and every one, in everything that they and their families *shichyu* are in need of, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and a blessing for success,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7331

B.H., 23 Nissan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the 4th of Chol Hamoed Pesach:

It is both understood and simple—and the doubt you express regarding whether you should involve yourself in the matter of... is surprising—for several reasons. First and foremost, the matter is a necessity, and you have already gained expertise in it (notwithstanding the undesirable aspects you write about).

Regarding the general content of this letter and your previous one—it is surprising that your grievances are not directed to the correct address. If you were to direct them properly, the entire foundation of your complaints would immediately vanish. Let me explain:

You have been gifted by Divine Providence with good and even superior talents, along with the energy required to bring them from potential into action. My intent is in the field of chinuch, in organizing matters, and in communal work. However, there are two points that hinder you from utilizing these talents **as much** as is required and **as much** as is possible (which, for whatever reason, you do not wish to change—and consequently, it seems to you that you also cannot): 

1. Cooperation with others (i.e., as partners, where both are interested solely in the good of the cause, and are therefore compelled to concede on various matters, and the wise will understand). 
2. That your energy—**as is usual** with the nature of many people—hinders you to a certain degree from conducting matters in an orderly and **planned** fashion. [By the way—cooperation with others is helpful for this as well, since the other person’s energy is not distracted by the first person’s, allowing for the preparation of a plan and calculation in good time.]

Despite the two points mentioned, your talents and the virtues listed previously **decisively** outweigh these two points, even though they are not entirely nullified. As you have surely witnessed in the past—i.e., in the overall result, which was good, and good not just barely, but much more than that, even though there were shortcomings, as mentioned above.

In summary: It is necessary and also good, not only in spirituality but also in physicality, that you continue in your affairs in... specifically. However, you should strive as much as possible—if not to nullify the two aforementioned points entirely, then at least to minimize them...

Regarding another point—the conclusion of your letter, where you mention speaking with... one of the elder Chassidim, who shouted at you, etc.—after the apology of that elder Chassid, along with the other elder Chassidim, I have nothing to go by other than what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: that action is the essence (and if you will, this is also an explicit Mishnah). When one makes a total of the actions of the elder Chassidim in... regarding actual accomplishment, one sees in practice: the Yeshiva they founded was steadily declining until it ceased to exist entirely [though the process was prolonged because, in the meantime, Anash arrived from Russia and acted on their own initiative, without the desire of the elder Chassidim of... etc., and in any case, the Yeshiva of... was founded], and the situation of... is surely known. The same applies to the state of the Chassidic shuls in... and their activities in spreading the wellsprings, etc. 

Consequently, it is no wonder that they advise others to conduct themselves in the aforementioned manner. However, those who heed their advice can look at the results of this method of the elder Chassidim regarding actual accomplishment, and estimate with certainty what the results would be in the present in **all** Chabad matters if, **G-d forbid**, one were to listen to their aforementioned instruction. It is a wonder—that although in general it is difficult for the aforementioned individuals to agree among themselves on any point, when it comes to the method of "sit and do nothing" (*shev v'al taaseh adif*), they are all of one mouth and one heart, becoming a single union. The wise will understand regarding this painful and alarming matter... It is understood and simple that it is in your hands and within your authority to show these lines to those who advise you and others like you to adopt the method of "sit and do nothing," etc.

Knowing your character, there is room to say that your first reaction upon reading my letter will not be the one I intended—to strive for **increased** activity—but rather the reaction in the style of our Sages: "What do I have to do with this trouble?" 

Or—which is also not desirable to a **great** degree—a sense of discouragement. Therefore, I repeat what I wrote in the first lines of this letter: you are gifted with exceptional energy and superior talents, and **you can and it is good in both spirituality and physicality**, and it is necessary and mandatory that you utilize them to their fullest. It goes without saying that the priority in this is for Chabad matters, especially since, as I have written **many** times—they influence and pour (*gissen*) success into all Chabad matters in an **unimaginable** way. However, what is required is actions, not just thoughts, and not debates and discussions in meetings whose conclusion is "sit and do nothing is better, and I have saved my own soul, for I have expressed my opinion," but rather actual, tangible actions, and actions in a broad manner, as instructed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe...

May it be G-d's will that you read and hear (*derheren*) this letter according to its **true** content and intent—that it should effect an elevation of spirit in both spirituality and physicality, and that you **increase** your activities out of joy and a good heart.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned, and as stated above, with joy,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7332

B"H, 28 Nissan, Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

## 7333

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday.

Regarding what was written in my previous letter concerning the distinction according to Shulchan Aruch, etc., it was not my intention to completely rule out prostate surgery if an expert physician advises it. Rather, I intended to point out the distinction in the methods of surgery, as there are physicians who do not sever the duct at all.

Regarding this, I cited what is transcribed in *Otzar HaPoskim*, Volume 1 [Second Edition with additions, Jerusalem 5715].

2) Even among those who do sever it—many perform this only after the main part of the surgery has been completed, at which point it is already necessary in practice [in their opinion, at least] to prevent complications, as opposed to when they begin with the severance.

And this is easy to understand.

I would also add that there are bladder surgeries where, for that same reason of preventing complications, they interrupt and sever, etc., in close proximity to the surgical site, and sometimes even in places that require deliberation according to the Shulchan Aruch. This is why I raised the point, even though in your letter, only the latter surgery was mentioned. I ask for your forgiveness for the additional comment.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in good health.

## 7,334

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 5 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the eve of Rosh Chodesh Iyar and the one preceding it.

Regarding the subject of this week’s parsha: "If a woman conceives and gives birth to a male" (*Vayikra 12:2*). The interpretation of the Alter Rebbe is well-known: this alludes to the *avodah* of the Creator, that when we engage in *is'arusa d'lesata*—the *avodah* of *Knesses Yisrael*, the Jewish people—then "she gives birth to a male," something of permanence.

May it be the will of Hashem that as we enter the era of the Geulah, it will be as stated regarding the redemption of the Jewish people: that Hashem sets up for them (arousing them to the truth, that the *yetzer hara* which was placed by Hashem to test man, is called) a "king" (for the body is a "small city," and he issues decrees upon it) whose decrees are harsh (like a high and difficult mountain) like Haman (who sought to destroy and kill **b'guf u'b'nefesh**, for he, the *yetzer hara*, is the Angel of Death). And the Jewish people perform *teshuvah* (in a single hour and a single moment, and with joy) and He returns them to the *mutav* (the source of good), and immediately they are redeemed—a redemption after which there is no exile, for it will be true and complete, a "song" (*shir*) in the masculine form.

With blessings for good tidings in all matters regarding which you write, both the general and the specific.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7235

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the Committee of the Nachlas Binyamin Synagogue in Tel Aviv, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—
May Hashem protect them and may they live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 12 Nissan, which was received in due course, in which you write the reasons for both sides regarding the question of merging the two synagogues on Nachlas Binyamin Street and Rav Kook Street, and ask for my opinion on this.

Now, as in many matters, there is the "ideal" type and the "feasible" type. Since everyone must judge their fellow favorably, it is possible—perhaps—that the "ideal" type mentioned below will also be within the realm of the feasible, and therefore I will write about it as well.

1) The best approach is that you recruit from among Anash in Tel Aviv several energetic and active individuals who will take upon themselves—some of them the development of one synagogue, and some of them the development of the second synagogue. But, of course, this should not be done through holding meetings among themselves and debating in the realm of theory, but rather through concrete actions to increase the number of congregants, the classes being taught in each of the synagogues, etc. And all the more so—a fortiori—if during this time several new synagogues have been established, then certainly those that have existed for a long time have the **full** potential for development. Especially since the Rebbe, my father-in-law, Nasi Yisroel, constantly encourages the success of activities of this nature. And here, too, the emphasis is on *actions*, in accordance with the adage: "One action is better than a thousand sighs." It is certain that both synagogues have the right to exist—a true existence, meaning a living existence, the essence of which is growth and development in both quantity and quality.

2) In the event that, based on the conduct until now, no one will involve themselves in establishing the synagogues for whatever reason, and consequently there is a concern that the development of matters will continue in the direction it has until now—i.e., that the first possibility, for the aforementioned reasons, will not materialize—then at the very least, you must meet with the representatives of the second synagogue and deliberate on what can be done to achieve at least a partial rescue.

3) That two minyanim should daven, one early and one after it—I do not see any deficiency or negative aspect in this, as I wrote to Mr. Shmerling, may he live, some time ago in detail.

Likewise, I do not see any negative aspect if some of the congregants are from our Sephardic brethren, provided that the *nusach* of the davening remains the Chabad *nusach*, the *nusach* of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

#### ***7235***

**In accordance with the adage:** See also above, Vol. 18, Letter 6552, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 7336

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn

Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished scholar, etc., our teacher Rabbi Yitzchak Yehuda
May he live

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write the suggestion that I should make a change, etc.

It is understood according to the halachic ruling of our Sages (Shabbos 10b): "A person should never differentiate [among his children],"—that even in one's initial thought, such a suggestion should not exist, and this statement of our Sages is brought as a halachic ruling in the Rambam, etc.

The magnitude of the consequences of making a distinction is understood from the words of the Tosafos there (and especially according to the Shelah, etc.). And in the very event from which they derived that one should not differentiate, there were the strongest possible reasons for doing so, as our Sages say regarding the verse "because he was a son of his old age," and regarding the verse "these are the generations of Yaakov, Yosef"—specifically Yosef. This was before the aforementioned commandment of our Sages, and despite all this, etc., and certainly all the more so after the commandment.

Furthermore, and this is also essential: that all of them (his peers) are beloved, all of them, etc. See also the holy Tanya, beginning of Chapter 32, that all of them are equal, etc. And I ask for your forgiveness for not accepting the suggestion.

In contemplating and searching for the reason for this writing, even though the matter is simple as stated, behold—there is no one among us who knows why. Perhaps this is the point: to provide an opportunity for me to reiterate the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who emphasized and repeated at every opportunity the great necessity to set times for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. Especially in these final days of our exile, which is a double and redoubled darkness, the necessity for the dissemination of the wellsprings outward is all the greater, for then the Master, the King Moshiach, will come. As is known, the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov regarding this, and surely for one such as you, elaboration is superfluous.

With respect and blessings.

Regarding the superiority of Yosef over the tribes, one should note the words of our Alter Rebbe on this. And these are his holy words: "For there the tribes ascended, etc., but regarding Yosef it is written 'And Yosef was brought down,' etc., and this is why they did not recognize him at all, since there is no comparison between them at all, for that which is an ascent for them is a descent for him, etc." (Torah Or, Additions to Parshas Vayechi, 284, in the discourse entitled *Lehavin Shoresh*. See there).

[12 Iyar, 5721]

...for the improvement of his health and the success of the medical treatment to which he has agreed. In any case, the doctor with whom he consulted surely explained that a strong sense of bitachon in Hashem—the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders—increases peace of mind and reduces anxiety, and will certainly contribute to the improvement of health and added success in the medical treatment. And if, in general, Chazal have informed us that the mind naturally rules over the heart, how much more so is this true after contemplating the words of our Torah, the Torah of life: "Hashem is with me, I will not fear; Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack," and especially according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the concept of hashgacha pratis.

In general, one should follow the instructions of a specialist doctor...

## 7379

B"H, Lag B'Omer, the Hillula of Rashbi, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 9th of Iyar.

As we stand on the day of the Hillula of Rashbi—whose mission and activity were to draw down the inner dimension of the Torah into the conditions [of this world], etc.—and even that which is inherently hidden and not subject to revelation, as explained in Chassidic thought; and furthermore, he opened the channel of influence for this, initially in his own generation, to the extent that even children revealed the secrets of the Torah.

And especially after this—as Rashbi himself stated—when we draw closer to the days of Moshiach, even the children of the world are destined to find the hidden matters of wisdom.

This is therefore a propitious time for awakening and for increased courage in the revelation and dissemination of the inner dimension of the Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the fountains of Chassidus and its teachings.

For on the day of his Hillula, there shines within him the aspect of the ultimate perfection of his soul, which had its root in the aspect of Moshe and the aspect of Moshiach. And these days are "remembered" and "enacted" (the influences and bestowals are brought down), as is known from the Arizal’s interpretation of the verse.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that each person act in this regard according to their capacity, and draw from this awakening and increase throughout the entire year, and with joy.

For in this, too, the day of the Hillula of Rashbi is unique—as is explained in many places—that it is not like any other day, etc., but on the contrary, it must be observed with joy.

With blessings for good tidings, in general and in particular.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7440

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all the members of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad everywhere,
And to the participants in the sixth annual convention in particular, may Hashem grant them life:

Blessings and peace!

The annual convention of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad is scheduled this year for the days immediately following Lag B'Omer—the Hillula (the yahrtzeit) of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai—and it will surely be imbued with his influence. Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai stood out among the greatest Tannaim for having studied and revealed **the satim u’pnimius haTorah**—the hidden and inner light and content of Torah—through the Zohar, Tikkunei Zohar, and so on.

Pnimius haTorah is connected to **pnimius Yisrael**—the inwardness of a Jew, of the Jewish neshamah—and it creates the inner connection of a Jew with Elokus, as Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai states in the Zohar and as is explained at length in Chassidus Chabad.

The pnimius of a Jew—the *pintale Yid*—is complete in all Jews, regardless of their external state or external circumstances. However, one must awaken this *pintale Yid*, both within oneself and in all those around one, so that the inner dimension is revealed, influences, and completely dominates the external dimension, down to all the details of daily life. This is one of the primary tasks of Chassidim in general, and of Chassidei Chabad in particular.

* * *

In the realization of this task, N’shei U’Bnos Chabad occupy a very important place. For Divine Providence has endowed Jewish women with special qualities and capabilities that can and must be utilized for this purpose.

The woman is the **akeres habayis** and is responsible for the inner light and Jewish warmth of the home, so that the Jewish home may be protected from the winds alien and hostile to Yiddishkeit that blow in the outside world.

Furthermore, a woman is endowed with a greater and more expressive measure of feelings and heart, and she is therefore suited to awaken and elicit the innate inner feelings of ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael.

* * *

The revelation of pnimius until the pnimius dominates the external and reaches into daily life brings the reward of *middah k’neged middah* (measure for measure)—that the inner and hidden aspect of Divine Providence, which is goodness itself, should be revealed down into all the needs of daily life—health, parnassah, and nachas from children—so that the hidden good may descend into *tov hanir'eh v'hanigleh* (good that is visible and revealed).

With blessings that the convention and all the members everywhere fulfill their tasks with great success, with joy and a glad heart.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7441

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Yehoshua, may he live:

After all, a female infant is considered as if she is already circumcised (immediately upon her birth). As for what is written in the sefer *Taamei HaMinhagim* (p. 396) regarding a rumor to wait five days—we are not responsible for such rumors, etc.

With blessings for mazal tov.

## 7,742

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of interruptions, your letter of 17 Iyar was received. I understand the surprise regarding the tone of your writing, implying that a shidduch with the daughters of our Sephardic brethren is, Heaven forbid, a "lowering of status." This is a matter that requires reflection.

2) Regarding the proposal of a shidduch for your son, may he live and be well—even though his older brother is not yet engaged, the older brother states that he does not mind this and asks for my opinion on the matter.

There are various opinions among the Acharonim regarding this. When one has reached the age of eighteen, there is no strict adherence to the aforementioned order of precedence, especially in a case such as this, where the older brother grants his full and complete consent. Furthermore, there is room to say—and it is highly probable—that this very act will serve as a *segulah* to hasten the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam in finding a suitable shidduch for the older brother as well.

It is a great wonder that you do not mention your activities in *hafatzas hama'ayanos*. I am certain that you will fill this in your next letter, with the necessary details. Especially since activities in this area also add to and hasten the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam in all that is needed, and *kal v'chomer*.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 7443

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn

Agudas Shochtim, Tel Aviv-Yafo
May Hashem preserve them and keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, confirming receipt of my letter and the *pidyon nefesh* by a member of your association.

It is my firm hope that since the time of your aforementioned letter, you have added in holiness and ascended in holiness—that is to say, an increase not only in quantity but also in quality, which is the true essence of an increase.

This is especially true in light of what is explained in many places, including the words of our Rebbe HaZaken and his grandson, the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, regarding *shochtim* and their role in *yiras shamayim*.

I take this opportunity, at this auspicious time as we stand before the *Shabbos Mevarchim* of the third month—in which the triple Torah was given to the triple nation—to express my blessings to each and every one of you, in the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness (*pnimiyus*).

With respect and blessing,

P.S.

Allow me to add a thought in a lighter vein (*derech tzahus*).

One can connect the concept of *Matan Torah* and *shechitah* based on one of the reasons given for eating dairy foods on the festival of Shavuos: that upon the giving of the Torah, the Jewish people were commanded regarding *shechitah*. Since everyone agrees that the Torah was given on *Shabbos*, and one does not perform *shechitah* on *Shabbos*, they were compelled to eat dairy foods, as brought in the *sefarim*.

And even though, on the face of it, they practiced *shechitah* even before this, as our Sages of blessed memory state regarding the verse, "Slaughter a slaughter and prepare" (*Chullin* 91a; and in the *Midrash* brought in *Tzror HaMor*, which derives the five *halachos* of *shechitah* from this), it is understood simply that the Jewish people before *Matan Torah* were not in the category of those subject to the *shechitah* that followed *Matan Torah*.

## 744

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Lag B'Omer:

1) You ask if there are commentaries on the Tanya.

Systematic commentaries, page by page, do not currently exist, except that some years ago the Tanya was translated into Yiddish, and now an English translation is being prepared for print. This is in addition to commentaries on various sections that have been mimeographed and are found among Chabad Chassidim and their supporters.

2) You ask where in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) you should settle after completing your current studies.

Since, according to your letter, you will finish in a year and a half, it is still too early to decide this matter, as conditions in our Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established) change, particularly regarding matters of livelihood in the manner you describe.

My hope is strong—consistent with your writing—that since you have become acquainted with the matters of Chabad and have met with its people, you are interested in studying its Torah. If, as you write, you find the Tanya difficult to understand, begin with the third part (Iggeres HaTeshuvah), then the second part, and after that study *Kuntres Uma'ayan*. The main thing is to discuss the matters you are studying with those who have already studied this Torah, for Torah is acquired through the bonding of friends and the *pilpul* of students. Regarding this, it is said: "If you have labored and not found, do not believe."

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 7245

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write:

1) There is a bochur who, despite being in a religious setting, does not adapt to a religious lifestyle; there is no discernible feeling of love for matters of Torah and mitzvos, etc.

Since our Sages have said that words coming from the heart enter the heart, surely speaking with the bochur in a manner of drawing him close—rather than in a manner of argument, but rather by offering suggestions—will certainly influence him. However, not every person is the same, and there are those to whom one must speak several times before the effect becomes visible to the physical eye and in practical action; yet, surely you will eventually succeed. Among the active suggestions regarding this is to make him a leader (for those younger than him in years) in matters of religion, the study of Torah, and the fulfillment of mitzvos. The responsibility he feels in this will motivate him and lead him to delve deeper into the subject, even to the point of explaining it to those placed under his guidance. Naturally, there must be supervision in this so that he does not err in his interpretation of the matters, etc.

2) Is every single man and woman of Bnei Yisrael capable and able to live their lives in accordance with the instructions of our Torah?

Certainly, this is so. It is also understood through the healthy logic of anyone who believes in the living G-d: since the Giver of the Torah and the Mitzvah commands every single man and woman of Bnei Yisrael—and as is well known, the precision that the giving of the Torah began in the singular form, specifically "Anochi Hashem Elokecha" (and not "Elokeichem"), to teach that the entire Torah and all its mitzvos were given to each and every individual—surely Hashem would not demand of a person matters that are beyond their strength. On the contrary, **prior** to the commandment, the ability and full possibility to fulfill the commandment were granted. Furthermore, this is to be done with joy and a glad heart, for that is how study and fulfillment must be, as is explained in several places. However, for a reason known to the Creator of man, free choice was given to each and every one of Bnei Yisrael, and Hashem desired that through free choice, one should choose the path of good and righteousness, as it is written, "See, I have set before you... and you shall choose life," and we are promised, "You have labored and you have found."

It is my hope that you have a fixed time for studying the teachings of Chassidus in addition to your study of the revealed Torah, and may it be His will that it be in a manner where the study leads to action.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 7,447

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn.

...And regarding your writing that this leads to conflicts with [Name] and his family—it is a **clear** ruling in our holy Torah that one who refuses to have his case adjudicated before the *mara d’asra* (at the very least through *zeh b’zeh*) is acting and working **against** the Torah, which is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*—for He and His wisdom are one. Consequently, he is causing damage to himself, his household, and all those who assist him—damage not only in the *Olam HaBa*, but also in this world, in a physical sense. It is only that the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is a merciful Father, extends His patience for a time, perhaps in the end he will do *teshuvah* through kindness and mercy and return from his rebellion against Hashem. From this, it is also understood that anyone who has a conflict with [Name] regarding the above is, in fact, his true friend, and anyone who assists [Name] is a companion to [Name]’s *yetzer hara*, whose craft it is to incite him to fight against the Torah and its *mitzvos*.

## 7849

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5721
Brooklyn

To the participants of the annual raffle for a trip in the coming month of Tishrei, which took place in Kfar Chabad, founded and directed by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, where Hashem commanded the blessing of life upon them—may they live.

Shalom u’vracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the list of participants in the raffle, along with the notification regarding the raffle and the winner of the drawing.

May it be Hashem’s will, as has been stated previously, that the winner, through his trip, will represent all the participants and bring them merit in every respect, both in quantity and in quality.

This is especially true given the significance of a *goral* (raffle/lot) when conducted properly, as explained in the Tanya, *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of Chapter 7, and as the verse explicitly states: "The lot is cast into the lap, but the whole judgment thereof is of Hashem" (Mishlei 16:33).

And according to the story told by the early Chassidim in the name of the great Chassid, tzaddik, and gaon, Rabbi Hillel of Paritch, that all the matters and *hiddurim* (beautifications) he performed were done so that "a *vort* (word) of Chassidus would settle better within him."

May it be Hashem’s will that regarding this as well—in addition to the matters of the trip—this essential element will also be added, and that for all the participants, and indeed for all the *Temimim* and *Anash* at large, "a *vort* of Chassidus will settle" in a manner of understanding that leads to *kein* (action). And furthermore—and in our times, this is also essential—they should not be satisfied at all with just "a *vort*," for "he who has a *maneh* (one hundred) wants two hundred," etc.

It is understood and simple that one should not wait for the benefits of the aforementioned until the trip actually takes place, for the beginning must be from the moment of the raffle and the decision. And this is clear.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above, and in the words of our Rebbe, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7849***

**In the annual raffle:** See also above, Vol. 17, Letter 6118.

**Story... of Paritch:** See also above, Vol. 17, Letter 6115, and the references in the notes there.

## 7550

[Iyar 5721]

However, through them it is not necessarily implied that nourishment is drawn (from Avraham, as it were) to the *chitzonim*—unlike Yishmael, regarding whom it was said, "If only Yishmael might live before You." Similarly, Yitzchak blessed Esav (and see *Torah Or*, *maamar* beginning *Anochi Magen*).

#### ***7550***

This letter is to R. Avraham Zusha Ziskind, and was written on the margin of his letter dated the 1st of the week of *Taharoh* (additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 18, 7355, and the references in the notes there).

**However, through them:** Regarding his question: In *Toras Shmuel* 5626, *maamar* beginning *Kol Holeich Al Gachon* (p. 72), it explains the difference between the line of the right and *Chesed* versus the *Gevuros*; that from the *Gevuros*, through the proliferation of *hishtalshelus*, there can be some nourishment, etc., and therefore from Yitzchak came Esav, even after he was circumcised, but from *Chasadim* there cannot be nourishment. And as for the fact that from Avraham came Yishmael, that was before he was circumcised. This requires further study, for there are the children of Keturah, and they are *pesoles* (refuse), especially Midian, as explained in *Kuntres Hechalotzu*, and they were born after he was circumcised.

**At the beginning of the third month:** This is as if all seven weeks have been completed, and Yisrael are prepared and standing to receive the Torah (*Torah Or* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Yisro*, *maamar* beginning *B'Chodesh HaShlishi*. And see the supplement there). And in *Pesikta d'Rav Kahana*, *Piska B'Chodesh HaShlishi*: "On this day they came to the wilderness of Sinai," and so it says, "This day Hashem your G-d commands you to perform, etc."

**Third month:** *Shabbos* 88a. And see R. Nissim Gaon there (from *Midrash Tanchuma*).

## 7,351

7,351

*[Iyar 5721]*

Regarding your questions: 

a) It is obvious that you are doing a good deed by printing the maamarim and sichos of our Rebbes, and the merit of the many depends upon you. 

b) As for leading the davening (yored lifnei hateivah) on the Shabbos before a yahrtzeit (during Mussaf and the like) — this is not our custom. If someone insists on doing so, where would we derive such a practice? (One could point out the Gemara in Sukkah 32b, bottom: "Since it has gone out..." etc.). However, to stir up controversy over this or similar matters is not merely contrary to custom, but a prohibition according to the Torah, and "Torah scholars increase peace."

## 7592

7592

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5721

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 26th of Iyar and the *pidyon nefesh* that was read at the holy gravesite.

As we stand at the beginning of the third month, in which the Merciful One gave the threefold Torah to the threefold people,

May it be His will that each and every one among the entirety of Israel will act and bring good tidings in all three things upon which the world (in its literal sense, and the "small world"—which is man) stands: Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*.

And may this draw down and add to the blessing of the Merciful One in all the needs of "man"—for you are called "man"—which are divided into three categories: children, life, and ample sustenance.

The central point of all the above is the matter of Torah and its reception. In the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe:

The reception of the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With blessings for the holiday and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your note—based on what is explained in the table of contents for *Nitzavim*, the reason for the valuations (*arachin*) is according to the years and not according to the levels—how does this align with the law regarding a non-Jew who is valued?

For it is explained there that one must (in the case of a Jew) value **oneself** first, in accordance with the teaching of the Alter Rebbe—from which it is understood that the valuation will be the **lowest possible** (for a person knows his own value)—and also for a non-Jew, the sum is the same, since there is nothing lower than that. This can be reconciled in *avodah*—based on the precision of the Alter Rebbe in *Tanya Kaddisha*, beginning of Chapter 30, where he cites the version "the man" (*ha'adam*—which includes even a non-Jew) and not "man" (*adam*). And this is clear.

#### ***7592***

A similar version was sent to several people. The letter is printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1306, and the addition in Vol. 2, p. 698.

**Called "man":** After the Giving of the Torah (*Tosafos*, *Niddah* 70b).

**In three categories:** See *Tikkunei Zohar Chadash* (103d): The mystery of the three names Y-H-V, which are threefold, and from them come children, life, and sustenance.

**Children, life, and sustenance:** Children from *Da'as* (which is drawn through the spinal cord), life from *Chochma*, sustenance from *Binah* (*Me'orei Ohr* 2, 67; cited in *Biurei HaZohar* by the Tzemach Tzedek [not yet printed at the time (see *Biurei HaZohar*, Vol. 1, p. 44 and onwards)] on *Parshas Vayeira*).

And so it is in *Tikkunei Zohar*, Introduction 15, 272b. It has already been noted that this requires study from *Likkutei Torah* by the Arizal, *Parshas Toldos*, and from *Likkutei HaShas*, *Berachos*. See also *Biurei HaZohar*, end of *Parshas Vayeira*.

**In the table of contents for *Nitzavim*:** *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 401.

## 7350

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a delay, your letter from 17 Iyar was received. I understand the surprise regarding what you wrote about weakness, etc., especially during the time of Sefiras HaOmer, the essence of which is "gathering bit by bit, day by day" (as is known, the precision that we do not say "second day," but rather "two days," for even the first day must be in its completeness). Like all mitzvos, the essence of this mitzvah is to draw its content into the entire year, and this is well understood. Since the Ribono shel Olam does not deal unjustly with His creations, it is certainly within a person’s strength and ability.

It is surprising and distressing—even though it is your way not to mention your activities regarding shidduchim—that this is the case, for there is an absolute command regarding this in our Torah, the Torah of life. Furthermore, there is an additional point beyond the above: this is a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that as we stand at the beginning of the third month, the commencement of Matan Torah (see Torah Or, the maamar beginning *B'Chodesh HaShlishi*, and the additions to Torah Or there), there will be an increase, with Siyata Dishmaya, in the aforementioned matters and in the matters you write about in your letter that require Siyata Dishmaya. May that assistance immediately be utilized for the matter of shidduchim as well, and may it ultimately be brought to fruition and completion in a good and auspicious hour.

With blessings for good tidings, and in the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## Z'terno

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of pauses, your letter of 26 Iyar, along with its enclosure, was received.

It is understood that in a case such as this, one must act according to the instructions of the specialist physician about whom you write. After all, it is also for the benefit of your daughter, tichyeh, as it is certain that at home she cannot receive all the matters and care possible in the environment the physician recommends. However, first, one must ascertain more details about the institution, and the main thing is to establish connections with the physician at the institution so that they can know what is being done with her, and most importantly, to be certain that they will treat her with the proper attention, and not in a routine manner, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, that the action on your part will be a vessel to receive the blessing from above, as it is written: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do."

Perhaps, if you have not clarified this until now, it is worth pointing out to the specialist physician regarding the state of her menstrual cycle; for if it is not in order, surely an improvement in this situation will improve her condition in general. Also, ask him whether in such a case there is room for supplements of the "amino acid" type, and regarding her condition, [ask about] treatment through shock therapy and the like.

It is surprising—especially in light of the reports received regarding your participation in the activities of disseminating the wellsprings [of Chassidus] and your success in this—that you do not mention anything in the aforementioned area. Based on the wonderment of our Sages regarding the magnitude of a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others (Moed Katan, end of 9a), seemingly you should have concentrated on the circles of the... party, and especially regarding the youth and young people within it. This is particularly true given what Mr.... shlita told me, that there is an attitude there that is sympathetic to religion and its matters, and even more than just sympathetic. After all, even in such a case, the test is the actual deed; I mean that in your meeting with them, you should propose a practical program for the fulfillment of practical mitzvos in reality, and with words that come from the heart.

As we stand on the eve of the time of the Giving of our Torah—the one Torah that unites the physical and the spiritual, the general and the particular—may it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings in the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good tidings.

## 7,557

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Iyar, in which you write regarding the idea of traveling here to meet, etc., and ask for my opinion on the matter:

In general, the matter does not seem appropriate to me, for several reasons. First and foremost, our Torah—Torah Chaim—limits and sets specific conditions for when one wishes to travel from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) to Chutz LaAretz. From this alone, it is understood that even if those conditions are met, it is still not a simple matter. When one adds to this the increase of debts—in other words, the fact that one would need an unnatural approach to fulfill this desire—it makes the matter more complicated.

And since, in spiritual matters, the physical distance is no obstacle [though it is understood that seeing with physical eyes is more satisfying],

May Hashem bless you that for long, good days and years, you should have true nachas—which is to say, Yiddishe Chassidishe nachas—from your children and grandchildren (may they live and be well), both those who are in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and those who are in Chutz LaAretz, in all respects.

At a time of favor, I will mention you and all those you write about at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

With blessings for a happy holiday and for good tidings.

## 7259

B"H, Yemei HaHagbalah, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Yosef, may he live, known as Dr. Burg

Greetings and blessings!

Approaching the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is arriving for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby send you my blessing for a joyous holiday, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:

To receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With respect and blessing.

P.S.

Regarding the matters of the day, and especially knowing that you appreciate wit, rhetoric, and wordplay: As many of our Jewish brethren are entering the "cauldron" of elections, and in accordance with the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that from everything a person sees or hears, he must learn a lesson in his avodah to his Creator—may it be His will that they learn a *kal v'chomer* (an a fortiori argument) from these elections: If a voter, who is merely flesh and blood, is nevertheless pursued by the candidate with heart and soul to find favor in his eyes—to the point that no effort or exertion, whether physical or spiritual, is too difficult for him, and he finds no taste in his food and his sleep flees from his eyes, all so that he may be elected in practice—how much more so regarding the One who chooses His people Israel (especially when He does so) with love, as was the case at the time of the giving of the Torah. Is it not fitting that one should conduct himself in the manner described, and more, to find favor in the eyes of the Chooser and to be truly chosen? Furthermore, while regarding a human voter, the candidate must reward the voter (provided, of course, that the promises made during the elections are kept, for even the Jewish people are presumed to be righteous, that their mouth and heart are one); this is not the case regarding the One who chooses His people Israel with love—for He is the Giver, and the one chosen is the recipient. And that which the chosen one must give to the Chooser—the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos—is itself for the benefit of the chosen one.

**Dr. Burg:** Additional letters to him—see Vol. 17, 6173, and the references in the notes there.

## 7662

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Mr. Moshe, shichye,
Shalom u’vrachah!

After a long interval, I received your letter of 4 Sivan, in which you write regarding the passing of your mother, a"h.

May it be the will of Hashem that from here on you know no further sorrow, chas v’shalom, and that you only hear good news in a revealed and manifest way.

Regarding what you wrote about the text for the matzeivah: It is surely known to you that Chazal state that the text must correspond to reality. This is especially true since the matter concerns a neshamah that has ascended to the World of Truth. In particular, since you write that she possessed many virtues, there are many praises that can be written about her that correspond to reality; those who knew her and the history of her life should compose the text.

However, in my opinion—and as I have answered several others who have asked regarding this—one should also mention in the text the names of our Rebbes, the Nesi’ei Yisrael. Since you write that your mother, a"h, was a supporter of Chabad institutions, this is the way to mention and specify the name of the Nasi, "founder of the institution [name of institution]," which she supported.

My intention in saying this—the benefit of mentioning the name of a tzaddik and Nasi—is based on the instruction of Chazal in many places, and specifically according to what is explained in the books of Kabbalah and elucidated in the books of Chassidus, that the name is what connects the neshamah with the body.

It draws from the neshamah, which is eternal, into the physical matters here below. When one mentions the name of a tzaddik and Nasi, it awakens the neshamah of the one who bears the name, and its arousal acts also below—especially when speaking of a Nasi of Israel, whose role and activity in life in this world was for the benefit of the many and for the guidance of the many. Certainly, for someone like you, there is no need to elaborate on this.

I conclude as I began, that you should report good news regarding your personal affairs and also regarding your activities in spreading traditional Judaism wherever your hand can reach.

With respect,

P.S.
I met with Mr. L. Eliav, shichye, who I believe is in charge of the development of the region that includes the Dead Sea and its surroundings. I am interested to know if you have met with him and if you have drawn closer to one another. When two of the Bnei Yisrael meet together, one should hope for an increase of light in the world (this "small world," which is the person himself, and in the world in the literal sense).

In the style of the verse, "Then they that feared Hashem spoke one with another" regarding matters of fear of Heaven.

#### ***7662***

**And as I have answered:** See also above, letter 7544, and the references in the notes there.

## 7663

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community, R' Moshe Tuvia HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the conclusion of the Yom Tov of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, in which you write about the arrangements during the days of the festival.

May it be G-d’s will that you draw from that inspiration for the entire year. Beyond the fact that, in general, all the matters of the Yomim Tovim are intended to provide inspiration for the entire year, there is an additional point regarding the time of the giving of our Torah: that every single day, one must be "new" [even though the statement of our Sages is sometimes cited as "like new"—with the *kaf* of comparison—see Rashi on Devarim 26:16: "May they be new in your eyes every day"].

It can be said that this depends on the state of a person’s *avodah* to his Creator; sometimes he is in an ascent, and sometimes, etc., where even then, at the very least, they must be "like new." But the hoped-for goal and the desire is that they be "new" in the literal sense, and this is understood.

Your letter was received, and this response is being written during the days of *tashlumin* (the makeup days) for the time of the giving of our Torah. Even in this time and in exile, this matter is established and engraved as a practical reality, as per the words of our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah), and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah), that we do not say *Tachanun* until the 12th of the month of Sivan, and this applies to everyone.

At a time of favor, please mention all those you write about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be G-d’s will that just as you brought the request, you should also bring good tidings regarding this, as well as regarding your holy activities in spreading the holy Torah and its *mitzvos* wherever your hand can reach.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

...Regarding your desire to add to your study of Tanya a study that is not from Chabad seforim (in the narrow sense) but is relevant to it—study the *Sefer Shelah* (and it is understood that this does not necessarily have to be in order, and you may skip around, and the like).

## 7664

[10 Sivan, 5721]

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 8 Sivan.

It is understandable that I read with the greatest astonishment a theory so strange, even as a mere passing thought, that one of your sons—may he live—would leave a framework saturated with Torah, the words of the living G-d, and its matters, to exchange it for a group managed by those who negate the aforementioned, etc., etc.

For surely, in our day, it is impossible to say that the Torah of Chassidus, its content, and its guidance are unknown to any circle of Torah scholars. And such knowledge does not leave the person who possesses it in a neutral state, since the Torah of Chassidus demands not only an inclination toward it, but also action. One can either accept it or reject it. At the very most, one could attempt to ignore the entire issue, but those whom you mention do not follow a policy of ignoring it (for whatever reason). On the contrary, it is their intention to instruct clearly on these matters.

And this is obvious.

Everything stated above remains in full force—even if we were not speaking of a son of Anash, and even if he were not of the caliber of talents and knowledge of your son—may he live—and especially [given his background], etc. There are **many** students like him with whom he can connect, as I recognize from their letters and also from outside information. It is understood that as a *chavrusa*, it is appropriate that there be compatibility not only in knowledge and talents, but also in character traits, etc. Therefore, you should consult with those who know the *avreichim*, and from among them, choose those who are presumed to be the most suitable. May Hashem grant them success.

It is highly probable that the state of mind of your son—may he live—about which you write, is not at all related to the matters you mention, but rather stems from the change of atmosphere, etc., from being here to Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

With a blessing that together with her husband, the Rav—may he live—you will raise all your children—may they live—in a manner appropriate to the will of our Rebbeim, and that you will derive from them true *nachas*—that is, Chassidishe *nachas*—in every respect.

## 7659

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied in communal needs, R' Yechezkel Yissachar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of 8 Sivan and the one preceding it. May Hashem Yisbarach help you to be able to report good news regarding both the general and personal matters that go hand in hand. May you also receive Hashem’s blessing in your personal affairs, with added measure, through your involvement in the communal matters that you and your colleagues, may they live, have merited to perform for the establishment and development of the village, founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael. At his holy resting place, you are remembered from time to time, together with all the activists of the village and those who seek its welfare, for great success in the affairs of the village and great success in your personal matters. May it be His will that all of this should be accomplished in ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, yet with the appropriate vigor.

We are currently in the days of *tashlumin* for the time of the giving of our Torah, whose ways are ways of pleasantness and all its paths are peace, and which brings peace to the world. At the same time, it is a *Toras Emes*—it reveals the truth in every thing and illuminates it (*Torah*—*Ohr*), and also provides precise instructions on how to fulfill them in their entirety, as they ought to be (*Torah* from the root *hora'ah*, instruction). Regarding both of these aspects, *Toras HaChassidus* explains at length that this is the wisdom and will of the Hakadosh Baruch Hu.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 7660

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer Steinman,

Greetings and blessings!

I have received news of you through Rabbi Chanoch Glitzenstein, and I was pleased to hear that you are already at home and preparing to continue your literary work, specifically in its inner dimension: spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus.

Since the core of Chassidus is the avodah of Hashem with joy and gladness of heart—which is, in fact, a clear halachic ruling in the Rambam, Hilchos Lulav (at the end), and is based on a full verse in Scripture as cited by the Rambam there—may it be Hashem’s will that you continue your aforementioned work with true joy. This means that the body, too, should not be a distraction; on the contrary, it should participate in the joy as well.

This is also one of the themes of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, from which we continue. In the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his Shulchan Aruch, Siman 494, Seif 18: "On the day the Torah was given, one must eat and rejoice, to show that the day the Torah was given is pleasant and acceptable to Yisrael."

Enclosed is a copy of a general letter and sicha which I hope will be of interest to you.

With blessings for proper health and good tidings, and with respect,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7667

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 12 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated Isru Chag.

As we stand at the conclusion and final seal of the *tashlumin* (days of completion) of Atzeres—the time of the giving of our Torah—and as it is known that the *tashlumin* of Shavuos extend through the 12th of the month inclusive, it can be said that these *tashlumin* possess a superiority over the *tashlumin* of Pesach and Sukkos. In those festivals, the completion takes place on days that are themselves festival days. Shavuos, however, adds a greater power: even on days that are in their own right entirely mundane, we perform and complete the matters of goodness and holiness of the day of Atzeres.

According to the instruction of the Alter Rebbe in his Siddur, that even in the Diaspora and even at this time we do not recite *Tachanun* during these days of *tashlumin*, this is proof that even after the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash and in the Diaspora, the reality of this concept remains.

From this, there is also a directive for a person’s *avodah* to their Creator: the possibility and the ability are granted during all these days to fulfill what was not done and to complete what was lacking—for whatever reason—on the day of the giving of the Torah. And "everyone agrees regarding Atzeres that we require 'for you'" —to draw all of this down below ten *tefachim*, and specifically into the matters of the body and its joy.

#### ***7667***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1312. A similar copy was sent to several people.

**"Everyone agrees":** *Pesachim* 68b; *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, 494:18. See also *Torah Or*, *Yisro* (68a and onwards).

## 7668

B"H, 13 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and man of action, etc.,
Rabbi Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

...Regarding your writing that you heard in my name that I said that, in general, one should immerse five times on Erev Shabbos, and you write that you found opinions of two, three, four, thirteen, and fourteen (though not all of them speak of Erev Shabbos immersion), but not five—

I do not know the basis for this rumor. For although there is a source for five immersions—and in the sefer *Pri HaAretz* (Parshas Lech Lecha, and copied in *Sefer HaBaal Shem Tov*, Parshas Yisro, section 25), it is brought in the name of the holy Rabbi Avraham, etc., son of the great Maggid of Mezritch—

And one should note the five immersions of the Kohen Gadol on Yom Kippur (and see *Likutei Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, end of Parshas Pinchas).

And furthermore, the five immersions, one higher than the other, which are relevant to everyone: for *chullin*, *maaser*, *terumah*, *kodesh*, and *mei parah* (*Chagigah* 2:6; and see *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaBrachos*, chapter 5).

But who am I to decide between all the aforementioned opinions?

Also, it should be noted that our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch* (Orach Chaim, section 88, paragraphs 11-12) brings the opinion that immersion for a *baal keri* is once, and for *teshuvah*—three times.

In the *Shelah* (brought in *Machatzis HaShekel* there), there are two opinions: fourteen and thirty-nine. The *Shelah* discusses this at length in *Shaar HaOsios*, letter *Kuf* (104b), and in *Maseches Yoma*, *Shaar HaTeshuvah*.

## 7659

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Rabbi Pinchas Aharon, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the conduct for the *hachnosas sefer Torah* into the *beis medrash*.

A letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the general order of these events has already been published. However, in every matter, one must take into account the custom of the city—by which I mean whether one lives in a Jewish neighborhood or a non-Jewish neighborhood, and the like—and arrange the *hachnosas sefer Torah* according to the specifics of the city, such as whether to walk extensively through the streets or not, and so on.

Regarding your writing about selling letters (for *beis medrash* needs or for *tzedakah* in general), it seems that this is the custom throughout the Diaspora. Nevertheless, as mentioned, it is worthwhile to ascertain the custom in the United States specifically, naturally among those who are G-d-fearing and observant of His *mitzvos*.

Regarding your writing that the appropriate day would be during the *Bein HaMetzarim* or even immediately after *Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av*—it is understood that the latter suggestion, to do this after *Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av*, is ruled out. Regarding *Bein HaMetzarim* as well, one should look into the matter: is it not possible to do it at a more appropriate time? For merit is brought about through a meritorious day.

To add names onto the *atzei chaim* of the *sefer Torah*—it is understood that this depends on whether the *sefer Torah* (and the *atzei chaim* included) is in his possession; if so, he may add names. And it is best, as you wrote in your letter, not to do so together and in the same place where the names of the original donors have already been inscribed.

As we stand in the days of the conclusion and seal of the *yemei tashlumin* of the time of the giving of our Torah, may it be His will that the *hisorerus* be drawn down permanently, so that "every day they shall be in your eyes as new," without the *kaf* of comparison (see Rashi, *Devarim* 26:11).

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***7659***

**Rabbi Pinchas Aharon, may he live:** Weberman, Miami.

**Already been published:** In his *Igros Kodesh*, Vol. 2, p. 412.

## 770

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a very long interruption, your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh arrived, in which you write regarding the expansion of your business.

In general, this is a proper thing, but one must seek to ensure that other anash should also have a livelihood from it. Especially according to your writing, that you see a necessity to hand over a portion of the work to someone else, it is understandable that the details and the manner in which this is done must be decided on the spot, according to the ways of commerce. However, in general—this should be the aspiration and the goal, especially as is known how much our Rabbeinu Nesi'im exerted themselves specifically regarding livelihood for anash, and that which pertains to the fulfillment of the love of fellow Jews.

Regarding your writing of the proposal for a partnership with someone else who already has such a business—this depends on the soul-traits and character of the person in question. Since, according to your writing, he has already been in this business for a long time, you surely know the particulars of this.

In general, one must take into account that when a partner comes from an already established business, he emphasizes his demands and feels stronger, and this also has a place in logic and fairness—therefore, one must take this into account in advance, as well as the second good side: that the competition is thereby reduced.

I hope that without waiting for the change in the business, you will increase your activities for Beis Lubavitch—as a mitzvah, and as an addition, that this is a conduit and vessel for the blessing of Hashem.

Certainly, you are maintaining the three daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 774

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Shimon, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of Wednesday,

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter. May it be the will of Hashem that you have a complete and speedy recovery, and that you return to your strength—both in the literal sense and in the deeper sense, as explained in the *maamar* "Maskil L'Eisan HaEzrachi" by our Alter Rebbe (printed in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*).

Regarding what you wrote concerning your position after two years—when you will enter the new building of the school: It is understood that there is no point in discussing this now. In the span of two years, it is likely that many changes will occur in the aforementioned building, as well as in the general situation of the schools in your camp, etc. Every person, within the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*, must be strong and confident in Hashem, who oversees every individual with *hashgacha pratis*, that all matters will be arranged in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed. Continue in your current position for now.

My hope is strong that you have a daily *shiur* in our Torah, the Torah of life, with an addition on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem. This, of course, includes a *shiur* in *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. Furthermore, you should influence your surroundings in this regard. Sometimes, the words of a professional regarding a matter that seemingly has no connection to the study of Torah—yet he speaks specifically of the necessity of it—are most influential.

I wrote "seemingly has no connection," because **in truth**—there is a connection. According to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, everything an individual Jew sees and hears, he can learn from it a lesson in his *avodah* to his Creator. Here is one example, which also serves as an answer to a question asked by the nations of the world and even by some of *Bnei Yisrael*: Since you are the fewest of all the peoples, what hope is there to influence and rectify the **world** under the sovereignty of Hashem, and not merely to be content with a lifestyle that is different from every other nation—living unto yourselves?

In your profession of chemistry, there is an answer to this: at every step, one sees how a very small quantity—at times—acts to reverse the course of events around it, a course involving a much larger quantity.

And more than that—even in a case where it does not change its own nature at all, as is the case with a catalyst.

With blessings for health and good news.

## 7776

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Shmuel, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

Following a pause, your letter of 17 Sivan was received, and as you requested, I am responding to it out of turn.

Regarding the vocational school for girls—based on what I have heard about the situation in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt speedily), and in general regarding education on the basis of *taharas hakodesh* (purity of holiness), in my opinion, it is imperative to maintain the institution, and furthermore, to establish it firmly and, if possible, to expand it. The reasons are clear:

1) Education on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*, especially now, is intended not merely to acquire knowledge, but—and this is the main point—as a preparation for a life based on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*. As we see tangibly, this influences and affects not only the students themselves, but also their homes in the present, and certainly their homes when they marry, and so on. Any weakening in any area of this is a weakening of the entire system of traditional Yiddishkeit. Even if there were room to question *ab initio* whether to enter a certain field of education, once it has already begun and has been operating for several years, and word has spread about the institution and its activities, the consequences of failing to establish it—or, Heaven forbid, closing it—are clear. These are consequences that could potentially have a ripple effect on other institutions of the movement to which this institution belongs, and would constitute a certain weakening of the entire front of education on the basis of *taharas hakodesh*.

2) A specific point regarding the aforementioned institution is that it has (or at the very least, should have) a connection and continuity with the Reshet institutions, etc. And although until now, to my great regret, sufficient attention has not been paid to the graduates of the Reshet schools, the *maamar* of Chazal is well known: "One who has eaten garlic and his breath is foul, should he eat more garlic...?" [i.e., one should not add to a bad situation]. In any case, the vocational school has, to some small extent, filled this void.

3) From the point you wrote about—establishing and improving the teachers' seminary—it is necessary to have a second institution that can also serve as a place to absorb those students whom the Chabad girls' schools are obligated to accept, but who are not suited for the required level of the teachers' seminary; there will certainly be such students.

4) **There** is room to say that a certain percentage of the vocational school will, over time, be "refined" in a way that will make them suitable for the requirements of the teachers' seminary. One must take care **in advance** to provide a reservoir from which students will come to the teachers' seminary.

5) One could add many more reasons to those already mentioned, and certainly for someone like you, there is no need for this.

It is understood that you may publicize everything written above in my name if it will be of benefit, and I look forward to hearing good news soon.

Regarding the content of the letter—it is being sent via express mail.

With blessings for success in your holy work, with joy and goodness of heart.

*) The above is a reason for why they requested three days from the outset. There was no falsehood in his request, for they did not speak at all about what would happen after three days, and it is obvious that they did not say that after three days they would return (as precisely explained by the Riva in his commentary on the Torah, beginning of Parshas Beshalach). Rather, it would be dependent and clarified **then**—and only based on this can we understand why, at the time of the Exodus, the Egyptians **saw** (and did not ask about it) that Bnei Yisrael took **all** their possessions with them and left nothing behind.

## 7778

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, Moshe Yitzchak, may he live,
Greetings and blessings!

...In response to your question regarding the reason why Moshe Rabbeinu asked Pharaoh to let the Jewish people go for a three-day journey, given that the ultimate intention was their complete liberation:

1) As with everything in Torah and mitzvos, there are "seventy faces to the Torah," and there are several reasons for this as well. One of them is to demonstrate that the plagues in Mitzrayim were a punishment measure for measure, for they were "evil and sinful." This is evidenced by the fact that after the request for a **three-day** leave—during the course of their labor and exile of **two hundred and ten years**—they refused to agree to it under any circumstances. Even after they agreed once, they reneged, until they saw there was no other way (at the plague of the firstborn). From this, there is a moral lesson for every person and for all generations: that every matter is conducted according to justice and righteousness, even if it is not understood at all by human intellect and presents many intellectual difficulties*.

2) Regarding the reason why several of the tzaddikim prior to the giving of the Torah were born from marriages that are forbidden after the giving of the Torah—namely, marriages between close relatives.

As mentioned above, here too there are "seventy faces to the Torah" and several reasons. One of the reasons, according to the simple interpretation, is that at that time, before the giving of the Torah, the world was extremely coarse, wrapped in matters of avodah zarah, corrupt ideologies, illicit relationships, and depraved character traits, etc. It reached the point where, in the words of the Rambam in Hilchos Avodas Kochavim (end of Chapter 1): "The fundamental principle that Avraham had planted was almost uprooted, and the **children of Yaakov** were returning to the errors of the world and their wanderings." This was all the more true before the influence of Avraham. Therefore, those select few who recognized their Creator and arranged their lives according to the path of justice and law—whose entire desire and will was to "command his household and his children after him to keep the way of Hashem"—were compelled not to deviate to the right or to the left. Rather, they had to seek their matches—for themselves and for their sons and daughters—from within the **select few**, whose number was, naturally, **extremely** small. The nature of children is similar to the nature of the mother and the nature of the father in their lineage. This is subsequently reinforced by the education they receive from the father and the mother. Therefore, this was the instruction of Avraham regarding his son (and likewise regarding himself), and so his children did after him, as it is written in the verse: "You shall go to my land and to my birthplace, and take a wife for my son, for Yitzchak."

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5721
