## 7880

7880

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Shelach, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Women’s Association of Brownsville and East New York
May Hashem grant you life

Blessings and peace!

The highlight of this week’s parsha, Parshas Shelach, is the mission of the twelve representatives of the Jewish people whom Moshe Rabbeinu sent to tour and explore the land that Hashem had promised the Jews, Eretz Yisrael.

On the face of it, this is difficult to understand: since the mission was sent by Moshe Rabbeinu, it was surely in accordance with the Torah. Why, then, did it result in a tragedy and a *bechiya l’doros* (a weeping for generations)—a tragedy that resonated even in subsequent generations?

The answer is: the mission was indeed in accordance with the Torah’s mandate, which requires that a Jew—both as an individual and as a collective—must do what is within their power *b’derech hateva* (in a natural way). However, at the same time, one must know that the *bracha* and *hatzlacha* come from Hashem, and if necessary, even *lema’alah miderech hateva* (supernaturally). The *meraglim* (spies), however, did not act or speak with this mindset. They made their own calculations regarding the outcome and success of conquering Eretz Yisrael, and began to persuade the Jews not to fulfill Hashem’s command.

Every endeavor, in private life and especially in communal matters—just like the entirety of Jewish life—is a mission from Hashem.

If one does not allow human calculations to obscure one’s *bitachon* in Hashem, success is guaranteed. Each and every person must do everything that depends on them, and Hashem will grant success *lema’alah miderech hateva* (in a supernatural way).

In particular, an endeavor that has as its goal and task to help an educational institution *al taharas hakodesh* (based on pure holiness)—an endeavor that directly connects its participants with the *Torah Hakedosha* and Hashem—is certain to be aided by the *zechus* of Torah and the *zechus harabbim*. And the greater the effort to fulfill the mission to the fullest extent, the greater the Divine *bracha*—and not only for the success of the work, but also in what one needs in their personal and family life: *nachas* from children, health, and *parnassah* in abundance.

With blessings for *hatzlacha* and for good tidings in your work and in general.

## 7780

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Shelach, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Bais Rivkah schools in general, and to the participants in the nineteenth annual banquet of the Bais Rivkah schools in particular, may Hashem grant them life.

Shalom u’vracha!

The annual banquet, which takes place this year during the week between Shabbos Parshas Shelach and Shabbos Parshas Korach, surely has a connection through Hashgacha Pratis to the content of these two parshiyos.

These two parshiyos recount two stormy and tragic experiences that our ancestors endured in the desert on their way from Mitzrayim to Eretz Yisrael: the uprising of the Meraglim (the shluchim whom Moshe Rabbeinu sent to tour Eretz Yisrael and bring back a report) and the machlokes of Korach and his assembly against Moshe Rabbeinu.

How did the women conduct themselves during these critical and fateful moments for the Jewish people?

Our Chachamim, zichronam livrachah, relate that the women, in general, did not join in the upheaval that certain wavering men had incited at that time. On the contrary, they demonstrated a very great measure of bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam, loyalty to Moshe Rabbeinu and to the Torah, and love for the Holy Land.

Therefore, they merited to raise a new generation of Jewish children who were imbued with bitachon and love for the Ribono shel Olam and for Torah and mitzvos, and they entered and inherited the Holy Land.

The fundamental lesson from this is clear. It shows how much a Jewish woman and mother can accomplish in the chinuch of children, even without the assistance of her husband—and certainly much more with his assistance—and how much a woman can have a positive influence on her husband and on the entire atmosphere of the home, to the point of being crowned with the title "builders of the Jewish home" (*Chachmas nashim ban'tah beisah*).

If in all times the Jewish woman has occupied a highly important place in shaping the Jewish home and Jewish life in general, this is certainly many times more true in our times and circumstances. Therefore, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, invested so much effort to found, maintain, and expand the Bais Rivkah schools, where precious Jewish daughters are raised *al taharas hakodesh* to be true builders of the Jewish home and to ensure the future of the Jewish people. Great is the zechus of everyone who takes part in the work to support and expand the Bais Rivkah schools, and great is the reward to be blessed in everything one needs, both in gashmius and in ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing for besuros tovos.

## 7282

B”H, 27 Sivan, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Sivan, in which you write regarding the health condition of your son, shlita, and the opinion of the doctors in this matter.

Based on the tone of your letter, although it is not explicitly stated, it seems that the consensus of all the doctors is that for the time being, there is no basis for considering serious treatments (such as surgery, chas v’shalom, or the like, not even an exploratory surgery), and this negative stance is understandable in connection with your son’s young age.

Since there is no practical difference in terms of action, according to the perspective of our Torah, the Torah of life, a person must be strong in their bitachon in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, that the situation will continue to improve.

However, in my opinion, you should prompt the doctors: if it is the case that the cause is that one of the bronchial tubes has a narrower passage than usual, then in such a case there is a mechanical remedy that carries no risk of being ineffective, chas v’shalom, but only potential benefit. This is the performance of exercises related to breathing and the neck muscles at a pace slightly faster and stronger than usual. As is the way with all organs, when they are accustomed to their function, this in itself strengthens and develops them. This also applies here, and I emphasize the words **slightly** **faster**, which eliminates all concerns in this regard.

The method of these movements should, of course, be decided by the doctor, as well as whether they should be done by machine or manually, etc. Perhaps there is room here to seek advice from nurses who specialize in physical therapy.

It is appropriate to have his tefillin checked—if this has not been done within the last twelve months—and your wife, tichyeh, should maintain the good custom of kosher daughters of Israel to set aside money for tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. It is also good to clarify whether, in the process of your shidduch, there was any slight to the honor of a son or daughter of Israel in a way that, according to din, requires asking for forgiveness.

Since everything is by Hashgacha Pratis, I have the obligation (and the privilege) to urge you regarding the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—fixed times every day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above.

## 7283

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following a delay, your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz was received, in which you write regarding the manner of continuing your son’s studies...

I am surprised by the question regarding such a clear matter, which surely must be in one of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos, whichever is more comfortable for him—whether in Montreal or New York. It might be good to inquire at both locations to see which is more suitable for him.

Regarding your mention of the difficulties in taking on further expenses—surely you remember the mesiras nefesh that existed in your country in the past for every individual, that their children should walk in the straight path of Yiddishkeit and Chassidus. Even though that was connected not only with money and health matters, but with literal mesiras nefesh, Heaven forbid, what value do these financial difficulties have compared to an education that impacts the entire duration of one’s life?

Especially since all Yidden are believers, the children of believers, in our holy Torah—the Torah of life—one of whose instructions is that for the expenses of one’s children for Talmud Torah, one is provided for from Above specifically (Beitzah 16a), and as our Sages say there, "If he adds, they add for him."

I hope that you are taking part, to the extent truly possible, in the dissemination of the wellsprings outward, and this is also a channel and vessel for receiving the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in all that is needed.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## 7284

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, the Month of Redemption, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished avreichim who accept the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven and the yoke of Torah and mitzvos, and above all — the laying of tefillin, to which the entire Torah is compared,
May Hashem grant you life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with great pleasure that I received the news regarding the celebration in connection with your beginning to lay tefillin.

Regarding this, Chazal have informed us: “Come and see: whoever lays tefillin upon his head and upon his arm, a voice goes up every day to all the living creatures of the Merkavah, the Ofanim, the Seraphim, and the angels appointed over prayers, saying: ‘Give honor to the image of the King, for he is the one who lays tefillin.’”

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you accept upon yourselves the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos with joy and a good heart.

For although the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos must specifically be through *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke)—just as it was when the entirety of our people, the Children of Israel, came under the yoke of Torah and mitzvos at the standing at Har Sinai, where they preceded "we will do" to "we will hear"—nevertheless, at the same time, it is a pleasant and good yoke. For there is no "good" other than Torah, and the study of Torah leads to action—the fulfillment of mitzvos and good deeds.

And in accordance with what is stated, “If you walk in My statutes and keep My mitzvos... I will grant [all the blessings]” as enumerated in that parsha, may it be the will [of Hashem] that you conduct yourselves in accordance with the aforementioned as is required, and may the Ribono shel Olam fulfill His promise that you be blessed with all that you need, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah—both the revealed and Chassidus—and in the fulfillment of its mitzvos,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7786

B"H, 4 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the eighth grade, Yeshivas Beis Hillel, Passaic
May Hashem keep them alive

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter regarding your preparations for the end of the school year. May it be His will that it should be in a good and auspicious hour, and may you go from strength to strength in the study of Torah and the performance of its mitzvos with joy and hiddur.

Upon reading in your letter about the subjects you study, it is surely unnecessary to note and emphasize that regarding the holy studies of our holy Torah—which is our life and the length of our days—Heaven forbid to speak of a "conclusion" or a "break" in them. On the contrary, it is an ascent to a higher level in both quantity and quality, which requires extra effort to fulfill the principle of "we elevate in matters of holiness." This is the essential point, as our Sages, of blessed memory, stated: "Great is the study of Torah, for it leads to action"—the actual performance of mitzvos in daily life and in "all your ways know Him."

It is also unnecessary to emphasize that those who say there are matters in our Torah that are difficult or impossible to fulfill are making a great mistake. This is the opposite of the faith of Israel, who are "believers, the children of believers," and it is also contrary to sound logic. Since the Torah and mitzvos were given by the Creator of the world and the Maker of man, it is self-understood that even before the commandment was given, He provided the strength to enable their fulfillment. It is impossible that the Creator would demand that which is impossible to fulfill; the matter depends solely on the strength of one's will.

Furthermore, regarding the subjects studied in school that are outside of holy studies—in which there is indeed a conclusion and a break—it is understood that when one is freed from these studies, one must increase the time dedicated to holy studies: the study of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the performance of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and live by them." The expression "dedicated" time is precise, for Israel, a holy nation, sanctifies all times and matters that pertain to it through Torah and mitzvos.

With blessings for outstanding success in the above, with joy and a glad heart.

## 7288

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your express letter of 4 Tammuz, received this morning, in which you write regarding the dispute between you and your brother, the G-d-fearing, learned, and esteemed [Name]—may he live—which has also affected the relationship between you and the family dynamics in general.

Since our Sages, of blessed memory, have said that peace is the vessel that holds the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He—and especially peace between brothers—it is understood and simple that you and your brother—may he live—must do everything that depends on each of you so that there be peace between you, as **soon** as possible.

Regarding the differences of opinion between you concerning the business from some time ago, you should follow the custom of Israel in this matter: present your arguments (each of you to the other) before a Rav who is a *moreh hora’ah* (decisor of law), and act according to his ruling and instruction. If you do not know of a Rav upon whom you both agree, call and ask the Agudas HaRabbanim (which unites the Rabbis of the United States and Canada), and rely on the Rav who is there and who adjudicates such matters.

But as stated, first and foremost, you must make peace between yourselves immediately. May it be G-d’s will that the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, be drawn down in greater measure, immediately.

Since Wednesday is the wedding day of your brother’s son—may he live—it is most appropriate and fitting that even if you are preoccupied and your mood is not quite suitable, you should nevertheless be present at least at the *chuppah*. Beyond the fact that this will increase peace and bring *nachas ruach* to your parents—may they live—which is one of the Ten Commandments, "Honor your father and your mother," it is explained in the holy *sefarim* that the time of the *chuppah* is an *eis ratzon* (a time of favor), and the *chassan* and *kallah* possess a special significance. It would be worthwhile for you to ask them to pray for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for good while they stand at their *chuppah*.

It is my strong hope that you will accept what is stated above with a good heart and a pleasant countenance, and that you will fulfill my request in accordance with the command of our Sages, of blessed memory, to make peace and increase the peace between you. May it be G-d’s will that you bring good news regarding this and all your affairs.

I look forward to hearing good news.

P.S.
The content of this letter is being sent via express/urgent mail.

## 7930

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Chag HaSiyum,
Montreal
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

On the occasion of the Chag HaSiyum, I send my blessing to all who are participating in this *simcha shel Torah*. For surely everyone understands that a *siyum* in a yeshiva in general, and in a Lubavitcher yeshiva in particular, is actually the beginning of a higher level in Torah and *mitzvos*. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant that this truly be the case for the students completing their studies, to the fullest extent.

This year, the Chag HaSiyum will surely be marked by the spirit of Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz. The concept of *zichron* (remembrance) among Jews is the lesson to be derived from it. The days of 12-13 Tammuz remind and teach each one of us that one must not take any difficulties into account—even very great ones—in order to make the study of Torah possible, and study *al menas la'asos u'lekayeim* (for the purpose of doing and fulfilling), the fulfillment of *mitzvos* in practice. And if this is true regarding helping others, it is certainly true regarding oneself. Another essential point in this is that if one desires with truth and with a firm resolution, one can overcome all difficulties. Although who can compare themselves to the *Nesi'ei Yisrael*, nevertheless, everyone, according to their standing and situation, possesses the necessary *kochos* for this, especially since these difficulties are not at all comparable to those that existed in those days and in that country.

May *Hashem Yisbarach* grant you success in ascending in the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim* and the fulfillment of its *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, with joy and goodness of heart.

With blessings for good tidings in the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7291

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

To my dear relative, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Yehuda Leib, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Tammuz, in which you write regarding the matter of a gathering in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) for the descendants of the Rabbanit, daughter of the Mitteler Rebbe, of blessed memory.

A decision regarding this depends on whether there will be someone who takes an interest in this with the necessary vigor so that the matter is planned and organized.

And according to the instruction, "In all your ways know Him," and with further explanation of this in the teachings of Chassidus, the intention of the aforementioned gathering should be to arouse matters connected to the worldview and way of life of the aforementioned Rabbanit—not merely a remembrance of days of **yore**, etc., but rather an arousal in the **present** regarding conduct, extending even to daily life, and so on.

In such a manner, any matter that adds to traditional Judaism, our Torah and its mitzvos—especially when illuminated by the light and vitality of Chassidus—is correct and good.

Surely you are preparing for the Chag HaGeulah, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which is approaching, and as is the purpose of every farbrengen, may you take from the arousal of these auspicious days in order to bring them into practice throughout the entire year.

With blessings for good tidings and with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah.

## 7,994

B"H, 11 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and reliable, etc., R' Dovid, shichyeh,

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, along with the enclosure, and per your request, this response is being sent without waiting for the regular turn.

In it, you write regarding the methods for repairing the mikveh, etc.

It is understood, and it is also simple, that it is preferable to have three *boros*. Likewise, it is necessary that the emptying of the mikveh be from above and not from below, due to the concern of *zochalin* (flowing water), even **if** the drain at the bottom is sealed with a material that does not become *tamei*.

However, the main point is that since there are several details and sub-details regarding the manner in which the *boros* are connected to the mikveh, it is most appropriate that you discuss this with the Ra'avad of Helmica, Rabbi Chananya Yom Tov Lipa Deutsch, shichyeh, at the address below [I believe he visited Mexico some time ago]. He is involved in the repair of mikvaos, and in the past, at my request, he visited many places and repaired and improved many things in many details, and *da'al* (a word to the wise is sufficient).

If this matter involves any potential offense to any of the Rabbis in Mexico, you should consult with the aforementioned individual himself on how to avoid such offense. In this, too, he is already experienced. As I mentioned—and I will repeat—since he is accustomed to the *halachos* of mikvaos and has already repaired mikvaos in practice, it is highly appropriate that before the repair, he should see the situation on-site and advise you. It is understood that you can telephone him to say that you are inviting him based on my suggestion, etc.

If the question of travel expenses is an obstacle, then, due to the importance of the matter of the purity of the daughters of Israel, I will participate, *bli neder*, in half of the travel expenses if required.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 796

B"H, Days of Redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 4th of Tammuz, as well as the one preceding it.

As we stand in these auspicious days of 12-13 Tammuz—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, and with him the redemption of all those who are connected to him and his affairs (for the body follows the head), within the entirety of Klal Yisrael—

#### ***796***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 692, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter. A similar version was sent to several people.

**"A star has stepped forth from Yaakov":** See *Yerushalmi* (Maaser Sheni, end of ch. 4) that this applies to every single one of the Bnei Yisrael. Now, according to *Yerushalmi Taanis* (ch. 4, halacha 5)—and this is also the ruling of the Ramban and several commentators on the Chumash—the verse speaks of Mashiach. There is no contradiction here; on the contrary, according to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, it is required for every individual of Yisrael to rectify and prepare the "portion of the stature of Mashiach that pertains to his soul" (*Meor Einayim*, end of Parshas Pinchas). This is understood in the context of a person’s avodah—based on what our Alter Rebbe wrote in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 4.

**"And Yisrael shall act with valor":** See the holy *Ohr HaChaim* on the verse. *Torah Ohr*, Yisro (74b): Thus the galus, etc., is in order that through it, etc., and likewise in the particular, etc.

See also the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek; examine the entry for the mitzvah of *milah* there carefully.

***

## 7998

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Moshe Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 6 Tammuz, in which you raise several questions, including some related to the compilation of the Kolel Chabad calendar and the customs of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established speedily.

It is understood that regarding such matters, you should speak with the editors of the calendar. However, in order to fulfill your request at least in part, I address your question:

Regarding a *bris milah* on Yom Kippur: If the *milah* takes place outside the *beis knesses* and after the *krias haTorah*, at which point the *Sefer Torah* is returned to the ark before the congregation leaves the *beis knesses*, there is a significant interruption until the *Mussaf* prayer, which is preceded by the recitation of *Kaddish*.

It is correct, as you wrote, that in such a case, one should recite a *mizmor* (psalm) before the recitation of the *Kaddish*.

It should be noted that the same applies to every *Rosh Chodesh* in those *batei knesses* where the custom is to put on *Rabbeinu Tam tefillin* and recite the *Shema* after the *Sefer Torah* has been returned, and, as is obvious and simple, before the *Mussaf* prayer. For even if one could argue that taking off *tefillin* is not an interruption, the same cannot be said for putting on *tefillin* and reciting the *Shema*.

2) On the night after *Tisha B'Av*, the *netilas yadayim* should be performed three times, just as it is done on the night after *Yom Kippur* before *Havdalah* and *Kiddush Levanah*.

3) Regarding the reason why we do not perform *Nesias Kapayim* during the *Ne'ilah* prayer: The reasons for the two practices regarding *Nesias Kapayim* are explained in the *Shulchan Aruch*. You should clarify the practice of *anash* in the Holy Land regarding this—on the spot, as mentioned above.

At a time of favor, you should mention him at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It is my duty (and privilege) to urge you regarding the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—a fixed time every day, with an increase on the holy day of *Shabbos*.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above.

***

7998

Part of this was printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 17, p. 439; part on p. 458; part on p. 563; and it was completed based on the secretariat's copy.

**R' Moshe Meir:** Schlesinger, Jerusalem.

## 7,899

[13 Tammuz, 5721]

In response to your letter of Thursday, in which you write regarding the education of your son, may he live, and the reasoning involved:

Since a decision in this matter depends on several details, and especially on the *tichunas hanefesh* (soul-disposition) of the aforementioned, it is appropriate to consult regarding this with those who are familiar with your son, may he live, and these details. For it is very often the case in such matters that the parents themselves are not entirely objective in evaluating their children. The concern is not only that they may lean too far to one side, but that sometimes, due to their closeness, they may lean in the opposite direction as well—in the vein of "a person cannot declare himself righteous," and so on.

May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, that you arrive at a truly good decision for your son, may he live—good in both material and spiritual terms alike.

And since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, it is my duty (and privilege), as commanded by our *Rebbeim*, to urge you regarding the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of *Chassidus*—a fixed study every day, with an increase on *Shabbos*, which is holy to Hashem.

#### ***7,899***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 22, p. 435.

## 7770

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

R' Shlomo Zalman, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 2 Tammuz. It is my hope that your recovery is progressing and that you are beginning to enter the path of disseminating traditional Judaism among all of Klal Yisrael, in accordance with the teaching of the Mishnah, "I was created to serve my Maker."

In connection with the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, whose path we follow—I was in that country at that time, and naturally, all the details of that episode are as vividly etched in my memory as if it were happening now. There is a powerful lesson and a living instruction here: how even one individual can act and overcome the greatest obstacles and hindrances, provided there is a firm resolve, with mesiras nefesh and without fear.

Regarding the present, I wish to express my blessing of mazal tov on the birth of your grandson, may he live and be well. May it be G-d’s will that his parents, may they live and be well, raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in prosperity and with health of body and soul.

With blessing.

Due to a certain reason, the sending of this letter was delayed, and I have just now received your letter with the good news of the wedding of your daughter, may she live and be well. May it be G-d’s will that they build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, an everlasting edifice, in true happiness, both materially and spiritually.

## 7 Tammuz

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Tammuz and those preceding it.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding all the matters about which you write.

It is understandable that your writing—that you feel almost alone in the campaign—is surprising. For it has been stated, repeated, and tripled in the sichos of our Rebbes, the leaders of our generation, in many places: that in every action a Jewish person takes for Torah and mitzvos, he is accompanied and assisted by the One and Only of the world, the Holy One, blessed be He, and so on. This is especially true in this generation, the footsteps of Moshiach, and regarding the matter of spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus. When a person does a little from below, they are granted success such that the action from above is great.

Indeed, you and your colleagues, may they live, who are **active** in Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, see this tangibly.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as we come from these auspicious days—the days of redemption—each one of you will take from this inspiration to increase your activities in spreading the wellsprings, to the point of "spreading out" without limits.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings.

## 7772

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Moshe Yosef Rubin, shlita,
Former President of the Union of Rabbis in Romania

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter and our conversation regarding the project of repairing the fences in the cemeteries of the communities in Europe that were destroyed and emptied, may Hashem have mercy, during the days of the war and the Holocaust, G-d forbid:

I say, "Well done for this good work." Great is the honor of the deceased, and in this case, it is also the honor of the living.

And if every kindness performed for the dead is a "kindness of truth" (*chesed shel emes*)—which is beyond the realm of reward, as one is granted from Above (by way of a gift) a level of *chesed shel emes* that is unlimited, even if one does something of small value, as the saying goes, "a father and a basket for burial"—

Then how much more so is this the case regarding the aforementioned matter, which is of great value, affects thousands of Jews, and especially involves the matter of *Kiddush Hashem*, so that the name of Israel not be desecrated among the nations.

And my confidence is strong that this project will find a proper echo in the hearts of our brothers, the Children of Israel, to volunteer with a generous spirit for its execution—to fence in the breaches in the cemeteries and rebuild what has been destroyed.

Until the prophecy of the L-rd Hashem is fulfilled: "Behold, I will open your graves and bring you up... and I will put My spirit in you, and you shall live."

With respect and blessing.

## 7404

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rav, G-d-fearing, illustrious, and distinguished, etc.,
Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, may he live, formerly Av Beis Din of Helmitz

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of Tuesday:

1) Regarding the custom concerning a father being in seclusion (*yichud*) with his daughter, or a mother with her son—I have not heard of this.

2) Regarding your question about our custom concerning eating meat after dairy products: In general, we follow the aforementioned practice—even after milk and butter—to wait one hour (and also, not to eat them during the same meal). This is written in the Shelah, Maseches Shavuos (180b). (Regarding what is written in Darchei Teshuvah, Yoreh Deah, end of Siman 89, end of subsection 19, "an hour or more," the measure of "or more" requires study, as does the source for this). However, I have not heard whether this is an instruction for everyone or merely a custom of individuals of high standing. See Pri Megadim to Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of Siman 89, Sifsei Daas, subsection 7, that a pause of one hour replaces the need for rinsing the mouth.

Despite the pressure of time, I have taken from my schedule to answer you promptly, as you requested in your letter.

With blessings for good tidings from your holy work to increase purity among the Jewish people, in good health.

P.S.
The letter was delayed in being sent, and meanwhile your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh was received, in which you transcribe from a certain book a source for the custom of those who wait half an hour after eating milk and butter.

[You compare this] to the ruling regarding the prohibition of performing work before davening, where the language in the Mishnah is "close to Mincha," and the measure, as explained in the Poskim, is half an hour, as the proximity ceases after this interval.

The honor of the author is in its place, but (at the very least, as you transcribed in your letter) the core proof is missing. For regarding the eating of dairy and meat, I have not found—at this time—the language of "close to," but rather "as one," "at one time," or "in one meal" (Zohar, Vol. II, 125a). And if we are specifically looking to find "proximity," all the aforementioned expressions in the Zohar are closer to the meaning of "immediately" (and even more so, as is understood).

And the measure of "immediately" is the distance of 22 amos, as ruled in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, Siman 166. Furthermore, it is also considered an interruption.

Regarding what is written in the aforementioned Darchei Teshuvah to wait an hour or more, one should note the measure of digestion, which is the distance of four mil (see the relevant sources in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, end of Siman 184).

## 775

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe Meir, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter dated 16 Tammuz, along with the donation from Mrs. Ruth Geshi, may she live, for the Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Lod, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily.

It is unnecessary to elaborate to one such as yourself regarding the magnitude of the merit of this deed, especially at this time of need, when, were it not for the lack of financial resources, it would be possible to greatly expand the activities of spreading Torah and strengthening Judaism in its pure, holy form. May your strength be increased to continue doing likewise and more.

Enclosed is a letter of acknowledgment and blessing for the aforementioned generous woman, may she live. Surely, if you find it appropriate to add an explanation to what is written, you will also find the suitable words for it.

P.S.

To connect the aforementioned good deed with the current period of Bein HaMetzarim: Our Sages, of blessed memory, said that Jerusalem was destroyed only because the children of the house of the Rebbe (the school children) were neglected (Shabbos 119b). The obligation to remember these events and these days is surely intended for the purpose of rectification by negating the causes that led to the destruction—namely, strengthening education in its pure, holy form. This is especially true in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily, which sits with its head covered like a barren woman who has not given birth, etc. We must increase and add there children of the house of the Rebbe, and "kids becoming goats"—students of the yeshivos—and so on, a double consolation, until the prophecy is fulfilled: "The smallest shall become a thousand, and the youngest a mighty nation."

## Z'Tashu

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

It gave me pleasure to read your letter in which you write about your upcoming wedding and your decision to establish your home in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life. May it be the will of Hashem that you fulfill this decision together with your chosen partner, especially since, as I have heard regarding your family, the rock from which you were hewn will also support you in this.

It is not for nothing that a woman is called the "foundation of the home" (*akeres habayis*), for the primary conduct of the home and its entire standing and state depend primarily on the mistress of the house.

Especially in our current era, which is full of events and upheavals, there is no foundation as strong and solid for the existence of a home in Israel as the Torah and its mitzvos. Upon this depends all of its happiness—not only spiritual, but physical as well—and all the more so in our Holy Land, the land upon which "the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." Even with a simple reflection—provided one is free of preconceived and biased notions—it is easy for a person of understanding to see how the events of our time, both the good and the not-so-good, have emphasized the concept of "You have chosen us from all the nations." It is understood that the Creator of the world’s choice of us to be His treasured people grants us not only special privileges but also special obligations: to illuminate all our actions and our daily lives with the true light, the light of Torah and mitzvos, in thought, speech, and—most importantly—in deed. Furthermore, it is our duty to spread and sow the light of Torah and mitzvos, in the language of the Baal Shem Tov as he brings in his letter, "May your springs spread outward"—springs of light and love, founded upon Hashem’s love for His people, the Children of Israel. For out of His great love, He sanctified us specifically through His mitzvos, which are the channel and the vessel for receiving the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam, in both physicality and spirituality alike.

With blessings of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, and for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

Attached is the content of a sicha from a recent N'shei Chabad gathering, which is, of course, directed toward you and your circle as well.

## 7757

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

The Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod
May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

...Regarding your question concerning the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim who participate in the activities of ATA and the like...

It is astonishing that there is any doubt or question regarding a matter that was explicitly stated by the founders and directors of Tomchei Temimim—the Rebbe (Rashab) and his son, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—may the merit of the righteous protect us. They clearly stated and wrote that all matters concerning the students are under the authority of the Yeshiva administration, and it is specifically according to their direction that they must conduct themselves, from the soul to the flesh. This is the only way for a "radiating light" to come into being—when there is first a "receiving light," as is well known from the holy sichos on this subject.

May it be the will that, finally, all branches of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim will develop in every place they exist, in accordance with the will and hope of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im.

And immediately thereafter—the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, Moshiach ben Dovid, as it is written: "A star has stepped forth from Yaakov, and a scepter has arisen from Yisrael..." and "Yisrael performs valiantly."

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7159

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5721

## 7513

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Tammuz, in which you write about the state of your daughter’s health... may she live, and the opinion of the doctors regarding it. Several of them are advising a surgical procedure on her hand, but it is not clear from your letter whether this is the opinion of a single doctor or many doctors. Furthermore, and most importantly: is this opinion based solely on a lack of knowledge regarding the cause of the ailment (which seemingly is implied, as other various treatments were performed), or do they clearly understand the ailment and the aforementioned treatments were indeed appropriate for it, but in this instance were unsuccessful? You will surely clarify the above, and decide in accordance with the information.

Furthermore, it should be added that in such surgeries, there is a type that is not so much about the surgery itself—which, in the terminology of the doctors, is considered minor—but rather about the extreme caution required not to touch the nerves and arteries that affect the movement of the finger or fingers. It is also appropriate to clarify the aspect that stems from "psychology"—that is, a matter that is not in the physicality of the finger and hand, but rather in the power of thought and imagination. It seems to your daughter that upon her return to work, the pain also returns. [In this case, her contemplation of the concept of Hashgacha Pratis—that He who watches over each and every person is also the "Healer of all flesh and performs wonders," and it is said, "In all your ways [you shall know Him]," with the emphasis on **all**, even the slightest of ways—there is room to say that this will weaken the imagination and the pains associated with it.] May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

My hope is strong that you have been active during these weeks in the matter of spreading the wellsprings wherever your reach extends, and you will surely fulfill this further at the next opportunity.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 7714

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5721
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, R' Shmuel Elazar, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following the longest of intervals, your letter of 17 Tammuz was received. You have surely already received my letter in which I also addressed my position regarding the coalition, etc. As I stated in my sicha, there has been no change in this regard, and the doubt is surprising. In my opinion, participation in a government coalition is forbidden according to Torah.

Since you do not mention anything regarding your health, etc., the hope is strong that all is in order. However, it is still surprising that you do not mention your participation in the farbrengens of anash over the past months, and recently during the days of 12 and 13 Tammuz, which we have just concluded. These days teach us wisdom, understanding, and knowledge: that even an individual, if his resolve is firm to disseminate traditional Judaism without any compromises—both the revealed Torah and Chassidus—and without taking into account any concealments or confusions whatsoever, will succeed. And if this is true in all places, how much more so in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, which is elevated above all lands to Jerusalem—which is as its name implies, and so it must be: *Yirah* of *Shalem*, a completeness of the fear of Hashem. Through this, the fear of flesh and blood is automatically nullified, as our Sages taught in their Mishnah: "Whoever accepts upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, they remove from him [the yoke of government and the yoke of worldly cares]." And if this applies to every person, how much more so to those who have a connection to my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, the master of the celebration, and especially to those who also have a familial connection. They must strive to the point that our Sages call "toiling" in the dissemination of the wellsprings outward, within the framework of disseminating Judaism in general. And this is understood.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

The delivery was delayed due to circumstances. In the meantime, your letters following the above were received, as well as the newspaper clippings, proclamations, etc. You will surely continue sending them, and thank you in advance.

## 7,615

*[Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5721]*

Regarding your note on *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 1 —regarding the phrasing **"but regarding teshuvah, etc."**—the continuation is: if one transgressed a positive mitzvah and repented, they are forgiven; if one transgressed a negative mitzvah, it is suspended. And even though a positive mitzvah overrides a negative mitzvah, this is from the perspective of the worlds and the soul; however, regarding the essence of the mitzvos themselves, negative mitzvos are on a higher level (see *Likutei Torah, Pekudei* 6d). But regarding teshuvah, a positive mitzvah is greater, for even [if one transgressed a negative mitzvah, teshuvah is effective, etc.] (see *Likutei Torah*, the *maamar* beginning *Mah Tovu*, Chapter 2).

2) How does what is written here reconcile with the well-known concept that Yom Kippur **atones for** all blemishes, etc.? And one must add the statement of our Sages that there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah.

However, here it is speaking of teshuvah **in general**, whereas Yom Kippur functions by virtue of the essence of the day itself, without the person’s own avodah in this regard, as is also evident in the *Shas*. See the aforementioned *maamar* beginning *Mah Tovu*.

#### ***7,615***

This letter is addressed to R' Ephraim Eliezer Yales, and was written in the margins of letter 7,611 above—dated Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av. Additional letters to him appear above in 7,555, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 7,616

[Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5721]

...And as we enter the month of Av, known in our tradition as "Menachem Av"—which begins in mourning but whose majority is consolation—may it be the will of our Father in Heaven, the Merciful Father, that He comfort us twofold, through the fulfillment of the prophecy that these days will be transformed into gladness and joy and festive seasons, with the coming of the true Redeemer, speedily and in our very days.

For these aforementioned actions nullify the causes that brought about the destruction, and they are actions of building that hasten the Redemption.

#### ***7,616***

## 7,718

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn

in Buffalo

This is especially true since the affairs of Bnei Yisrael—the material and the spiritual—go hand in hand, for they are "one nation on earth." It is well known how our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, explains that we draw down unity into this lower world, and the rest is understood.

**Bein HaMetzarim:** On the 17th of Tammuz the city was breached and the destruction of Jerusalem began, continuing throughout the period of Bein HaMetzarim.

## 7519

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

- Hillula of our teacher the Arizal -
The avreichim, students of the yeshiva in Manchester
May Hashem protect them and may they live

Greetings and blessings!

Your *pidyon nefesh* was received and will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

As we find ourselves in the *Bein HaMetzarim* period, when, as our Sages of blessed memory state, Jerusalem was destroyed only because the children of the *beis medrash* were neglected,

And since the purpose of the study of *tishbar* (children of the *beis medrash*) is that the kids should become goats—that is, yeshiva students and subsequently Torah scholars—

This serves as a reminder and an impetus to strengthen and increase twofold our efforts in the study of Torah. This study is the rectification for the cause that brought about the destruction of Jerusalem.

Furthermore, and most importantly, the study of Torah must be in the manner it is intended to be, as our Sages of blessed memory state regarding why the land was lost: "Because they did not recite a blessing over the Torah first." See the commentary of the *Bach* on this at length, and it is understood according to what is written in *Likutei Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*).

May it be the will that each one of you will "bless the Torah first" according to the aforementioned inner meaning, and the promise will be fulfilled: "A person sanctifies himself a little from below"—

And no matter how much a person increases his sanctification, it is still "a little" compared to Above—

"They sanctify him greatly from Above."

With blessings for success in all of the above and for good tidings in this regard.

## 7720

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 3 Menachem Av, in which you outline the current order of your life and ask:

a) How to overcome the battle with the *yetzer*.

Based on the well-known statement of our Sages that even a little light pushes away much darkness, and all the more so a great amount of light, your first priority must be to conduct your daily life in accordance with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and through the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." In this, the point of "I have set Hashem before me **always**" is key; the verse does not depart from its literal meaning. When one contemplates that Hashem stands over him and sees not only his actions and speech, but his thoughts as well, this will surely restrain the *yetzer* and enable the *nefesh elokis*—the side of good—to prevail and conduct itself in accordance with the will of Hashem, the Creator of the world (in the literal sense, and this "small world" is man).

To increase special assistance from Above in the aforementioned, it is appropriate that every weekday, before morning *davening*, you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*, and also that your *tefillin* be checked—if this has not been done within the last twelve months.

b) Regarding your inquiry about a place to settle permanently.

The words of the great teacher, the Rambam, are well known: "It is the nature of man to be drawn in his opinions and actions after his friends and associates, and to conduct himself according to the custom of the people of his place" (*Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 6, at the beginning; see there). From this, it is understood that one must endeavor to establish his residence in an environment of those who are *chareidim* to the word of Hashem and who fulfill His *mitzvos* in practice every day. This is especially true regarding a place of residence after marriage, for when Hashem blesses one with sons and daughters, the environment is a **major** factor in their upbringing—no less, and perhaps even more so, than the parents and their influence. And since all of the above is included in the commandment of Hashem, it is certain that Hashem only asks according to one’s capacity, and therefore, the possibility exists to fulfill all of the above.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the great principle in the Torah, "Love your fellow as yourself," from which the immediate result is to spread Yiddishkeit and its matters among the children of Israel wherever your hand can reach.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**To settle permanently:** See also above, Vol. 17, Letter 6141.

## 7,761

B"H, 8 Menachem Av, 5761
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, son of ancestors and son of Torah, R' Y. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

It is with pleasure that I acknowledge receipt of the books *Chochmah U'Mussar* – *Ohel Yesharim*.

Many thanks for this gift, especially in these days, regarding which our Sages state: "For what reason was the land destroyed? Because they did not recite a blessing over the Torah first" (Bava Metzia 85a). As is known, the Bach provides a wonderful and deeply profound explanation of this (in Tur Orach Chaim, siman 47). Its core point is the necessity of studying the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, through which one arrives at the "way of life" and "reproof of instruction" (as explained at length in *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by the Rebbe Rashab, father of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory). This is the study of *chochmah* (the *chochmah* and will of Hashem, which is our holy Torah) and *mussar* (its *pnimiyus*, as mentioned above).

The essence of these days, the remembrance of the *Churban*, is to awaken us to nullify the cause of the *Churban* and to hasten the *Geulah* and the rebuilding—the true and complete *Geulah* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will come and redeem us speedily in our days.

The *Geulah* itself is also dependent upon the study of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, as is explained at length in many places (cited in the aforementioned *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*), based on the introduction of Rav Chaim Vital to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, according to what is written in many places in the *Zohar* and *Tikkunei Zohar*.

It is somewhat surprising that this was not mentioned (as fully as is required) in the *Shaar HaGeulah* in the aforementioned book *Ohel Yesharim*.

With respect and blessing, and awaiting good tidings of the arrival of the "bringer of good tidings," at which time these days will be transformed into joy and gladness and festive holidays.

#### ***7,761***

**R' Y.:** Katzin, Brooklyn.

## 7724

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

To Mr. Menachem, may he live,

I hereby acknowledge, albeit with some delay, the receipt of your letter in due time. It is my hope that the matter of the Eiruv in the Moshav Bar Giora has surely been arranged by now, in accordance with the style of your writing.

Although, naturally, the phrasing—that you are satisfied because it "causes me *nachas ruach*"—is certainly true, it does not compare to the essence of the matter itself. As is well known, Chazal spoke at great length regarding the importance of observing Shabbos, to the extent that they said that if the Jewish people were to observe even one Shabbos properly, they would be redeemed immediately.

I emphasize here "Chazal" (our Sages), rather than the common expression "Rabboseinu" (our Rabbis), because anyone who observes with sound reason the history of the Jewish people throughout their most diverse and lengthy exile will realize the magnitude of Shabbos observance. My intention is how its observance preserved the existence of the Jewish people in the spiritual sense, and there is room to say in the physical sense as well. One must add another point to this, which is also relevant to these days: that the rest of the day of Shabbos removed many barriers, bringing together and uniting Jews from the most distant circles—both in terms of their livelihood and their level of spirituality—as they met together during davening, which on Shabbos was specifically attended by a large crowd, as well as during the hours of rest throughout the day, and so on.

The relevance to these days is that we have just come from days in which the memory of the Churban is emphasized, and as the statement of Chazal mentioned above states, the observance of Shabbos brings the Geulah closer.

Regarding these days specifically in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, in addition to the above, there is the connection to the cauldron and propaganda of the elections. It is precisely then that existing barriers are raised, and furthermore, new barriers are built; each party with its own style. But apparently, the common denominator among them all is that "party" (*miflagah*) comes from the word for division (*pilug*) and splitting (*pitzul*), and from there it is but one small step to separation and machlokes.

I hope you will forgive me for these words, as their purpose is to express my wishes that, at the very least, these phenomena will be kept to the absolute minimum possible. I will take the liberty of enclosing a passage of my words regarding the above.

With respect and blessing,

[Signature]

## 7725

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 11 Menachem Av.

As we stand on 15 Av, regarding which our Sages, of blessed memory, said that there were no days as festive for the Jewish people as 15 Av, etc., it is a day defined by reasons that are opposites—opposites both in terms of time and in terms of content.

Regarding the time:
- It is the day when the dying in the desert ceased, which corresponds to 15 Av in the lunar month—at which time the moon is in its fullness, as our Sages, of blessed memory, relate regarding this.
- It is the time when the strength of the sun wanes, which is specifically 15 Av in the solar month.

And similarly regarding the content:
- It is the day when they ceased cutting wood for the *ma'arachah* (the altar pyre) because the wood began to become worm-eaten, and the day the slain of Beitar were permitted for burial—matters relating to destruction.
- It is the day when the tribes were permitted to intermarry, etc., and the day of the ascent of all the tribes of Israel for the pilgrimage, etc.—matters relating to building.

And as the conclusion in the *Gemara* states: "From here on, he who adds, will add"—that one adds nights to the days to engage in Torah, and "he will add life to his life."

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon the prophecy will be fulfilled that matters of destruction will be transformed into matters of building, as it is written: **"And I will turn** their mourning into joy."

This will reach the point where the Jewish people will say, "I thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me," where the thanksgiving is also for the fact that **"You were angry,"** for "Your anger will turn away and You will comfort me"—a double comfort: comfort in its own right, and the anger itself which has been transformed into comfort.

This is like the superiority of *ba'alei teshuvah* over *tzaddikim gemurim*, for *ba'alei teshuvah* possess merits in their simple sense, and also their *zedonos* (willful sins) which have been transformed into merits, and their *avodah* is also doubled: if one was accustomed to reading one page, he shall read two pages.

And from the 15th of the month—the fullness of the moon, when the *sihra* (moon) stands in its completeness—may we arrive speedily in our days at the fulfillment of all the matters of the Jewish people, who are destined to be renewed like it, in complete fullness, with our true and complete Redemption.

With blessings for good tidings, in general and in particular,

**M. Schneerson**

And all these things happened regarding the aforementioned, and as mentioned, I ask for your great forgiveness...

## 7727

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Yaakov Yosef, may he live,
Shochet u'Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

...Returned herewith is the responsa regarding the *Shehecheyanu* blessing at a *bris milah*. Time does not permit a proper review; nevertheless, out of regard and respect, I will offer a few brief comments:

Regarding the matter of the *Shehecheyanu* blessing being optional, etc. — see the *psak din* of the Tzemach Tzedek at the end of the *Likutim* and the sources cited there.

Concerning *Shehecheyanu* on Purim during the day — we also find a dispute between the Mechaber and the Rema, but **the opposite** of their opinions regarding *milah* (Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, beginning of 692; Yoreh Deah 265:7) — from which it is proven that they did not address this based on the idea that the *Shehecheyanu* blessing is different from other blessings.

The fact that the Sephardim in London and Amsterdam, etc., recite *Shehecheyanu* at a *milah* proves that the difference in actual practice is not between Eretz Yisrael and the Diaspora, but rather between Sephardim and Ashkenazim.

On the face of it, this is not the way **to determine a practical halachic ruling** on which the Rishonim and Acharonim have disagreed — by bringing proofs from the *Shas*, which both of these great authorities surely did not overlook.

And if you were to say — the fact that the *Shas* nowhere mentions *Shehecheyanu* at a *milah* proves the Ashkenazic custom that one should not recite it.

See regarding this in the sefer *Kesser Shem Tov* (*Taamei Minhagim*) by Rabbi Gagin, Vol. 1, page 563. In addition to the reason not to recite it due to the infant's pain and the concern that he might not survive (mentioned in the enclosed responsa), two other reasons are brought in the sefer *Taamei Minhagim*: because it is incumbent upon the father (the *Baal HaHalachah*), and that it is better from the outset that there be no *orlah* (the Rebbe of Ruzhin). See also *Mitzvas Milah* in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek.

***

**7727**
Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 306.

**R' Yaakov Yosef:** Raskin, Rishon LeZion. Additional letters to him — above, Vol. 14, 5195, and in the notes there.

**The responsa:** By Rabbi Charlap.

## 7768

7768

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Chaim Hillel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 15th of Av, along with the enclosure, in which you inquire regarding the time for the conclusion of Shabbos on Motzaei Shabbos.

This is not the same in all countries or in all months of the year; therefore, one must consult with the halachic authorities in Paris and its surroundings—those who possess knowledge of this great area of Halacha.

To know the exact time of sunrise and sunset in practice, one should consult the calendar published by the French Astronomical Society, as they are experts in this field and are reliable. However, they indicate the actual sunset, which is not always the sunset according to the Shulchan Aruch, and there is no need to elaborate further here.

With blessings for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 7629

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 19 Menachem Av, in which you ask for advice regarding your lack of consistency—that you resolve to conduct yourself in a certain way, but it does not last long, you change your behavior, and consequently, this causes confusion both for others and for yourself.

In general, such changes often occur because one decides on matters that are not commensurate with one's current state—that is, one wishes to leap ahead, whereas the standard order is "little by little I will drive them out" (Shemos 23:30), to ascend in holiness step by step [except in exceptional cases, where the order is to leap and jump, and even to go from one extreme to the other in a single moment, but this is not the order of the daily, consistent service].

Furthermore, the advised counsel for a resolution and decision to be lasting is to connect oneself (farbindt zich) with a friend or chavrusah in this matter. This makes it difficult (macht eing) not to keep the resolution, since by failing to do so, one causes unpleasantness for the other, and the rest is understood.

It is also understood that the yetzer hara strives to cause confusion in this service and conduct as well. But on the contrary, from this very fact one must derive strength in the war against the yetzer. As is known, one should contemplate the immense, strange, and varied efforts the yetzer makes to entice a person. Since this is the purpose of its creation, there must be an effort many times greater on the part of the person to fulfill the purpose of his own creation, as the Sages say, "I was created to serve my Maker." And we have been promised: "If a person sanctifies himself a little from below, they sanctify him greatly from above."

With blessings for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 7730

B"H, 21 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday, in which you write regarding the matter of clothing.

It is surprising that you have any doubt about this, especially since you yourself cite in your letter the statements of Chazal and the halachic rulings that mandate this matter. See also the Responsa of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, Siman 91 (and the omission to the aforementioned at the end of Shaar HaMiluim there), which is based on the verse (Tzephaniah 1:8).

As for your note regarding what is written in Likutei Torah explaining the statement of Chazal that they did not change their clothing—that this refers to the beard and peyos—it is simple that this is in addition to what was stated; this statement does not depart from its literal meaning: actual clothing, external garments.

It is my firm hope that you have fixed times for the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah, and furthermore, that you are increasing this from time to time, as we have been commanded to ascend in matters of holiness.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 7331

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter of 14 Menachem Av, in which you write about your study of Chassidus. I am confident that you are not only continuing in this, but also increasing your efforts from time to time, in accordance with the directive of Chazal to "ascend in matters of holiness." Indeed, the directives of the Sages indicate that it is possible to fulfill them through the performance of the mitzvah.

Regarding your writing about publishing maamarim of Chassidus in Lashon HaKodesh and in a style understandable to the youth you mention:

You should discuss this with Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, as you likely know some of them. This is especially relevant since their activities—lectures given to the aforementioned youth—are surely conducted in the very style you describe.

Regarding what you wrote about the health of your parents, may they live and be well, in connection with their current work at the institution: While you are certainly correct in a general sense that the work is demanding and that there is a need for a vacation from time to time, at the same time, people who have been accustomed for decades to work that provides great spiritual satisfaction will find that a cessation of this work—chas v'shalom—or even, as you put it in your letter, a prolonged vacation, would cause a void in their spiritual lives. Even if such a break were to improve their physical health in and of itself, a person for whom the spiritual component of life occupies the most important place will not forgo it for a gain in the physical realm.

Furthermore, the physical gain itself would likely diminish due to the lack of spiritual satisfaction.

I am confident that your concern for everything regarding your parents, may they live and be well, is expressed first and foremost through your efforts to bring them true nachas ruach, through daily conduct that aligns with the instructions of our Torah—Toras Chaim—and through the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." This is one of the most important factors for strengthening the parents' health in the literal sense as well—the health of the body. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Please convey my regards to your parents, may they live and be well, and with blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7732

7732

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5721

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 13th and 20th of Menachem Av, as well as those preceding them, along with their enclosures. As you requested, I am replying without waiting for my turn.

Regarding the scheduling of the wedding, moving it up in such a case is, of course, appropriate. Whatever you decide, may it be in a good and auspicious hour in all its details.

You wrote regarding the *shoshvinim* (best men/escorts), noting that there is a rationale for choosing a certain person, yet on the other hand, there is a reason to the contrary, and there is a concern that choosing one might cause offense to others.

In such a case, and especially when it involves a matter concerning the honor of a son and daughter of Yisrael, one adds to the number of *shoshvinim*—meaning, three couples walk [the chosson and kallah to the chuppah]. It is revealed before Heaven which two couples are the [primary] *shoshvinim*, and for the aforementioned reason, it is understood that all of this should be done without any emphasis or fanfare.

With blessings for good tidings, both in this and in general matters.

## 7,733

[24 Menachem Av, 5721]

It is surprising that there is no news from you regarding your arrangements for parnassah. After all, this too is a command of our Torah—Toras Chaim—that a person must engage in matters of parnassah through actual, physical action. Furthermore, the Mechilta states that this command is akin to a positive mitzvah. See Kuntres U'Maayon, Chapter 25, regarding how physical action is specifically required in our world, the world of Asiyah. Since the matter is necessary, it is certain that the strengths and possibilities for it have been granted [which further increases the necessity of actual, physical action, so that these possibilities should not remain in vain, chas v’shalom]. I hope that these lines will suffice to arouse you regarding all that has been said, and that you will act upon this with the necessary vigor. I will be brief and await good news in this regard, and may it be His will that it comes soon.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that regarding the above, and in the life of a Yid in general, one must maintain an orderly routine. **This** is specifically the conduct of kedushah [unlike the opposite, where there is no order or accountability, etc.]. I refer to order in all matters: in rising from sleep, in studying Torah—both Nigleh and Chassidus—in eating and drinking, and so on. And in this, it is understood that the primary focus is on matters of the home, for great is the peace between a husband and wife, as then the Shechinah dwells between them.

#### ***7,733***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 26, p. 437.

## 7734

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5721
Brooklyn.

Mr. Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I am enclosing herewith what has been published recently, which I hope will be of interest to you. Even if this is not directly within your field of activity, after all, all matters of the world are interconnected, for unity is drawn down from the highest heights to the lowest depths.

The foundation of our faith—that Hashem is One—is that He is the Creator of the world, so that within it, too, one may draw down this unity. This is as our Alter Rebbe explains regarding the verse, "One nation on earth" (*Goy Echad Ba'aretz*): a nation that draws down unity even into worldly matters.

This is also the inner point that our Torah emphasizes specifically regarding the matter of peace and unity, to the extent that Chazal said, "Great is peace, for the entire Torah was given to create peace in the world."

From time to time, I feel special gratitude to Rabbi A. Ch. Glitzenstein, may he live, for informing me of your state of health, and may it be Hashem's will that you have a complete and speedy recovery.

As is the custom of the Children of Israel to conclude with a topic of the day, as we are approaching Rosh Chodesh Elul, the month of mercy and favor—and especially according to our Alter Rebbe, that Elul is an acronym for *Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li* ("I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"), signifying that the King is in the field (*Likutei Torah, Maamar Ani L'dodi Li*, 2)—

May it be Hashem's will that despite the efforts during these days to divide hearts and distance even those who are close, all the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, will draw closer to one another.

And in the traditional phrasing, may they all become one single bond to serve Him, may He be blessed, with a whole heart.

And as the teachings of Chassidus demand—with joy and a glad heart.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 7335

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Re'eh, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand at the beginning of the month of Elul, the month of mercy and favor, may it be His will that it be in accordance with the opening words of the parsha from which we draw our inspiration: "See, I am setting before you today," where each of the five words represents a complete concept in itself:

**See:** The mode of avodah—at the level of "seeing" (for hearing is not comparable to seeing).

**I:** The strength and assistance for this are granted from "I," *Anochi mi she'Anochi*—the level that is not grasped by any name, nor alluded to by any letter or stroke at all.

**Am setting:** The strength and assistance come through a gift, for one who gives, gives with a generous eye.

**Before you:** That the giving is in a manner that it enters and is absorbed into one's inner being.

**Today:** That every single day, all of the above is renewed.

And all of this applies to both types of avodah:

**A blessing:** In the aspect of "do good," the positive mitzvos.

**And a curse:** In the aspect of "turn from evil," the negative mitzvos.

Through all that has been stated above, we begin the days of favor on Rosh Chodesh Elul, like the first days, and the Ribono shel Olam is reconciled with Yisrael with joy and a whole heart, and we are inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

With blessings for a *ksiva v'chasima tova*,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***7335***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 696. A similar copy was sent to several people.

**The level that is not:** *Likutei Torah*, Pinchas 80b. And see *Zohar Chadash*, Vol. 3, 11a.

**Through a gift:** See *Likutei Torah*, beginning of Parshas Ha'azinu. *Ohr HaTorah*, Bereishis 16b.

**Before you:** See *Eruvin* 54b. *Torah Ohr*, beginning of Parshas Mishpatim.

**Today:** See *Sifrei*, Devarim 6:6.

**Days of favor:** See *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li" (32a).

**And the Ribono shel Olam is reconciled:** Rashi, Shemos 33:11.

## 7336

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Menachem Av, in which you ask whether a yeshiva student in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) is obligated to be drafted into the army there.

It is surprising that you are in doubt about this, to the point that you need to ask from afar. After all, the clear halachic ruling of the Rabbis of Israel is well-known and publicized—and, needless to say, it is grounded in our Torah, the Torah of life—that yeshiva students should not be drafted and should not go out to the army. Their study of our holy Torah with persistence and diligence protects and saves our holy land (may it be rebuilt and established) and those who dwell upon it.

With blessings for a good and sweet year,

## 7741

[2 Elul, 5721]

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 25th of Menachem Av, as well as the three letters that preceded it.

It is a great wonder that you are so agitated by the letter you received, and that you wish to interpret it as though there has been a change in my attitude toward you.

It is simple: I am not responsible for what others write. Indeed, there has **not** been a change in my attitude toward you. Just as it was before, so it is now: my hope is that you are currently (and in the future) occupied with spreading the teachings of Chassidus in your environment, in your city, and wherever your reach extends, and that you will do so with joy and a glad heart, in a manner that is ever-increasing.

Regarding what you wrote about the activities of another person in the city, etc.—there is enough work in spreading the wellsprings and Yiddishkeit for both of you; and it would suffice for many more, if only they were available...

My hope is that since we have entered the month of Elul, you will also strengthen your trust in Hashem Yisbarach, who watches over each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*, for we begin to recite twice daily: "L’Dovid, Hashem is **my light** **and my salvation**," etc.

## 7742

*[3 Elul 5721]*

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul, in which you write regarding your birthday, and also about your place of study—that it is not in... because in your opinion, the educational institution in... is not at the same level.

The surprise and wonder are understandable, especially knowing your home, a Chassidishe home, and your upbringing of this nature. According to this, it should be clear in your mind, and definitively so, that the highest level is precisely this—that the institution was founded by and is under the leadership of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel. The interpretation is certainly not that the knowledge is the main thing, but rather the results—that they should be appropriate for the role of a person in his world, as our Sages of blessed memory said, "I was created to serve my Maker." The fulfillment of this role depends on the measure of yiras shamayim in the education and on the help from Above, with siyata d’shmaya.

And since, as you wrote, you are entering a new year, in which "the majority of years impart wisdom," may it be the will of Hashem that He place you upon the truth, that the "beginning of wisdom is the fear of Hashem"—to be educated within a Chassidishe framework, within the four amos of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. Surely, through this, you will add to the arousal of great mercy regarding your other matters as well.

And may it be His will that in exchange for this—as there were surely those who learned from you regarding their educational institution as mentioned above—from here on in, you will serve as a living example of a Chassidishe girl in your education and your place of residence. I mean this simply: education in the institution of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, as stated above.

With blessings for good tidings soon, and with the blessing of kesivah v’chasimah tovah.
