## 7444

B"H, 5 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul has arrived.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

It is understandable that there is great astonishment upon reading the beginning of your letter regarding sadness and a poor mood. Surely you are aware of what is explained in many holy seforim, and especially in Chassidus, that sadness must be distanced **entirely.** In truth, for a person of understanding, it is **simple:** at the beginning of the day, we recite the *Birchos HaShachar*, and even before that, *Modeh Ani Lefanecha*. Since this implies the literal meaning of the words, it must surely bring about great joy, and not, Heaven forbid, the opposite of *Modeh Ani*. Surely, for you, there is no need to elaborate on this.

This is especially true in your case, as in recent times you have merited to marry off your children, *shichyu*, in a good and auspicious hour, and more and more besides. Hopefully, this will be sufficient to illuminate and clarify the situation **as it truly is.** From now on, you should be in a state of joy and goodness of heart, as we are instructed in our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*.

This is especially relevant as we now find ourselves in the auspicious days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy and favor.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah*.

However, surely when you explain your reasoning to him, he will comply with your request in this regard.

While this is surely known to you, I felt it my duty to note regarding the above that there are various methods for performing the treatment, and there is a practical difference between them according to *Shulchan Aruch*—there is a permitted method, and there is a method that is, etc.

7749

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 13 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter—though it lacked the date of writing—along with the enclosure.

May it be the will of Hashem that you be inscribed and sealed for a good year, together with all of Anash. This is hinted at—as is the manner of avodah in this—at the very beginning of this week’s parsha:

**"When you go out to war" (Ki Seitzei):** The "going out" itself, even before engaging in the war.

**"Against":** In a manner of "above"—transcending your enemies—because one contemplates and knows that "Hashem your G-d walks with you."

**"Your enemies":** Written with a *yud* (plural), indicating many: the enemy in matters of the body and the enemy in matters of the neshamah. They are included in a single word because Yisroel are "one nation in the land," subjugating the body and physicality to the neshamah and spirituality, thereby revealing the one Truth within them.

This "going out," in this manner, acts and draws down that:

**"And He will deliver":** In the singular. He delivers the root from above, which is the yetzer hara (the enemy of the neshamah), which is the Angel of Death (the enemy of the body).

**"Hashem your G-d into your hand":** A complete delivery, to the extent that:

**"And you take captive his captives":** The captives of your enemies. To rescue even that which was already in the captivity of your enemies.

This applies not only to one who has committed a transgression in the literal sense and performs such a great teshuvah that his willful sins become for him like actual merits;

It also applies to elevating matters of "permitted desires" that had temporarily descended into the *sitra achra*. And on an even higher level in the avodah of the *beinoni*—which is the measure for every person, and which every person should strive for—the strength of his soul that is from *kelippas nogah* is transformed into actual good. And an avodah higher than that: to transform the *midos* of the *nefesh habehamis* within the heart (which are a Divine spark) to become entirely good, like the *yetzer hatov* itself.

- And it is possible to say that this also includes the avodah of elevating what one did—through Torah and mitzvos—simply, not *lishmah* and not *shelo lishmah*.

These actions remain in the "externalities of the worlds," and when one returns and performs them *lishmah*, then even the action done "simply" emerges from the externalities of the worlds, connects and joins with the action done *lishmah*, and ascends on high to stand specifically before Hashem.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

***

7749

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 2, p. 697.

**Great teshuvah:** See Tanya, ch. 7.
**Permitted desires:** Tanya, ch. 7.
**Measure for every person:** Tanya, beginning of ch. 14.
**Strength of his soul:** Tanya, ch. 35.
**To transform the midos:** (The level of a *tzaddik*) See Tanya, end of ch. 37, end of ch. 10. Likkutei Torah, *d.h. Ki Seitzei* (the second), ch. 3.
**What one did:** See Tanya, ch. 39-40.
**Externalities of the worlds:** And the return of the sparks must be "before You, so that they may be included and unified, etc., in the Ohr Ein Sof, blessed be He" (Likkutei Torah, beginning of *d.h. Ki Seitzei* (the first)).

*) Some, such as in the sefer *Aderes Eliyahu* (by the author of *Mishnas Chassidim*), forbid it outright. In *Shu"t Chasan Sofer* (sec. 27), he writes, "There are concerns regarding this, as has already been heard from a great scholar who **raised an outcry** about it." Incidentally, this proves that the *Chasam Sofer* **did not** do so, contrary to what P. told him. And in the sefer *Me'asef L'chol Hamachanos*, he gathered a group of *poskim* who hold that not wearing tefillin does not constitute a violation of "You shall not cut yourselves" (*lo titgodedu*). And similarly, the *psak* of the *Tzemach Tzedek* in his *psak* on Orach Chaim, sec. 236.

## 7551

B.H., 15 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, Branch:
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

We are currently in the midst of the month of Elul, when every Jew, man or woman, must perform a *cheshbon hanefesh*. This is an accounting of the year that has passed—for the good—and a preparation of a suitable program for the coming year, which approaches us for good and for blessing, accompanied by a firm resolution to carry it out in practice.

Among Jews, everything is connected to Torah. The Torah, which is *Toras Chaim*—a Torah that teaches how to live, which makes life a true, full life, and instructs how to conduct oneself in every matter and every minute of daily life.

***

It has already been discussed at length that one of the tasks of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad is to encourage and strengthen their husbands, brothers, and children to study Torah.

This is, after all, an obligation and *mitzvah* upon everyone—young or old, rich or poor, and so on.

And this study should take place every day, to the greatest extent possible, and—as with all matters of *Yiddishkeit*—it should be done with *simcha* and vitality.

***

The special connection of women to the fulfillment of this Torah study is because:

a) It often happens that the reason for not studying Torah to the proper extent is the husband’s great preoccupation with matters of *parnassah*, in order to provide the home and family with all necessities—often things that only seem to be necessary, as one convinces oneself.

Therefore, it is especially necessary and important that the woman, the *akeres habayis* (the manager of the home), encourage and **urge** her husband to study Torah daily, and to study as much as possible, even when this involves certain material limitations in the way her home and family are managed. This study is certainly the correct means to bring happiness to the entire family.

b) Even when the encouragement and urging to maintain Torah study **as it should be** is expressed in words only from time to time, the daily sight of one’s husband is in itself a constant reminder of this.

c) By strengthening and urging their husbands to study Torah (and by sending their sons to kosher *chadarim* and *yeshivos*), women have a share in their Torah study—that is, in the **mitzvah** of Torah study itself.

In addition to the study being a means to know how to conduct oneself—as explained in the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe (at the end of the first chapter)—they consequently also enjoy the *schar* (reward) for this *mitzvah*.

And, like the *mitzvah* itself, its *schar* is greater than the *schar* of other *mitzvos*.

***

My request is that during these days, a special movement and increased activity should begin among you to encourage your husbands, brothers, and children to strengthen and increase their daily Torah study—both *nigleh* and *Chassidus*—studying with vitality and *simcha*.

And may the Almighty, the Giver of the Torah, add to and increase His blessings to each person in whatever they need, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*, and grant everyone, within the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*, a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* and a good and sweet year.

With a wish for good tidings from **each** of you regarding the above, and with the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
It would be good if those who will turn with a request to be mentioned—they and their family—at the *tziyun hakadosh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulh"h, nbg"m, zya"e*, during these days of mercy and favor, would also add to their request the *shiurim* of study that are maintained by their husbands, so that this, too, may be mentioned together with the request for a blessing.

***

[Secretariat letter regarding the instruction at the end of the letter]

B.H., 18 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To every one of *Anash*, *shlita*,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

Based on what we have heard from the Rebbe, *shlita*, we come to note and also to request:

That in the *pidyonos nefesh* (panim) being sent—and especially those sent during the days of mercy and favor, and for the days of mercy and favor—which are matters of prayer and petition from below to above, to awaken [the flow] from the source above to below—each person should indicate their *shiurim* in Torah study.

According to what is known, that Torah and its study are the "middle line," through which the elevation from below to above and the drawing down from above to below occur.

This aligns with the simplicity of the matter: that in Torah is the instruction of how man’s *avodah* to his Creator should be, from below to above.

And through this *avodah*—"If you walk in My statutes"—comes "I will give your rains in their time," from above to below.

The *is'arusa d'lesata* (awakening from below) brings about the *is'arusa d'le'eila* (awakening from above). In the language of *nigleh*, this is the measure of the Holy One, blessed be He: "measure for measure." And the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that follows this—

This is not "compelled" (in and of itself), *chas v'shalom*, but it is certainly a matter of necessity, so to speak, that it be so, because it is written in the Torah.

—See *Likutei Torah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (Devarim 84b): "And in a specific way, every day is the matter of *Talmud Torah*..." See there.

With respect and the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

Secretariat

Those who have already sent a *pan*—it is understood and simple that it is proper and good to add the above as soon as possible.

## 7752

B"H, 18 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the organizers of the group traveling here, during the days of mercy and favor, and for the days of mercy and favor, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

Based on the teaching of our Sages that one only encourages the already diligent, I write to note that what was written last year regarding the inspiration for Torah and mitzvos in connection with the trip here, and the arrangements for it, remains in full force this year as well.

On the contrary—in accordance with the directive to ascend in matters of holiness, surely you will increase in this, each person according to their capacity.

And we have been promised: whoever adds, it is added to him.

And in matters of goodness and holiness—where even the physical affairs of the holy Jewish people, the person is commanded to make them holy—no matter how good the situation may be, one must add, going from strength to strength, increasing and illuminating.

It is surely unnecessary to note that the above also includes matters related to influencing others. On the contrary, since "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah, and the teaching of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, is well known: that "Love Hashem your G-d" and "Love your fellow as yourself" are one and the same. And this is understood.

As we stand on the birthday of the two great luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe, may it be the will [of Hashem] that they illuminate our lives, even down to our day-to-day life, regarding our thoughts, speech, and actions below ten tefachim.

And in this, too, it should be in a manner of increasing and illuminating, until the prophecy is fulfilled that "the night shall shine like the day," through man’s avodah to his Creator, and in a manner of "from below to above"—to transform darkness into light and bitterness into sweetness.

The precision here is in the word "transform"—that the darkness and bitterness themselves shall become light and sweetness.

And through this, it will be brought about in the world—that the darkness of the world itself will be transformed into light, that the night itself will shine, in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

Awaiting good news regarding all of the above, and concluding with the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

**M. Schneerson**

## 7,353

B"H, 22 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following a hiatus, your letter of 17 Elul was received, in which you write the main points regarding your current studies and also regarding your state of mind.

Regarding what you wrote as to whether it is possible to be a vessel for Elokus, etc., to fulfill what is written, "Nullify your will before His will," to serve Hashem with joy, etc.

It is a great wonder that you ask about such a simple matter. For all that has been mentioned are the core and foundations of our holy Torah, which is a "Torah of life." Certainly, and most certainly, this is relevant to you, and you are obligated in this; it depends on nothing but your will, as it is written, **"And you shall choose** life."

However, just as all the commandments in the Torah are also stated in the language of a promise for the future, for "one who comes to purify himself is assisted," and we have been promised that "none shall be cast away from Him." Furthermore, even when a person sanctifies himself only a little from below, they sanctify him greatly from above.

These days are especially auspicious for a fundamental shift in all that has been mentioned, for they are days of mercy and favor, as explained at length by our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, that the King (the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He) is in the field and receives everyone with a welcoming countenance, etc. (See Likutei Torah, discourse *Ani L'Dodi*, 32b. See there at length).

With blessings for good tidings and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 7,454

7,454

By the Grace of Hashem, 22 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you outline the history of your life and your current position, which is primarily dedicated to the guidance of youth.

Fortunate is your lot, that you have been given the opportunity to influence and take part in shaping the character of Jewish youth—an influence that may affect the entire duration of their lives, i.e., decades of years, and the building of their homes when they marry, and so on.

My writing regarding the aforementioned "fortunate is your lot" is twofold: If it is a good portion when it is possible to help someone in material or spiritual matters, even in a temporary or fleeting way—then how much more so when the matter concerns assistance that is, as mentioned, both material and spiritual, and for a long duration, perhaps even for the entirety of their lives.

However, in all matters concerning which our Torah—the Torah of life—has said, "I have set before you life and good, death and evil," and the hope, as the conclusion of the matter in the Torah states, "Therefore choose life," we hope that the person to whom this opportunity has been given will choose the path of life and good. That is to say, he will utilize all his ability and influence to guide those he educates toward true life and goodness. And as with any matter of truth, the test of this is that it does not pass and vanish after a few moments, days, or weeks, etc., but continues for a long time, and even into eternity.

But together with this, the *yetzer hara* intervenes, confuses, and entices one to utilize this opportunity at the opposite extreme. It is understood that for each person it speaks "in its own tongue," with arguments and temptations that it hopes will be heeded. But since in the world all matters are in order and by calculation, and not by way of chance, Heaven forbid, every person is given the possibility to choose one of the two paths, and is also given the ability to stand firm against the temptations and incitements of the *yetzer hara*.

When one does so, his merit is very great, and as mentioned above, fortunate is his lot—it is good and beautiful.

The answer to the famous question is well known: Since the *yetzer hara* sometimes disguises itself in a good and beautiful cloak—i.e., it entices with arguments that at first glance have the "appearance" of goodness and justice—what, ultimately, is the test to know whether the argument comes from the side of good or from the side of evil?

Based on what was written above, one of the tests for this—at least regarding a specific detail or individual case—is that when one commits a transgression (due to the intensity of desire and will), after the act, one feels a sense of regret, and as time goes on, this feeling intensifies. Conversely, in doing good, after the act, there is even greater satisfaction.

A test regarding the collective (and this also applies to your case, where the discussion is about guiding a group or a specific circle): One must contemplate the history of our people, the Children of Israel, and see what the conduct was that preserved the existence of our people through various and strange periods of its long history—an existence despite the fact that, as the familiar phrasing goes, in every generation they have risen against us to destroy us, and many and mighty (the nations of the world) have risen against the weak and few.

Even a slight contemplation shows that all those circles that turned and strayed from the accepted path and placed their trust in the culture of the lands surrounding them—even if they "translated it into the language" of our people, or wanted to adapt it to our culture (those who followed Ashur and Bavel in the period of the First Beis Hamikdash, the Hellenists at the beginning of the Second Beis Hamikdash, and in a much later period, those who leaned toward the philosophy dominant in Spain during the Middle Ages, and similarly, the students of Mendelssohn in Germany who leaned toward the French *Haskalah*, the progenitors of the Reform movement)—

After a generation, two, or three, not a remnant or survivor remained of them within our people, the Children of Israel. Some of them returned from their aforementioned opinions, and some were completely assimilated among the nations surrounding them, and as mentioned—without leaving any impression at all on the generation that followed them.

Only the matter of *mitzvos* performed in action—which from the days of the Giving of the Torah at Mount Sinai, when it was said, "You shall not make for yourself a graven image," "Observe the day of Shabbos," "You shall not do any work," etc., and in the same way the *mitzvos* of *tzitzis* and *tefillin*, the prohibition of eating animals that do not have split hooves and do not chew their cud, and the like—these are what we find throughout the entire three thousand years and more of the history of the Children of Israel without any changes. The conclusion is understood.

May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that you utilize the opportunity that has been given to you in the aforementioned direction, and in its fulfillment, until you also influence your colleagues—the guides—that they may see from you and do likewise. And the merit of the many, those who are educated and influenced, will assist you.

These days, the days of the month of Elul, are days of favor in this regard as well—the month of accounting for the past year, and the month of preparation for the coming year.

And especially regarding you, as you prepare, as you wrote, for your wedding in the near future, when one is in need of a special blessing from the Creator of the world and its Guide: your actions for the good, for the benefit of the many, are the very channel and vessel for increasing the blessing of Hashem Yisbarach in what is needed for you and your bride, *tichyeh*. May it be His will that you bring good tidings in all the aforementioned, and from time to time—in a manner of "increasing and continuing."

It is understood that it is within your permission and also your merit to share all that is written here with all your fellow guides.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and with the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

## 7755

23 Elul, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the *avreich*, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished *tamim*, Rabbi Aharon, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter, along with the proofs of the *Perush u’Piskei Ri’d* on *Maseches Shabbos*, which you have merited to edit and prepare for publication.

Happy is his portion to be occupied with the Torah of the *Rishonim*—the *Rishonim* who are like angels, the masters of the *Tosafos* by whose words we live.

Often, in their pure and concise style, they illuminate the way through the sea of the *Talmud* in such a way that, from the outset, there is no room for difficulties, refutations, and the like.

As is known, the *Rebbe* (my father-in-law) would cite a saying in this regard, in the name of his ancestors, our *Nesi’im*, regarding the difference in the style of the *Rishonim*: in a few lines, they clarify a difficult matter, issue a ruling for practical *halacha*, and the matter is illuminated. This is in contrast to the style of the *Acharonim*, who extend themselves in *pilpula d’Oraisa*, in debate and negotiation in the "war of Torah," until they arrive at a conclusion and a *psak din*. And even then, it does not possess the same simplicity and light as in the works of the *Rishonim*.

They gave an example of this: A person is in a large hall, and the entire hall is filled with light. He immediately finds what he needs—whether it is a door, a window, or the like. This is unlike the later generations, where the darkness has intensified to the point of "darkness that can be felt," and hearts have diminished, etc. The person in the hall who wants to find an exit must grope until he finds a space; he begins to search for proofs—is this the door that leads outside, or is it merely an open window, or perhaps a sealed window? He looks for proofs from the side and all around. Hearing, understanding, and grasping are not the same as *seeing*. Even in intellectual matters, there are these levels: a conclusion reached through debate and the negation of contradictory matters, or "seeing" with the eye of the intellect, where one sees the matter clearly, to the point that all difficulties and refutations cannot contradict the conclusion, nor even weaken it.

As is known, the example of this is the matter of "Rav remained silent." Even though they posed difficulties to his *psak din*, he did not retract it, because he knew clearly in his intellect that this was the *psak*, despite the difficulty and the refutation.

May it be His will that you increase your efforts in the study of Torah—both the revealed and the inner dimensions together, for it is one Torah. May your study lead to action—as our Sages taught—which includes the publication of such books, and may you aim for the truth in interpreting the matters and concepts. This is achieved through study conducted with *yiras Hashem* and *bitul* to Him, may He be blessed, for that is the path to aiming for the truth. As our Sages taught regarding the verse "and Hashem was with him" (*Sanhedrin 93b*): it is possible to know how to debate in the "war of Torah," to understand one thing from another, and to present arguments in *halacha*, but to aim for the truth—that the *halacha* is according to him—is only when "Hashem is with him," for He dwells only with the crushed and lowly of spirit (*see the Maamar "Vayedaber... Anochi" 5627, and those that follow*).

With blessings for success in all the above, and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

**Menachem Schneerson**

P.S.
For the sake of affection for the matter, I have added a few notes, even though the time—the days of the month of Elul, the days of mercy and favor, and all the more so during the days of *Selichos*—is set aside for engaging in *tefillah* and supplication, and for joining with the community that pours out their hearts like water before our Father in Heaven, the King who desires life.

**General Note** – In many places in this book, you transcribe the language of the *Shas* exactly as it is without any addition or explanation, even when it is not a *psak din* and does not pertain to *halacha*. For example, "Rabbi Elazar said... like a reed, his head" (*p. 70, 159*).

Perhaps the author had variant readings in these places, and by transcribing them, he intended to establish the correct version.

- There is almost no commentary in the entire book on the *Aggadah* portions of the *Maseches*.

**Page 1.** "The departures of Shabbos are two that are four outside... and inside." In the note, you mention that this is the version of the Cambridge Mishnayos 5702 (**outside** and then **inside**).

Now, as I have written regarding the variant readings in the Romm edition Mishnayos, we have not found a peer for this version.

It is incomprehensible how there is no trace of the version the *Ri’d* chose.

However, upon careful examination, one must conclude that the author—the *Ri’d*—also read **inside** and then **outside**, as he writes **immediately** in his commentary: "Meaning, the departures of Shabbos are two by Torah law inside... and two... by Torah law outside..."

And even if you were to say that commentators generally follow the rule of "opening with that which one concludes," here it is impossible, because the commentary begins with the words "The departures of Shabbos" which are at the **beginning** of our *Mishnah*.

Also, further on, it is implied that the author's version is inside **and then** outside, as he writes (*bottom of p. 2*): "This is the explanation of the two entries inside... and the two departures outside..." And on the bottom of p. 3: "Behold, he explained... now there are two entries inside... and two departures outside..."

To resolve the contradiction between the transcription of the *Mishnah* and the commentary, one could say:

Many *Rishonim*, in their commentary on the *Shas*, do not transcribe the *Shas* at the beginning of their *dibbur hamaschil*, but only a few words, or they wrote the commentary on the margins of the *Shas*, and the *Ri’d* did the same here. The transcriber, who was not precise (as he did not notice the aforementioned contradiction), was also not precise in transcribing the language of the *Mishnah*, or perhaps he happened to have the Cambridge Mishnayos. But a great man like the *Ri’d* is not signed on this version, and therefore we have not found a peer for it, as mentioned above, even though many have drunk from the waters of the *Ri’d*.

**Ibid.** "Inside, meaning... entries." – Here is a place to note that this is like the commentary of *Rashi* in *Shevuos (5a)*, and not like *Rashi* and *Tosafos*, etc., here.

**Ibid.** "That they are four" – This is not the beginning of a new paragraph, but a continuation of the first paragraph. Its conclusion is "and regarding the poor man"—because he is explaining the *bava* he began to interpret. After this, "and he challenges in the *Gemara*" begins a new subject.

**At the end of the book.** Page 489, "What is *amor*?" – It should be (?) "Who is *amor*?"

**Ibid.** "I am *misasek* (engaged) for play and I do not need to know the measure of the water." The word the *Ri’d* added, **"for play"** (and one must search if this addition—or something similar—is found in the commentators) – seemingly, it can be explained as coming from the language of "they play with a ball on Shabbos." Meaning, even though one should have an accurate measurement, it is called merely *misasek* and is permitted, since he is measuring only for the sake of play and does not need to know the measure of the water. This is like the opinion of the *Avi HaEzri* (*Tur Orach Chaim, end of 306*), that it is permitted to measure three *amos* three times and to whisper, etc., and the reason is that it is *misasek*.

But it could also be explained that "for play" is from the language of "jest and lightheadedness," as in "I am playing" (*Proverbs 26:19*), meaning there is no intention for measurement at all, but merely *misasek*. See the commentary of *Rabbeinu Chananel*: "And *misasek* merely means I am measuring and I do not intend for measurement." And like the language of our *Rabbi* in his *Shulchan Aruch (306:18-19)*: "He measures not for any need **at all**," and then it is specifically permitted. Regarding the aforementioned whispering—it is considered measurement (but it is permitted because it is a measurement for a *mitzvah*). This requires further study.

Since I have arrived at this, it requires study why the law that *misasek* is permitted in measurement was not brought in the *Rambam*, *Shulchan Aruch*, *Rema*, etc.

**Ibid.** "A barrel is lifted" (*nital*) – It seems it should be: "He lifts a barrel" (*notel*).

**Ibid.** In the note: "Blessed is the Merciful One who..." – It seems the elaboration is: "Blessed is the Merciful One who helped [us]."

## 7756

B.H., Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Atem Nitzavim, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and abundant blessing,

We find ourselves in the days of preparation for the new year that is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing.

If in every matter our Torah is *Toras Chaim*—the teacher and guide for a Jew—then this is certainly true, and of special importance, when it comes to preparing for a new year; a year that we pray and hope will begin a new, much better life—better in all respects.

***

The Torah portion for these days—*Atem Nitzavim*—which "is always read before Rosh Hashanah, and this is also indicated by the word *Hayom* (today), which refers to Rosh Hashanah"—gives us the instruction for the aforementioned at the very beginning of the *sedra*:

**"You are standing today, all of you, before Hashem your G-d"** (*Devarim* 29:9).

**"You are standing"** (*Atem Nitzavim*)—Jews must stand firm and unyielding, regardless of the fact that they are the fewest of all peoples.

And this can be achieved when they are connected and united together—**"all of you"** (*kulamchem*).

But how is it possible to create a true and lasting union between different people, with distinct thoughts, interests, and aspirations?

The answer is—**"before Hashem your G-d."** The union of all Jews is possible because, in truth, they are already connected through their *neshamah*, the *nefesh ha-elokis*, which is a literal "part of G-d from above," found in every Jew without exception. And the deep contemplation that one is standing **"before Hashem"**—who is **"your G-d,"** your source of strength and life—brings out and actualizes the connection of one Jew to another, and of the individual to the collective, to the fullest extent.

What is the goal and purpose of this union? The Torah explains immediately: **"To enter into the covenant of Hashem your G-d... which Hashem your G-d is making with you today"**—so that you may enter into a covenant with the *Ribono shel Olam*, accepting His oath—a covenant that the *Ribono shel Olam* makes with you **"today,"** anew. A covenant made **"in order to establish you today as His people"**—that you should be established as the people of the *Ribono shel Olam*—

A people who conduct themselves, even in their daily life, according to the Torah of the *Ribono shel Olam* and fulfill all His instructions.

May it be His will that the aforementioned be carried out by each and every one in a good way and to the fullest extent, and that the new, approaching year be a *shanah tovah u’mesukah* (a good and sweet year) in both material and spiritual matters.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in revealed and manifest goodness.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 7,557

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Atem Nitzavim Hayom Kulchem, 5721
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the residents of Shikun Chabad in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established, via the members of the committee, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the telegram regarding the residents moving into Shikun Chabad, and that you are beginning to daven, learn, and farbreng in the location this Shabbos, Nitzavim.

May it be Hashem’s will that the move be at a propitious and successful time, and may the neighborhood be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed. Consequently, blessing will be abundant and joy will be multiplied in the homes of all the residents and their families, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Since the move is taking place during these auspicious days, and the dedication of the home through Torah and Chassidus is occurring on the Shabbos before Rosh Hashanah—when we always read Parshas Nitzavim (and see Likutei Torah by the Alter Rebbe, beginning of Parshas Nitzavim)—and as is well known, the allusion to this in the word **"Hayom"** (Zohar III, 231a), may it be the will from Above that the verse be fulfilled in you: "You are standing today, all of you, before Hashem your G-d," with all the interpretations and allusions contained therein, the essence of which is unity, inwardness, and a heartfelt desire in actual practice, as part of the preparation for the new year that is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, and for continued influence throughout all the days of the year.

With respect and with a blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

#### ***7,557***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 528.

## 7758

You write regarding the unfortunate events that occurred in the past, and conclude with the question of how to deal with those who can still be brought back to the right path, and how to prevent such evil in the future.

First and foremost, in the style of our Sages, "What shall a son do and not sin?" Since the learning environment is one of mixture (even when the subject matter is secular or holy studies), the mixture continues thereafter. Even during the time of study, it is "like fire in tow," as per the ruling of our Sages, who were well-acquainted with human nature. When one wishes to negate the possibilities of an **effect**, one must nullify the cause and the source. Remedies intended to heal and change the effect only work for the moment, and even then, their efficacy is in doubt.

Since even a temporary remedy is still a matter of importance (especially if the moment is utilized as required), and although every individual has their own unique traits, the common denominator among them all is that there is no propaganda more effective than being a living example—the very person who is lecturing them on morality and wishes to bring them back to the right path.

And another point common to all: the fulfillment of mitzvos as much as possible. For if a little light pushes away much darkness, then certainly a great deal of light does so all the more.

Another point: the success of such efforts is tied to them being conducted in ways of pleasantness, but at the same time, they must be carried out with the appropriate firmness. This is especially true regarding the phenomenon you write about, which, if not abolished, is a source for all corruption and evil, *rachmana litzlan*.

Along with what has been said, every single Jew is a child of Hashem, our Elokim. Therefore, each one is commanded to do everything within their power to set them on the good and straight path, to live their daily lives according to the instruction of our Torah—the Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them." We have been promised that words coming from the heart enter the heart of the listener and accomplish their effect.

#### ***7758***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 22, p. 405.
